Removed the explicit announce from the DELETE route to avoid double-posting; the announcement now carries the real exit code instead of always reporting `null`. Added `reconcileTerminalSessionsForChat(chatId)` which sweeps DB rows where `exitedAt == null` whose IDs aren't in `ptyManager` (orphans from a previous server lifetime), marks them exited, and posts a close announcement noting that the session likely ended at the last restart. Hooked into the chat GET handler so reconciliation runs before messages are fetched. TerminalEmbed dispatches a `quilltap:terminal-exited` window event on WS exit; the salon page listens and calls `fetchChat()` so the close announcement appears inline without a manual refresh.

#### Fix: terminal_list tool returned empty results for chats with live sessions

`TerminalSessionSchema` declared `label`, `exitedAt`, `exitCode`, and `transcriptPath` with bare `.nullable()`, but the SQLite hydration layer converts NULL → `undefined` to play nice with `.optional()` schemas. Every read silently failed Zod validation and the row was dropped, so `findByChatId` returned `[]` even when sessions existed. Switched the four fields to `.nullable().optional()` (matches the rest of the codebase) and updated the call sites that compared with `=== null` to use `==`/`!=` so the live/exited check still works.

#### Fix: custom dev server (server.ts) now serves Next dev features properly

The custom server's upgrade handler was calling `socket.destroy()` for any upgrade path that wasn't a terminal stream, which killed Next's HMR / dev RSC / devtools WebSocket connections (Next attaches its own listener to the same `http.Server`). Pages would render once and then sit on a dead HMR socket — no compile feedback, no fast refresh. Fixed by `return`ing instead of destroying for non-terminal paths so Next's listener gets the event. Also passed `httpServer: server` to `next({...})` so Next can attach its upgrade listener at prepare time rather than lazily on the first request. Verified `/_next/webpack-hmr` returns 101 + `turbopack-connected` + `sync` frames after the fix. Swapped scripts: `dev` is now `tsx server.ts` (the custom server, default for development); `dev:next` is the bare `next dev --turbopack` for cases where the custom server gets in the way.

#### Fix: node-pty spawn-helper exec bit on macOS

`node-pty`'s prebuild for `darwin-arm64` / `darwin-x64` ships `spawn-helper` without the executable bit on some installs, which makes `pty.spawn()` fail with `posix_spawnp failed`. Added `scripts/fix-node-pty-permissions.js` and wired it as a `postinstall` hook so a fresh `npm install` chmods the helper to 0755. No-op on Linux (where the prebuild already has the bit) and Windows (where there's no spawn-helper).

#### Added in-chat terminal sessions (Ariel)

Open a real PTY shell inside a Salon chat via xterm.js + node-pty over a custom WebSocket server. Sessions are scoped to the chat and end when the chat is deleted. LLM access is read-only via new `terminal_read` and `terminal_list` tools; only the user can type into the terminal. New `ariel` systemSender announces session open/close.

#### Added Manifesto character field

Added a Manifesto field to characters: a Markdown property holding the character's basic tenets and most important facts of existence — the axiomatic core that every other field should remain consistent with. Syncs to the character vault as `manifest.md` and feeds into the per-chat system prompt (above Personality), the AI Wizard, Summon From Lore, and the Memory Optimizer.

#### Embedding profiles gain Matryoshka truncation + L2-normalize controls

Embedding profiles can now slice the provider's raw vector to a configured length before storage. For Matryoshka-trained models like Qwen3-Embedding the first N components are themselves a valid embedding at dimension N, so truncating 4096d to 1024d cuts storage and cosine-search work to a quarter with negligible quality loss — and no provider call required.

- **Schema.** `EmbeddingProfileSchema` (`lib/schemas/profile.types.ts`) gains `truncateToDimensions: number | null` (post-process slice target) and `normalizeL2: boolean` (default true; formalizes the previously hardcoded behavior). New SQLite migration `add-embedding-profile-truncation-fields-v1` adds the matching `embedding_profiles` columns. Seed default profile in `first-startup/index.ts` initializes both fields. The repository round-trips both new fields automatically via the Zod base.
- **Pipeline.** New exported `applyEmbeddingProfile(rawVector, profile)` helper in `lib/embedding/embedding-service.ts` slices to `truncateToDimensions` (when set and the raw vector is longer) and L2-normalizes (unless `normalizeL2 === false`). Both `generateApiEmbedding` and `generateBuiltinEmbedding` route their results through it. Returned `dimensions` reflects the post-truncation length.
- **API.** `POST /api/v1/embedding-profiles` and `PUT /api/v1/embedding-profiles/[id]` accept the two new fields with shape validation. Truncation/normalize changes do **not** trigger the existing auto-reindex flow on save — that path is reserved for provider/model swaps; truncation has its own re-apply trigger.
- **UI.** `ProfileForm` and `ProfileModal` (`components/settings/embedding-profiles/`) gain a "Truncate output to (Matryoshka)" number input and a "Normalise to unit length" checkbox, hidden for BUILTIN. The profile list shows the configured truncation as metadata and exposes a two-click "Re-apply (Matryoshka)" action button on the default profile when truncation is set.
- **Sanity guard.** New `EmbeddingDimensionMismatchError` class and `assertEmbeddingDimensionsMatch()` helper in `lib/embedding/embedding-service.ts`. `cosineSimilarity` now throws the typed error with both lengths, so all five existing callers (`vector-store.ts`, `help-search.ts`, `memory-service.ts`, `conversation-search.ts`, `memory-dedup.ts`) get a useful diagnostic for free. Document chunk search (`lib/mount-index/document-search.ts`) does a single pre-flight check at search entry so a stale corpus surfaces a clean error instead of failing on the first chunk.
- **Re-apply runner.** New service module `lib/embedding/reapply-profile.ts` with `reapplyEmbeddingProfile(profile)`. Walks every embedding-bearing table — `memories`, `vector_entries`, `conversation_chunks`, `help_docs` (main DB), and `doc_mount_chunks` (mount-index DB) — slicing+renormalizing any row longer than the target. Pre-flight `VACUUM INTO` backups produce `<dbname>.bak-pre-truncation-<date>.db` for both DBs before any write. Per-table transactional rewrite, then VACUUM. Refuses to operate when stored vectors are *shorter* than the target (would need re-embedding). Cleans up the in-memory mount-chunk cache and unloads all character vector stores after rewrite.
- **Job + trigger.** New `EMBEDDING_REAPPLY_PROFILE` job type with handler at `lib/background-jobs/handlers/embedding-reapply-profile.ts`, enqueued via `enqueueEmbeddingReapplyProfile` and exposed as `POST /api/v1/embedding-profiles/[id]?action=reapply`. Endpoint refuses if `truncateToDimensions` is unset.
- **Help docs.** `help/embedding-profiles.md` gains a "Matryoshka Truncation & Unit Normalisation" section explaining when to enable, how truncation interacts with the existing `dimensions` field, the re-apply flow with backup behavior, and a troubleshooting entry for the new dimension-mismatch error.

#### Memory extraction runs per turn instead of per assistant message

The memory extraction pipeline previously fired once per assistant response. In multi-character turns where N characters spoke, that meant N separate jobs, each running its own user-pass against the same user message paired with a different assistant slice. Each pass also only saw a single 2-message window, so attribution had to be inferred without the surrounding turn context. This is now refactored to run extraction once per *turn* (one user input + every character contribution that followed), with the joined transcript fed to all three extraction passes.

- **New transcript builder.** `lib/services/chat-message/turn-transcript.ts` walks chat history forward from a turn opener (the most recent non-system USER message) and groups every ASSISTANT contribution by participant into ordered character slices. System whispers (Host, Librarian, Concierge), tool messages, and silent-mode messages are filtered out. Greeting-only history (no user opener) yields a transcript with `userMessage: null` so downstream extraction skips the user pass.
- **Transcript-shaped extraction prompts.** `extractUserMemoriesFromTurn`, `extractSelfMemoriesFromTurn`, and `extractInterCharacterMemoriesFromTurn` (`lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks/memory-tasks.ts`) replace the prior `extractMemoryFromMessage` / `extractCharacterMemoryFromMessage` / `extractInterCharacterMemoryFromMessage` trio. They share a single `renderTurnContext` helper so every pass sees a byte-identical PARTICIPANTS roster + TURN TRANSCRIPT prefix — when the cheap-LLM provider supports prefix caching, all N self-passes within a turn hit the same cacheable prefix.
- **Per-turn memory processor.** `processTurnForMemory(ctx)` in `lib/memory/memory-processor.ts` replaces `processMessageForMemory` and `processInterCharacterMemory`. It runs ONE user-pass against the joined transcript (with the resulting candidates written to every character that participated), N self-passes (one per character), and N×(N-1) inter-character pair passes — all against the same transcript. Rate limiting still gates per character, and the gate / dedup / SKIP_NEAR_DUPLICATE / SKIP_EMBEDDING_FAILED machinery is unchanged downstream.
- **Per-turn job payload.** `MemoryExtractionPayload` (`lib/background-jobs/queue-service.ts`) is now `{ chatId, turnOpenerMessageId, connectionProfileId }`. The handler (`lib/background-jobs/handlers/memory-extraction.ts`) reads the chat at execution time and rebuilds the transcript from current state, so the job carries no message contents. Dedup at enqueue time keys on `(chatId, turnOpenerMessageId)`: if a job is already PENDING or PROCESSING for that turn, additional finalize calls within the same turn return the existing job ID rather than enqueueing duplicates.
- **Inter-character job type retired.** `INTER_CHARACTER_MEMORY` enqueueing is removed (`enqueueInterCharacterMemory` deleted, `triggerInterCharacterMemory` removed); inter-character extraction is folded into the per-turn job. The job type and handler stay registered as a no-op stub (`handleInterCharacterMemory`) so any rows enqueued before the change drain to COMPLETED instead of failing repeatedly.
- **Finalizer fires only on turn close.** `lib/services/chat-message/message-finalizer.service.ts` now calls `triggerTurnMemoryExtraction` only when `turnInfo.isUsersTurn === true` (control returns to the user — i.e., this was the last assistant in the turn). Earlier characters' finalize calls in a multi-character turn skip the trigger; the last speaker's call enqueues a single job covering the whole turn. Mid-turn tool / continuation cycles don't toggle `isUsersTurn` either, so they don't produce spurious extractions.
- **Help-chat orchestrator** (`lib/services/help-chat/orchestrator.service.ts`) updated to call `triggerTurnMemoryExtraction` directly. The help-chat path was already effectively per-turn (single response cycle), so the migration is a 1:1 swap.
- **Batch enqueue API.** `enqueueMemoryExtractionBatch` now takes `Array<string | null>` of turn-opener IDs instead of `MessagePair[]`. Both production callers (`app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/memories.ts` for the "queue memories for this entire chat" action, and `lib/import/sillytavern-import-service.ts` for SillyTavern imports) walk chat history, collect every non-system USER message ID, and enqueue one per-turn job each. The `messagePairs` payload field on the v1 schema is retained for compatibility but ignored.
- **Candidate cap lowered from 5 to 3.** `HARD_CANDIDATE_CAP` in `lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks/memory-tasks.ts` reduced from 5 to 3, bounding both the prompt instruction (`Return at most ${maxMemories} memories`) and the post-parse `.slice(0, HARD_CANDIDATE_CAP)`. With cheap-LLM `maxTokens` ≥ 24001 the previous ceiling produced up to 5 candidates per call. The cap-of-3 holds candidates per call to a more reasonable ceiling, which together with the per-turn deduplication reduces aggregate memory churn (and the downstream EMBEDDING_GENERATE fan-out) per turn.
- **Test coverage.** New `__tests__/unit/lib/services/chat-message/turn-transcript.test.ts` covers the transcript builder edge cases (turn opener resolution, system-sender filtering, multi-character grouping, greeting-only history). `__tests__/unit/background-jobs/memory-extraction-handler.test.ts` rewritten for the per-turn payload. `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/memory-processor-regression.test.ts` rewritten to exercise the new processor across user/self/inter-character passes, rate-limit modes, and gate skip outcomes. Finalizer test asserts `triggerTurnMemoryExtraction` is silent mid-turn and fires only when control returns to the user. The `INTER_CHARACTER_MEMORY` handler test pinned to the legacy-drain stub.

#### Fix: rolling summary no longer rehashes the persona system block

`buildCompressedSystemMessage` in `lib/chat/context/compression.ts` was concatenating the rolling compressed-history summary onto the end of the full system prompt and returning a single string, which `assembleContext` in `lib/chat/context-manager.ts` then pushed as system block 1. Every async compression cycle (every 5–7 messages once compression warms up) produced a new summary text, which rehashed block 1 and invalidated the cacheable persona prefix on every provider — observed in the LLM logs as Friday's `systemBlock1Hash` flipping every turn (`ab5488e8` → `ce3ec8bf` → `387c3ada` → …) while Amy's stayed at a stable `550842358846b47a` because compression had not yet fired for her. Z.AI returned `cached_tokens: 0` on every Friday turn as a result. Fixed by replacing the function with `buildCompressedHistoryBlock`, which returns only the wrapped history (or null when no history). `assembleContext` now emits the compressed history as a separate system block 3 after the persona prompt and identity reinforcement, so blocks 1 and 2 stay byte-stable while the rolling summary churns in its own block. Test suite at `__tests__/unit/lib/chat/context/compression.test.ts` updated to match the new contract.

#### Fix: Z.AI plugin now reports prompt-cache hits

The Z.AI plugin (`@quilltap/qtap-plugin-z-ai` v1.1.3) was reading `usage.prompt_tokens / completion_tokens / total_tokens` from Z.AI's OpenAI-compat response and never extracting `usage.prompt_tokens_details.cached_tokens`. As a result every `chat_messages` row from Z.AI logged `cacheUsage: null`, making it impossible to tell whether GLM Context Caching was hitting. Fixed by extracting `cached_tokens` and emitting `cacheUsage: { cacheReadInputTokens, cachedTokens }` on both the sync and streaming response paths, matching the OpenAI plugin's contract. Plugin lives at `~/source/qtap-plugin-z-ai`; bumped to `1.1.3` and republished.

#### Fix: Host re-announcing the same off-scene characters every turn

`assembleContext` in `lib/chat/context-manager.ts` was passing `existingMessages` (the trimmed `{ role, content, id?, thoughtSignature? }` view used for LLM context) into `findIntroducedOffSceneCharacterIds`. That view is stripped of `systemSender`, `systemKind`, and `hostEvent`, so the dedupe filter never matched a prior Host announcement and every turn re-announced every mentioned off-scene character. Fixed by re-loading the full chat history via `repos.chats.getMessages(chat.id)` for the dedupe check; the LLM-context path is unchanged.

#### Cheap-LLM token floor raised to 2048; compression tasks bumped to 4000

`executeCheapLLMTask` in `lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks/core-execution.ts` now floors `effectiveMaxTokens` at 2048 (`Math.max(maxTokens ?? 2048, 2048)`) instead of defaulting to 1000. Callers that don't pass an explicit `maxTokens` move from 1000 to 2048; callers that pass a value below 2048 are bumped up. The three compression tasks in `lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks/compression-tasks.ts` (`compressConversationHistory`, `compressSystemPrompt`, `compressMemories`) now pass `maxTokens: 4000` explicitly so longer summaries are not truncated mid-output, matching the budget already used by `craftImagePrompt`, `craftStoryBackgroundPrompt`, and `updateSceneState`.

#### Image prompt crafting raised to 4000-token output

`craftImagePrompt` and `craftStoryBackgroundPrompt` (`lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks/image-scene-tasks.ts`) were using the default 1000-token cap from `executeCheapLLMTask`, which truncated longer multi-character prompts mid-paragraph. Both bumped to 4000 tokens to match the budget already used by `updateSceneState`.

#### Rolling-window summary replaces full-history payload

Replaces the gate-with-full-history approach from Phases 1-4 with a true rolling-window cadence: the chat-message LLM call now sees `[Librarian summary whisper] + [last 5–10 turns]` instead of the entire conversation. Older USER + character messages are dropped from the LLM context once a fold has covered them. The Phase 4 broadcast Librarian summary, edit-aware invalidation, and `compactionGeneration` plumbing all carry over unchanged.

- **Fold cadence, not token thresholds.** New constants `FOLD_TURN_BATCH = 5`, `FOLD_TAIL_FLOOR = 5`, `FOLD_TRIGGER_DELTA = 10`, `T_HARD_TURN_THRESHOLD = 50` in `lib/chat/context-summary.ts`. `evaluateSummarizationGate` now returns `'skip' | 'fold' | 'hard'`; signature is `{ currentTurn, lastFoldedTurn, lastFullRebuildTurn }`. Below 10 turns no fold fires (LLM sees full conversation). At turn 11 the first fold absorbs turns 1–5; at turn 16 the next fold absorbs turns 6–10; etc. T_hard is a periodic full from-scratch rebuild that absorbs everything except the last 5 turns in one call.
- **Update-style fold prompt.** New `foldChatSummary` task in `lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks/chat-tasks.ts` (exported from `lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks/index.ts`). Prompt frames the call as an *update* with four labeled sections — Active threads, Resolved decisions, Emotional state, Open questions — and explicit carry-forward / drop / add verbs per section. The carry-forward framing reduces drift across many folds. Replaces the previous `summarizeChat` / `updateContextSummary` calls in `generateContextSummary`.
- **Turn partitioning + staff filter.** New exported `partitionMessagesIntoTurns` in `lib/chat/context-summary.ts` walks chat history chronologically, treating each non-staff USER message as a turn boundary. ASSISTANT replies attach to the current turn. Messages with `systemSender` set (Host, Librarian, Concierge, etc.) are excluded from summary input but do not affect turn numbering. Leading greeting messages (ASSISTANT before any USER) attach to turn 1.
- **Older messages dropped from LLM context.** `lib/chat/context-manager.ts:buildContext` now filters `messagesToProcess` by `chat.summaryAnchorMessageIds` — anything covered by the running summary is dropped before the recency budget runs. The most recent broadcast Librarian summary whisper survives (its own ID is not in the anchor set), so the surviving tail begins with that whisper followed by post-fold turns. This is the actual-compaction step the prior phases lacked. `MultiCharacterMessage` (`lib/llm/message-formatter.ts`) and `attributeMessagesForCharacter` (`lib/chat/context/message-attribution.ts`) now preserve the source `id` so multi-character mode can filter the same way.
- **Cache breakpoint on the running summary.** New optional `cacheControl?: { type: 'ephemeral' }` field on `ContextMessage` (`lib/chat/context-manager.ts`) and `StreamOptions.messages` (`lib/services/chat-message/streaming.service.ts`). Context-manager sets it on the first surviving Librarian summary whisper (detected via `SUMMARY_CONTENT_PREFIX`). Anthropic plugin (`plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-anthropic/provider.ts`) now honors caller-supplied `cacheControl` in addition to the existing `system_and_long_context` last-user breakpoint. Result: when the summary changes (every 5 turns), only the summary-and-after re-prefills; system+tools (~50K cached tokens) stay hot. Plugin bumped to 1.0.31.
- **Reused chat fields, no DDL change.** `chat.lastSummaryTurn` is repurposed as the fold anchor (renamed semantically to "lastFoldedTurn" in code; column kept). `chat.lastFullRebuildTurn` continues to anchor T_hard. `chat.compactionGeneration` bumps on every fold (Phase 3 frozen-memory archive recomputes every 5 turns; the prefill savings dwarf the archive recompute cost). No migration needed.
- **Test coverage.** `__tests__/unit/lib/chat/summarization-gate.test.ts` rewritten for the fold cadence — covers skip/fold/hard transitions, the 11/16/21/26 cadence over a 30-turn chat, and T_hard preference over fold at 50 turns. New `__tests__/unit/lib/chat/summary-fold.test.ts` exercises `partitionMessagesIntoTurns` for the staff-message filter, multi-character round packing, leading greetings, and non-message events. New `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/fold-chat-summary.test.ts` snapshots the four-section prompt and verifies the placeholder fires on the first fold.

#### LLM cost reduction Phase 4: single broadcast summary + edit-aware invalidation

Phase 4 of the cost-reduction plan, scoped down per direction: drop the per-character summary fan-out entirely; one broadcast Librarian summary is visible to every present character. Witness-set / per-character filtering / structured JSON facts (the original Phase 4) are dropped along with their motivation. Edit-aware invalidation lands as a small hook.

- **Single broadcast summary whisper.** `generatePerCharacterSummaryWhispers` and the per-participant visible-message-slice helpers (`buildVisibleMessagesForParticipant`, `visibleConversation`, `GeneratePerCharacterSummariesParams`) are removed from `lib/chat/context-summary.ts`. `generateContextSummary` now sweeps prior librarian summary whispers anchored to older generations and posts ONE Librarian whisper with `targetParticipantIds: null`. Every present character sees the same text. The `lib/services/dangerous-content/resolver.service` import remains — uncensored fallback still applies to the broadcast summary on dangerous chats.
- **Catch-up summary path removed.** `generateCatchUpSummaryForParticipant` and `triggerCatchUpSummaryAsync` are gone. With broadcast summaries already in chat history, newly-joined participants with `hasHistoryAccess === true` see the existing whisper. If no summary exists yet, the next gate fire produces one for everyone. Removed both call sites: `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts` (PUT update path) and `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/participants.ts` (POST add path).
- **`summaryAnchorMessageIds` on chat metadata.** New `summaryAnchorMessageIds: UUID[]` field on `ChatMetadataSchema` and `ChatMetadataBaseSchema` (`lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`) tracks the conversation message IDs (USER + ASSISTANT) that fed the current `contextSummary`. Migration `add-summary-anchor-message-ids-field-v1` ALTERs `chats`; fresh-install DDL in `sqlite-initial-schema.ts` carries the column natively. DDL.md updated. `generateContextSummary` writes the array alongside the summary text on every fire.
- **Edit-aware summary invalidation hook.** New `invalidateContextSummaryIfMessageCovered(chatId, messageIds)` in `lib/chat/context-summary.ts`. When called with one or more changed message IDs, clears `chat.contextSummary`, resets `summaryAnchorMessageIds`, bumps `compactionGeneration` (so memory caches and whisper anchors refresh in step), and zeros `lastSummaryTurn` / `lastFullRebuildTurn` so the next gate evaluation sees "first-time generation" and fires soft. No-ops when none of the changed IDs were covered (typo fixes on a recently arrived message leave the summary intact). Wired into both PUT (edit) and DELETE (single-message + swipe-group cascade) paths in `app/api/v1/messages/[id]/route.ts`.
- **Test coverage.** New `__tests__/unit/lib/chat/summary-invalidation.test.ts` — 7 tests covering empty-id short-circuit, no-summary skip, no-anchor skip, non-covered-message skip, covered-message invalidation (with generation bump check), one-of-many coverage, and findById-failure resilience.

#### LLM cost reduction Phase 3: stable memory pool + whisper anchoring

Phase 3 of the cost-reduction plan. Replaces the per-turn rank-driven memory injection with a two-pool design that keeps the bulk of recall byte-stable across turns within a compaction generation. Identity reinforcement and persona content are deliberately untouched, so the LLM-visible structure is unchanged except for memory ordering and a smaller dynamic head.

- **Two-pool memory architecture.** New `lib/memory/frozen-archive-cache.ts` returns the top 25 memories by effective weight (importance × time decay) at the current `compactionGeneration`, sorted by `memory.id` ascending so the formatted text is byte-stable across turns. Cache key is `(characterId, compactionGeneration)`; on generation bump the entry recomputes from the `findMostImportant` repository call. `lib/chat/context/memory-injector.ts` adds `formatFrozenMemoryArchive` (uses `memory.summary`, no per-turn re-rank, deterministic order) and `formatDynamicMemoryHead` (top 5 by current-turn rank, `[m_xxxx]` rank tags, hard-capped at 200 tokens — `DYNAMIC_HEAD_TOKEN_BUDGET`). `lib/chat/context-manager.ts:buildContext` now calls both: archive in the cacheable-prefix slot of the LLM-context tail, dynamic head appended after with a "Most relevant memories for this turn:" header. Memories already in the archive are filtered out of the dynamic head so the LLM doesn't see the same entry twice.
- **Removed `maxMemories` option from `BuildContextOptions`.** Replaced by `FROZEN_ARCHIVE_SIZE = 25` and `DYNAMIC_HEAD_DEFAULT_SIZE = 5` constants in the new modules. No external callers used the option (only `context-builder.service.ts` set it to its default of 18); dropped the unused parameter from both call sites.
- **Whisper anchoring with `summaryAnchor` field.** New `MessageEvent.summaryAnchor: { compactionGeneration: number } | null` field on `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, mirrored on `lib/database/repositories/chats-messages.ops.ts` and `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`. `postLibrarianSummaryAnnouncement` (`lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts`) accepts a `summaryAnchor` parameter and stamps it on every per-character summary whisper. `generatePerCharacterSummaryWhispers` (`lib/chat/context-summary.ts`) replaces the prior content-prefix sweep with an anchor-based sweep: removes only whispers whose anchor is from an older generation (or whose anchor is missing — the legacy fallback uses the prefix match for unanchored rows). New migration `add-summary-anchor-field-v1` ALTERs `chat_messages` to add the column; fresh-install DDL in `sqlite-initial-schema.ts` carries it natively. DDL.md updated.
- **Cache-determinism CI test.** New `__tests__/unit/cache-determinism/system-prompt.test.ts` exercises `buildSystemPrompt` against a fixed character fixture and asserts (a) byte-identical output across consecutive calls and (b) the SHA-256 hash matches a checked-in golden. Hash drift fails CI; engineers update the golden intentionally with `UPDATE_GOLDEN_PROMPT_HASH=1`.
- **Test coverage.** New `__tests__/unit/lib/chat/context/memory-injector.test.ts` covers the new formatters (deterministic order, byte-stability across calls, summary not body, token-budget truncation, [m_xxxx] tags). New `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/frozen-archive-cache.test.ts` covers cache hit/miss by generation, recompute on generation bump, sorted-by-id output, archive-size cap, and per-character isolation. The character-voice eval scaffold (`__tests__/eval/character-voice/README.md`) is updated to defer the runnable harness to Phase 4 — Phase 3 changes are mechanical enough not to need a regression gate.

#### LLM cost reduction Phase 2: triple-gate summarization

Phase 2 of the cost-reduction plan. Replaces the per-checkpoint summarization trigger with a budget-driven triple-gate so most turns reuse the cached summary unchanged. Independent of any architectural redesign — just a smarter trigger. Title-checkpoint logic is unchanged and runs on its own clock.

- **Triple-gate trigger.** New `evaluateSummarizationGate` in `lib/chat/context-summary.ts` returns `'skip' | 'soft' | 'hard'` based on three thresholds: `T_SOFT_TOKEN_THRESHOLD = 8000` (8K tokens added since last refresh), `T_SOFT_TURN_THRESHOLD = 8` (8 interchanges since last refresh), and `T_HARD_TURN_THRESHOLD = 50` (50 interchanges since last full rebuild). `T_promote` is intentionally deferred to Phase 4 since the layered-summary structure does not exist yet. Most turns return `'skip'` and reuse the existing `chat.contextSummary` unchanged. `checkAndGenerateSummaryIfNeeded` calls the gate after the (unchanged) title-checkpoint logic runs and uses `forceRegenerate: decision === 'hard'` so soft fires take the cheap incremental `updateContextSummary` path while hard fires reset accumulated recursive drift.
- **Compaction-generation tracking.** Four new columns on `chats`: `compactionGeneration` (monotonic counter bumped on every fire — used by Phase 3 to anchor memory pools and per-character whispers), `lastSummaryTurn`, `lastSummaryTokens`, `lastFullRebuildTurn`. Schema in `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts` (added to both `ChatMetadataSchema` and `ChatMetadataBaseSchema`); migration `add-summarization-gate-fields-v1`; fresh-install DDL in `sqlite-initial-schema.ts`; DDL.md updated. `generateContextSummary` now writes all four fields when it persists a new summary.
- **Removed redundant inner gate.** The previous `chatNeedsSummary` early-return inside `generateContextSummary` (which rejected updates on chats with < 100 messages) was incompatible with the upstream gate — the gate would decide to fire and `generateContextSummary` would short-circuit. Removed; the gate is the single decision point now. `chatNeedsSummary` is retained as an exported helper for any external caller that might still want it.
- **Per-character whisper outcome metrics.** The "regenerate" vs "reuse global summary" decision in `generatePerCharacterSummaryWhispers` was logged at DEBUG level; promoted to INFO with a structured `whisperOutcome` field (`'regenerated' | 'reused'`) so reuse fraction is queryable without enabling debug logging. Validates Phase 4 ROI before committing to the redesign.
- **Test coverage.** New `__tests__/unit/lib/chat/summarization-gate.test.ts` exercises the gate decision matrix (skip below threshold, soft on either threshold, hard on 50-turn ceiling, hard preferred over soft when both fire) plus a 50-turn simulation that asserts fire count drops from ~9 (old behavior) to 5–8 with at least one hard fire.

#### LLM cost reduction Phase 1: cache observability + provider parity

Phase 1 of the cost-reduction plan in `docs/developer/features/llm_api_costs_breakdown.md`. Closes provider-parity gaps in cache instrumentation, canonicalizes the tools array, and adds the cache-key parameters that providers need to keep cache hits from sharding across machines. No behavioral changes to chat output.

- **Cache token extraction on OpenAI / Grok / Google plugins.** Anthropic already returned `cacheReadInputTokens`; the others didn't. `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openai/provider.ts` and `qtap-plugin-grok/provider.ts` now read `usage.input_tokens_details.cached_tokens` from the Responses API; `qtap-plugin-google/provider.ts` reads `usageMetadata.cachedContentTokenCount`. All three populate `cacheUsage` on `LLMResponse` and the final stream chunk so the existing `streaming.service.ts` → `logLLMCall` path captures hit counts end-to-end. Bumped patch versions on each plugin (manifest + package).
- **Per-tier prefix hashes in `llm_logs`.** New `requestHashes` JSON column on the `llm_logs` table holds SHA-256 (truncated 16-char) hashes of the cacheable tiers: system block 1, system block 2, the canonicalized tools array, and the frozen-history tail (everything except the trailing message). Hash drift in any tier signals the provider cache will miss. Computed in `lib/llm/cache-prefix-hashes.ts:computeRequestPrefixHashes` and threaded through `streaming.service.ts`. New migration `add-llm-logs-request-hashes-column-v1` ALTERs the existing `llm_logs` table; the constant `LLM_LOGS_TABLE_DDL` in `move-llm-logs-to-separate-db.ts` was also extended for fresh installs. Schema added to `lib/schemas/llm-log.types.ts` (`LLMLogRequestHashesSchema`) with re-exports in `lib/schemas/types.ts`. DDL.md updated.
- **Tool list canonicalization.** `lib/tools/canonicalize.ts:canonicalizeUniversalTools` sorts `universalTools` alphabetically by `function.name` and recursively sorts JSON-Schema object keys inside each tool's `parameters`. Applied in `lib/tools/plugin-tool-builder.ts` after the tools are assembled and before the provider's `formatTools()` is called. Without this, plugin tools registered via `Map` iteration order or schema-key authoring order produced byte-different tool arrays across requests, defeating the prefix cache. Snapshot test in `__tests__/unit/lib/tools/canonicalize.test.ts`.
- **Provider `prompt_cache_key` parameters.** New module `lib/llm/cache-key.ts` defines `PROMPT_CACHE_STRUCTURE_VERSION` (currently `1`) and `buildPromptCacheKey(chatId)` → `quilltap:chat:<chatId>:v<version>`. `streaming.service.ts` injects this into `profileParameters.promptCacheKey`. The OpenAI plugin reads it and sets `prompt_cache_key` on Responses API requests (plus `prompt_cache_retention: '24h'` for gpt-5.1 / gpt-5.2 / gpt-5.5 — `gpt-5.3-chat-latest` is intentionally excluded since it's not in the extended-retention model list). The Grok plugin (which targets the xAI Responses API via the OpenAI SDK) sets the same field; without it Grok round-robins across servers and effectively never hits cache. Bump policy: changing tool schemas, system-prompt structure, persona block format, or memory-pool format requires bumping `PROMPT_CACHE_STRUCTURE_VERSION` to invalidate provider caches in lockstep.
- **Anthropic mid-history breakpoint + streamMessage fix.** New `applyMidHistoryBreakpoint` in `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-anthropic/provider.ts` places a second `cache_control` breakpoint on a message ~15 indices back from the tail when `messages.length >= 20`. The index is rounded down to the nearest multiple of 15 so the breakpoint stays at the same content block for several turns rather than rewriting cache every turn. Without this, Anthropic's 20-block lookback from the tail breakpoint silently misses cache on long tool-use-heavy turns. Same call also fixes a parallel bug in `streamMessage` that still used `find(m => m.role === 'system')` post-commit-68a9eba6 (so block 2 was being silently dropped on streaming requests); now uses `filter` and emits all system blocks identically to `sendMessage`.
- **Eval harness scaffold.** `__tests__/eval/cache-stability/` asserts hash stability for systemBlock1 / systemBlock2 / tools across synthetic 30-turn fixtures, with an append-only-history transition counter. Phase 3 will plug recorded `BuiltContext` snapshots into the same harness. `__tests__/eval/character-voice/README.md` documents the deferred Phase 3 voice-regression gate.

#### Prompt restructure: two system messages, off-scene characters move to Host history

- **Two system messages instead of one.** `buildContext` (`lib/chat/context-manager.ts`) now emits the chat character's identity stack as the first system message and the (now fully static) Identity Reminder as a second system message. Together they produce a long stable prefix that providers can prefix-cache; the previous monolithic single-message prompt mixed cacheable and turn-variable content in the same string and defeated caching.
- **Identity Reminder is now fully static.** `buildIdentityReinforcement` (`lib/chat/context/system-prompt-builder.ts`) no longer accepts `userName` or `otherParticipantNames` and no longer interpolates a per-turn "do not write dialogue for [list]" of active participants. Phrasing is now the static "Do not write dialogue, actions, or thoughts for any other character." Other-participant attribution comes from the existing Host roster announcements + per-message `name` fields. Removed the unused `userName` / `otherCharacterNames` arguments at the help-chat call site (`lib/help-chat/system-prompt-builder.ts`). Test suite updated.
- **Off-scene character cards moved out of the system prompt.** Workspace characters that get name-dropped in chat history but aren't current participants used to have their full character cards spliced into the per-turn system prompt — re-injected on every turn, varying turn-to-turn based on regex hits. They now ride as one-time Host introductions in chat history. New helpers in `lib/services/host-notifications/writer.ts`: `buildOffSceneCharactersContent`, `findIntroducedOffSceneCharacterIds`, `postHostOffSceneCharactersAnnouncement`. Idempotence is per character ID per chat — once introduced, never re-introduced.
- **`hostEvent` schema widened.** `participantId` and `toStatus` are now optional, and an optional `introducedCharacterIds: UUID[]` is added so the off-scene announcer can stamp which character IDs an introduction covered. Mirrored in `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/chats-messages.ops.ts`, `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`, and the local `MessageWithParticipant.hostEvent` type in `lib/chat/context/message-attribution.ts`. The presence-window pipeline (`computePresenceWindowsForParticipant`) now requires both fields to be set before processing an event, so off-scene-introduction announcements are correctly ignored.
- **`formatMentionedCharactersSection` retired.** The function and its tests in `__tests__/unit/mentioned-characters.test.ts` were removed; coverage moved to `buildOffSceneCharactersContent` tests in `__tests__/unit/lib/services/host-notifications-phase-c.test.ts`. `findMentionedCharacterIds` is unchanged — it still drives the off-scene mention scan.
- **Anthropic plugin: multi-system-message support and prefix-cache breakpoint.** `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-anthropic/provider.ts` now collects every system-role message from `params.messages` (it previously kept only the first and silently dropped the rest). When prompt caching is enabled, the cache breakpoint is placed on the FIRST system block (the stable identity stack); subsequent system blocks follow outside the cached prefix. When caching is disabled with multiple system messages, all blocks are emitted as text blocks rather than collapsing to a single string.
- **New help page.** `help/salon-host-introductions.md` explains the once-per-chat Host introduction in Quilltap's voice.

#### Fix: scene state tracking truncated at 1000 completion tokens

- `updateSceneState` in `lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks/image-scene-tasks.ts` was calling `executeCheapLLMTask` without a `maxTokens` argument, so it inherited the cheap-LLM default of 1000 in `core-execution.ts`. Scenes with several characters and a non-trivial location description ran out of room mid-JSON, causing parse failures. Now passes `maxTokens: 4000` explicitly.

#### AI Wizard + Summon From Lore: vantage-point field semantics

- **Shared preamble.** Extracted `FIELD_SEMANTICS_PREAMBLE` into `lib/services/character-field-semantics.ts` so the character optimizer, the AI Wizard, and Summon From Lore all instruct the LLM with the same identity / description / personality / title definitions. The optimizer now imports the constant from the shared module.
- **AI Wizard prompts rewritten.** `lib/services/character-wizard.service.ts` adds an `identity` entry to `FIELD_PROMPTS`, rewrites `description` to drop "Physical appearance" (it now asks for behavior, mannerisms, and verbal patterns only — appearance is generated separately into `physicalDescription`), and tightens `personality` to the self-knowledge vantage point. Each of the three vantage-point prompts injects the shared preamble. `WizardRequest` now carries `identity` in `existingData` and `fieldsToGenerate`. `buildContextPrompt` surfaces existing identity and tells the LLM that any visual reference is for `physicalDescription` only — it must not bleed into identity / description / personality.
- **Summon From Lore prompts rewritten.** `CHARACTER_BASICS_PROMPT` in `lib/services/ai-import.service.ts` adds an `identity` JSON key, restates the description / personality definitions in vantage-point terms, and prepends the shared preamble. `assembleQtapExport` writes `identity` onto the character object so the import path picks it up via `repos.characters.create({ ...charData })`.
- **AI Wizard UI.** `components/characters/ai-wizard/types.ts` adds `identity` to `GeneratableField`, `FIELD_LABELS`, and `FIELD_DESCRIPTIONS`; `steps/FieldSelectionStep.tsx` slots the new checkbox between Title and Description; `hooks/useAIWizard.ts` lists identity in the available-fields default.
- **Apply paths + new-character form.** `app/aurora/[id]/edit/page.tsx` applies generated `identity` alongside description/personality. `app/aurora/new/page.tsx` adds `identity` to `formData`, the wizard apply spread, and the form itself (new Identity textarea between Title and Description, and rewritten placeholder copy on Title / Description / Personality so they match the four-vantage-point definitions used elsewhere).
- **Help docs.** `help/ai-character-import.md` adds a "Field Vantage Points" section and updates the basics-step row to mention identity; `help/character-creation.md` rewrites the AI Wizard field list to the new ordering and notes the four vantage points.

#### Maintenance: dead-code cleanup from Knip

- Unexported local-only types in `lib/help-guide/categories.ts` and `lib/file-storage/project-store-bridge.ts`.
- Removed unused barrel re-exports from `components/wardrobe/index.ts`.
- Refreshed `docs/developer/DEAD-CODE-REPORT.md` with the 2026-04-29 Knip findings and cleanup notes.

#### Fix: scope:project diverged from the project's official document store

- **Root cause.** `convert-project-files-to-document-stores-v1` (April 23) moved every project's on-disk file directory into a database-backed mount point and `add-project-official-mount-point-v1` (April 25) wrote that mount's id into `projects.officialMountPointId`. Prospero already advertises this mount as the canonical "project-official" store and tells the LLM that `scope: 'project'` is an alias for it. But `lib/doc-edit/path-resolver.ts:resolveProjectPath` was never updated — it kept resolving `scope: 'project'` to `<filesDir>/<projectId>/<path>` on disk. Every `doc_write_file({ scope: 'project' })`, `doc_create_folder`, etc. silently recreated the legacy directory and wrote into it, while Document Mode UI / the Scriptorium read from the database mount. Files written by Friday looked fine to `doc_list_files` (which also walked the legacy fs) but were invisible to the UI.
- **Resolver fix.** `resolveProjectPath` now looks up `project.officialMountPointId`. When set, it dispatches through that mount: database-backed mounts return a `ResolvedPath` with `mountType: 'database'` and `mountPointId` populated (so `readFileWithMtime` / `writeFileWithMtimeCheck` route bytes through `lib/mount-index/database-store`); filesystem/Obsidian mounts return a path under `mountPoint.basePath`. Only when no official mount exists does it fall through to the legacy `<filesDir>/<projectId>/` layout.
- **Handler fixes.** Two doc-edit handlers bypass the path resolver and walk the legacy fs directly: `handleListFiles` and `handleGrep` in `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts`. Both now check `resolveOfficialProjectMount(context.projectId)` first. When an official mount exists, `handleListFiles` enumerates from the database mount (only when `scope: 'project'` is explicitly requested — multi-scope mode picks it up via the document_store branch already), and `handleGrep` skips the legacy walk entirely. All other doc-edit handlers (`handleWriteFile`, `handleMoveFile`, `handleCopyFile`, `handleDeleteFile`, `handleCreateFolder`, `handleDeleteFolder`, `handleMoveFolder`) already dispatched on `resolved.mountType === 'database'`, so they pick up the new resolution automatically.
- **Reabsorb migration.** New migration `reabsorb-leftover-project-files-v1` (`migrations/scripts/reabsorb-leftover-project-files.ts`) handles instances where the divergence already happened. For each project with `officialMountPointId` set and a leftover directory at `<filesDir>/<projectId>/`, it walks the directory, imports any file not already in the database mount (compared by `relativePath`), and renames the directory to a fresh `_doc_store_archive_v2` (collision-suffixed up to `_v99`, then UUID). Skips projects whose official mount is filesystem-backed (path semantics already match) and projects with no official mount (resolver fallback is correct for them). Idempotent — re-running on an instance that's already been handled is a no-op because the directory is gone.
- **Concrete impact (Friday).** Project `Quilltap Plans` (`f29e2112-...`) had three Scenarios files written via `doc_write_file({ scope: 'project' })` on April 29 that landed in `~/iCloud/Quilltap/Friday/files/f29e2112-.../Scenarios/` but were absent from the `Project Files: Quilltap Plans` mount (`4c1a9cf6-...`). The Document Mode picker couldn't see them. Resolver fix alone makes new writes land in the right place; the reabsorb migration moves the existing leftover Scenarios + Feature Requests + Folio Drafts files into the mount.

#### Fix: backup + restore failed with "Invalid string length" on large instances

- **Root cause (write side).** `writeJsonFile` in `lib/backup/backup-service.ts` called `JSON.stringify(data, null, 2)`, which returns a single string. With ~17k LLM-log rows totalling ~720 MB of `request`/`response` text, the encoded string exceeded V8's ~512 MB max-string limit and threw `RangeError: Invalid string length`. The route returned a generic 500 and the client logged `Backup creation failed {}`.
- **Fix (write side).** Added `writeJsonArrayFile` that streams the array to disk via `Readable.from` + `pipeline`, encoding one element at a time so each `JSON.stringify` call stays bounded. All twenty data-array writes now use it; `writeJsonFile` is reserved for the small manifest. Output format is byte-identical to the previous pretty-printed JSON.
- **Root cause (read side).** `readJsonFile` in `lib/backup/restore-service.ts` did `fs.readFile(path, 'utf8')` followed by `JSON.parse(content)`. Both steps materialize the whole file as one string, so a large `llm-logs.json` would throw `ERR_STRING_TOO_LONG` before parsing even started — making backups created on large instances impossible to import.
- **Fix (read side).** Added `readJsonArrayFile`, a JSON-aware streaming scanner that reads the file in 1 MB chunks, tracks string/escape state and brace/bracket depth to find top-level element boundaries, and `JSON.parse`s one element at a time. Per-element memory stays bounded by individual row size (a few MB at most). All twenty data-array reads in `parseBackupZip` route through it (with a `readJsonArrayFileOptional` variant for back-compat optional files); `readJsonFile` is kept for the manifest. Smoke-checked against escaped quotes, `}`/`]` inside strings, nested objects, unicode, and multi-MB elements crossing chunk boundaries.

#### Character optimizer: about-self filter + new `identity` field

- **Memory pool filtered to about-self.** `runCharacterOptimizer` (`lib/services/character-optimizer.service.ts`) now pulls candidates via `findByCharacterAboutCharacter(characterId, characterId)` and `searchByContentAboutCharacter(characterId, characterId, query)` instead of `findByCharacterId` / `searchByContent`. Memories the character holds about other participants (the user, other characters in a scene) are excluded so behavioral-pattern analysis isn't averaged across other people's habits. Legacy null-`aboutCharacterId` memories are excluded by design — the post-attribution-overhaul pipeline collapses self-references to the holder, so null is genuinely unattributed and not a fallback.
- **New `identity` Character field.** Adds `identity` to `CharacterSchema` (`lib/schemas/character.types.ts`), the characters table DDL (`migrations/scripts/sqlite-initial-schema.ts`), and a new migration `add-character-identity-field-v1` (`migrations/scripts/add-character-identity-field.ts`) that runs an idempotent `ALTER TABLE characters ADD COLUMN identity TEXT` on existing databases. Also wired through `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`.
- **Field semantics, canonized.** Schema JSDoc, CLAUDE.md, the Aurora editor placeholder text, and `help/character-editing.md` now spell out the four character fields by vantage point: identity (outside / public), description (acquaintance / behavior), personality (inside / self-knowledge), title (private user/character framing). The optimizer's `getAnalysisPrompt` and `getGeneralFieldsSuggestionsPrompt` carry the same preamble and enforce the vantage-point rule when proposing edits.
- **Vault overlay wired for identity.md.** `character-properties-overlay.ts` adds `CHARACTER_IDENTITY_MD_PATH`, registers the markdown descriptor, and reads/writes identity through the same all-or-nothing overlay as description/personality. The `readCharacterVaultIdentity` helper joins the existing readers; `populateVaultWithCharacterData` (`lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts`) now writes `character.identity ?? ''` into `identity.md` instead of the synthesized name + pronouns + aliases header (the dead `renderIdentityMarkdown` helper was removed). Existing vaults whose identity.md still holds the old auto-rendered header will surface that content as the seed for the new field on read.
- **Aurora editor + view.** New Identity textarea before Description in `CharacterBasicInfo.tsx`, with placeholders rewritten to match the four-vantage-point definitions. View page (`CharacterDetails.tsx`) renders Identity above Description. `CharacterFormData` and the form-init in `useCharacterEdit.ts` carry the new field. The optimizer suggestion-apply path (`useCharacterOptimizer.ts`) treats `identity` as a simple-field update; ApplyConfirmation labels and badge classes include identity.
- **Help docs.** `help/character-editing.md` rewrites the Title / Description / Personality entries and adds Identity, with the four canonical definitions in Quilltap voice. `help/character-optimizer.md` documents the about-self filter and the four-field eligibility list.
- **DDL.md** column annotations spell out the vantage-point split next to the `characters` table definition.

#### Inter-character memory fetch: SQLite ranks and caps each partition

- **Window function instead of unbounded fetch.** `MemoriesRepository.findByCharacterAboutCharacters` (`lib/database/repositories/memories.repository.ts`) now takes a required `limitPerCharacter` and runs a `ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY aboutCharacterId ORDER BY importance DESC, COALESCE(lastReinforcedAt, createdAt) DESC)` CTE through `rawQuery`. Each partition is ranked and capped server-side, so we decode a bounded number of rows per about-character instead of every matching memory. Hand-hydration handles the JSON-encoded array columns (`keywords`, `tags`, `relatedMemoryIds`) since the rawQuery path bypasses `SQLiteCollection.find`. The `embedding` BLOB rides through `MemorySchema.safeParse` directly.
- **Tie-break key.** Sort key approximates `calculateEffectiveWeight` so a recently-reinforced memory beats a stale one of equal raw importance — the formatter still re-ranks by effective weight in JS over the much smaller post-CTE set.
- **Budget-driven sizing.** `lib/chat/context-manager.ts` derives the per-character cap from the inter-character whisper budget: `maxEntries = ceil(interCharacterBudget / 40)`, `maxEntriesPerCharacter = max(20, ceil(maxEntries / otherChars) × 3)`. The 3× buffer absorbs (a) effective-weight re-ranking diverging from raw importance order and (b) shorter-than-average lines packing tighter than the 40-token estimate.
- **Concrete impact (Friday + Charlie + Amy).** Old: 10,081 rows decoded, importance down to 0.35. New (200k-context budget, 150 per character): 600 rows, all at importance ≥ 0.95 — the same rows that would have made it through the budget cut anyway.
- **Tests.** New unit suite `__tests__/unit/lib/database/repositories/memories-find-by-about.test.ts` pins the SQL shape (window function present, partition + sort key, parameter wiring), early-return paths (empty `aboutCharacterIds`, non-positive limit), and the JSON-column hydration + `rn` strip. The existing `context-management.test.ts` assertion for the call signature was updated to allow the new third argument.
- **`rawQuery` recognizes `WITH` and `EXPLAIN`.** The SQLite backend's `rawQuery` (`lib/database/backends/sqlite/backend.ts`) routed only `SELECT`/`PRAGMA` through `.all()` and everything else through `.run()`. CTE-leading queries fell into the `.run()` branch, which returns a `RunResult` instead of rows — caused `rows is not iterable` for the new partition fetch. Now also routes `WITH` and `EXPLAIN` through `.all()`.

#### Memory attribution: holder-dominance tiebreaker + whispers carry full content

- **Tiebreaker (v2).** `resolveAboutCharacterId` (`lib/memory/about-character-resolution.ts`) now accepts a `holderCharacter` argument and applies a dominance check when both holder and about-character are named in the same memory. New helpers `namesForHolder` and `countNameOccurrences` count word-boundary hits for each side; if the holder is mentioned **strictly more often**, the row flips to a self-reference. Ties go to the about-character (the original Q3 policy is preserved). Holder names exclude `user`/`the user` so we don't double-count generic aliases that only matter for matching user-controlled about-targets. The runtime call site in `createMemoryWithGate` now loads holder + about-character in parallel before invoking the resolver.
- **v2 backfill migration.** `migrations/scripts/align-about-character-id-v2.ts` (`align-about-character-id-v2`, depends on `align-about-character-id-v1`) re-walks the memories whose `aboutCharacterId` is set and not self, applies the dominance check, and flips rows where the holder dominates. Logs per-character flipped counts. Targets the residual borderline tail v1 left behind — memories like *"Friday calls the current moment a 'hinge' and urges Charlie to switch on the fix"* (Friday × 2, Charlie × 1) that v1 kept attributed to Charlie because v1 was a presence check, not a dominance check.
- **Whispers carry full content, not summary.** `formatRelevantMemoriesForContext` and `formatInterCharacterMemoriesForContext` in `lib/chat/context/memory-injector.ts` now compose each per-line whisper from `memory.content` (falling back to `memory.summary` when content is empty). The recap path (`memory-recap.ts`) stays on `summary` because that's the cache-friendly input the cheap LLM narrates from. The token-budget guard runs against the longer line, so high-budget whispers carry the original extraction body verbatim while low-budget ones still cap correctly.
- **Tests.** `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/about-character-resolution.test.ts` gains a `holder-dominance tiebreaker (v2)` describe block covering: dominance flip, tie keeps about-character, about-character dominance keeps attribution, missing `holderCharacter` falls back to v1 behavior, holder-aliases count toward dominance but generic user aliases don't. Plus new specs for `countNameOccurrences` and `namesForHolder`.

#### Fix: self-referential memories were being labelled "about the user"

- **Root cause.** `lib/memory/memory-processor.ts` ran two parallel auto-extraction passes per turn — `extractMemoryFromMessage` (about the user) and `extractCharacterMemoryFromMessage` (self-referential, about the character themselves) — but both branches called the same `createMemoryFromCandidate` helper, which hard-coded `aboutCharacterId: ctx.userCharacterId || null`. Every self-extracted memory was therefore written as if it were about the user (or null when no user-character was resolved), polluting the inter-character signal in the data and skewing optimizer / recall ranking.
- **Helper split.** `createMemoryFromCandidate` is replaced by two helpers in `memory-processor.ts`: `createUserMemoryFromCandidate` (about-target = `ctx.userCharacterId`) and `createSelfMemoryFromCandidate` (about-target = `ctx.characterId`). Each extraction branch wires to its own helper.
- **Skip user-memory pass when no user-character is attached.** When `resolveUserIdentity` does not produce a `characterId`, the user-memory extraction call is bypassed entirely instead of fabricating a `null`-targeted memory. A debug log line and a one-time Host whisper (`systemKind: 'no-user-character'`) prompt the operator to attach or create a user persona. The whisper is idempotent — only one is posted per chat — and is suppressed in chats that already have one.
- **Name-presence safety net.** New module `lib/memory/about-character-resolution.ts` exports `nameAppears`, `namesForAboutCharacter`, and `resolveAboutCharacterId`. `createMemoryWithGate` (`lib/memory/memory-service.ts`) now applies the rule before insert: for AUTO memories with a non-self `aboutCharacterId`, if the about-character's name + aliases (plus generic `user` / `the user` for `controlledBy: 'user'` characters) do not appear in `summary + content`, `aboutCharacterId` is collapsed to the holder's id (self-reference). MANUAL memories pass through unchanged so explicit user attributions are honoured. Failures in the lookup never block a write.
- **Backfill migration.** `migrations/scripts/align-about-character-id.ts` (`align-about-character-id-v1`, depends on `sqlite-initial-schema-v1` and `rename-persona-columns-v1`) walks every memory and applies the same rule:
  - Memories where `aboutCharacterId` is set but the about-character's name set is absent from the text → flipped to the holder's id.
  - Memories where `aboutCharacterId IS NULL` → if exactly one user-controlled character's specific name/aliases appear, attributed to that persona; otherwise if generic `user`/`the user` appears AND there is exactly one user-controlled character system-wide, attributed to that persona; otherwise flipped to the holder.
  - Memories where the holder and the existing about-character are both named in the text are left as-is (the existing about-attribution wins).
  - Self-references (`aboutCharacterId === characterId`) and ambiguous null rows (multiple user-personas named, or generic-user with multiple personas) are left untouched.
  - Per-character flipped/attributed/untouched counts are logged at the migration's `info` level so post-run spot-checks don't need a separate query.
- **New host whisper helper.** `postHostNoUserCharacterAnnouncement` in `lib/services/host-notifications/writer.ts` posts the advisory whisper. It checks the chat's existing messages for a `systemSender: 'host'` row with `systemKind: 'no-user-character'` and is a no-op if one exists.
- **Tests.** New unit suite `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/about-character-resolution.test.ts` covers the name-presence rule, alias handling, and the user-controlled augmentation. The existing `memory-processor-regression.test.ts` was updated to (a) thread `userCharacterId` through `baseContext` so the user-memory pass still fires under the new gate, (b) mock the host-notifications writer module to avoid pulling in the database stack, and (c) add three new cases verifying the no-user-character skip, that self-pass writes `aboutCharacterId === characterId`, and that user-pass writes `aboutCharacterId === userCharacterId`.

#### Fix: sync-properties-from-vault hits UNIQUE constraint on rebuild

- The `sync-properties-from-vault` action on `/api/v1/characters/[id]` rebuilds wardrobe items and outfit presets by deleting all existing rows and reinserting from vault files. It was using `repos.wardrobe.delete` / `repos.outfitPresets.delete` and `.create`, every one of which awaits `syncCharacterVaultWardrobe` as a post-write side effect. That sync calls `ingestVaultOnlyWardrobeIntoDb`, which sees the just-deleted item still on disk and promotes it back into the DB before the next iteration runs. The table never empties, and the recreate phase fails with `UNIQUE constraint failed: wardrobe_items.id`.
- Fix: added `deleteRaw` to `WardrobeRepository` and `OutfitPresetsRepository` (mirrors the existing `createFromVault` / `findByCharacterIdRaw` bypass methods) and switched the route handler at `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts` to use `deleteRaw` for the wipe and `createFromVault` for the rebuild. Both bypass the sync chain so the loop runs to completion without re-ingesting itself.

#### Collapsible Staff-message bars in the Salon

- **New `systemKind` field.** Added a string column on `chat_messages` (Zod field on `MessageEventSchema` and `ChatMessageRowSchema`) carrying a stable kebab-case sub-classification of any Staff-authored message — e.g. `timestamp`, `project-context`, `memory-recap`, `tool-run`. Migration: `migrations/scripts/add-system-kind-field.ts` (`add-system-kind-field-v1`). Every writer now persists a `systemKind`: Lantern (`avatar` / `background` / `character-image`), Aurora (`opening-outfit` / `outfit-change`), Librarian (`opened-by-user`, `saved`, `renamed`, `summary`, etc.), Concierge (`danger`), Prospero (`connection-profile-change`, `project-context`, `tool-run`), Host (`add` / `remove` / `status-change` / `scenario` / `roster` / `timestamp` / `silent-mode-enter` / `silent-mode-exit` / `user-character` / `join-scenario`), Commonplace Book (`memory-recap` / `relevant-memories` / `inter-character-memories` / `consolidated`). Tool-run TOOL rows from `actions/tools.ts` and `actions/run-tool.ts` get `systemKind: 'tool-run'`.
- **Salon collapse UI.** Staff-authored assistant rows in the Salon now render as a thin one-line bar by default — sender display name, humanized kind label (e.g. "project information", "time"), timestamp, chevron — and expand to the full message on click. A new "collapse" chevron in the action bar reverses the state. Expansion state is tracked per-message in `expandedSystemMessageIds` on the Salon page and threaded through `VirtualizedMessageList` into `MessageRow`. Sender/kind labels live in `app/salon/[id]/components/system-message-labels.ts`. New `qt-chat-system-bar*` utility classes in `app/styles/qt-components/_chat.css` with light/dark tokens in `_variables.css`.
- **Schema/export updates.** `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json` and `docs/developer/DDL.md` updated for the new column.

#### Tool calls render as standalone bubbles attributed to the actor

- **All TOOL rows are standalone.** `useChatData.groupToolsWithMessages` is removed; both character-initiated and user-initiated TOOL messages render as their own row in the salon timeline. The `Message.toolCalls` field, the embedded-tool render block in `MessageRow`, and the `embedded` prop on `ToolMessage` are removed as dead code.
- **Character attribution.** `saveToolMessages` in `lib/services/chat-message/tool-execution.service.ts` now persists the responding character's `participantId` on TOOL rows; both call sites (`message-finalizer.service.ts` and `orchestrator.service.ts`) pass it through. `VirtualizedMessageList` resolves `headerAvatar` via `getMessageAvatar`, falling back to the most recent ASSISTANT row's participant when the TOOL message predates the participantId persistence change.
- **Unified `ToolMessage` header.** `ToolMessage` now takes a single `headerAvatar` prop (replacing `systemAvatar`) and renders a consistent layout: the author avatar on the left, the author name (Prospero or the character) in the header, an `actor ran <tool>` line below it, and the existing collapsible Request/Response panes. For Prospero rows the actor is the operator (`toolData.operatorName`); for character rows the actor name matches the header and is suppressed below it to avoid duplication.

#### User-initiated tool runs are Prospero bubbles

- **Standalone Prospero rendering.** TOOL messages produced by the Run Tool modal are no longer visually grouped into the user's bubble. `useChatData.groupToolsWithMessages` only groups character-initiated TOOL messages under the preceding ASSISTANT message; user-initiated TOOL messages render as their own row.
- **Prospero authorship.** `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/run-tool.ts` now persists `systemSender: 'prospero'` on the TOOL message and embeds the operator's display name (`user.name || user.username`) in the JSON content. `VirtualizedMessageList` passes a `systemAvatar` prop to `ToolMessage`; the standalone layout swaps the muted tool-icon circle for the Prospero portrait and shows a "{operatorName} ran `{toolName}`" attribution under "Prospero". Existing collapsible Request/Response panes with individual copy buttons are unchanged.
- **Private (whisper) toggle.** `RunToolModal` has a new "Private (whisper)" checkbox (default off). When checked, the API writes the operator's userId into `targetParticipantIds`. The userId is a UUID but never a participant ID, so the salon visibility filter at `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx` hides the bubble unless "show all whispers" is on, and `filterWhisperMessages` excludes it from every character's LLM context.
- **Single-character context honors TOOL whispers.** `lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts` now drops TOOL messages with non-empty `targetParticipantIds` that don't include the responding character before building conversation messages, so private runs don't leak into single-character chats (multi-character mode already filtered via `filterWhisperMessages` in the context manager).

#### Per-character Librarian summaries

- **Summaries are now whispered, not broadcast.** The Librarian still regenerates `chat.contextSummary` at the same checkpoints (used by title generation, danger classification, story background, etc.), but the conversation-summary message in the transcript is now produced once per LLM-controlled CHARACTER participant and whispered privately to them via `targetParticipantIds`. Each character may have entered mid-chat or stepped away and back, so each gets a summary tailored to what they actually saw.
- **Visible-slice computation.** For each participant, the summary input is built by composing (1) the existing `filterMessagesByHistoryAccess` slice (skip messages before they joined unless `hasHistoryAccess === true`), (2) a new presence-window slice that drops messages during periods they were `absent` or `removed`, and (3) the existing `filterWhisperMessages` step. Presence windows are computed from Host status announcements — see the new `computePresenceWindowsForParticipant` and `filterMessagesByPresenceWindows` helpers in `lib/chat/context/message-attribution.ts`.
- **Host status announcements now carry structured data.** Added `hostEvent` JSON column on `chat_messages` (`{ participantId, toStatus }`) plus a Zod field on `MessageEventSchema` and `ChatMessageRowSchema`. `postHostAddAnnouncement` / `postHostRemoveAnnouncement` / `postHostStatusChangeAnnouncement` in `lib/services/host-notifications/writer.ts` now require `participantId` and persist `hostEvent`. Migration: `migrations/scripts/add-host-event-field.ts` (`add-host-event-field-v1`). Other Host announcements (scenario, roster, timestamp, silent-mode, join-scenario) leave `hostEvent` NULL.
- **Call sites updated** in `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts`, and `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/participants.ts` to pass `participantId` (and `initialStatus` for adds). The add path was reordered so the new participant is resolved before the Host announcement fires.
- **Old whispered summaries are swept.** When a fresh per-character summary whisper is posted, prior Librarian summary whispers targeted at the same participant are deleted from the chat. Identified by `systemSender === 'librarian'`, exact single-target match, and the new `SUMMARY_CONTENT_PREFIX` content marker. Old broadcast summaries (from before this change) are not touched.
- **New repository helper.** `chats.repository.ts` and `lib/repositories/user-scoped.ts` expose `deleteMessagesByIds(chatId, ids[])`; underlying op added on `chats-messages.ops.ts`.
- **Reuse-when-equal optimization.** When a participant's visible slice contains exactly the same message IDs that fed the global summary (single-character chats with no absences and no whispers, etc.), the global summary text is reused verbatim rather than calling the cheap LLM again.
- **Catch-up summary on join.** When a character is added to a chat with `hasHistoryAccess === true`, `triggerCatchUpSummaryAsync` fires in the background to whisper a summary of prior history to the joining character right away — they don't have to wait for the next checkpoint. No-op when `hasHistoryAccess` is false; that case waits for the next regular regen.
- **Writer signature change.** `postLibrarianSummaryAnnouncement` now accepts `targetParticipantIds`. The exported `SUMMARY_CONTENT_PREFIX` constant is the canonical body marker for sweeping prior summaries.

#### System Prompt Refactor (Phase A + B + C + D + E + F + G + H + I)

Begun the move of dynamic state out of the per-turn system prompt and into Staff-authored ASSISTANT messages, so the system prompt can become a static, cache-friendly artifact and the chat transcript can become the single source of truth for state changes.

- **New Staff persona — the Commonplace Book.** Added `commonplaceBook` to the `systemSender` enum in `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/chats-messages.ops.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/types.ts`, and `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`. New writer module at `lib/services/commonplace-notifications/writer.ts` exports `postCommonplaceWhisper` (persistent path) and `voiceCommonplaceContent` (per-turn voicing helper). Avatar at `public/images/avatars/commonplace-book-avatar.webp` wired into `getMessageAvatar` in `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`. No database migration needed — the `chat_messages.systemSender` column has no CHECK constraint.
- **Memory tail moved out of the system prompt.** The memory recap, relevant memories, and inter-character memories used to be concatenated onto the system prompt. They are now persisted as a single consolidated Commonplace Book whisper per turn — voiced in the steampunk Quilltap style ("*The Commonplace Book lays open at your bookmark…*") — visible in the salon UI right after the user's message that triggered it, with the Commonplace Book avatar. For the LLM call, the same recall content is inlined into the new user message body in plain second-person framing ("You remember the following entries that bear on this moment: …") — no Staff persona, no meta-narrative, no consecutive-assistant alternation issue. Past Commonplace Book whispers are filtered out of `existingMessages` before context building (they live in the transcript for the user, but the LLM gets fresh recall each turn). The memories table remains the source of truth.
- **System transparency filter no longer drops Staff messages.** For opaque characters (`systemTransparency !== true`), `lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts` now strips the `systemSender` attribution but keeps the message body, so the LLM still receives content (scenario, status, memory) as a generic assistant line. Previously, opaque characters lost the message entirely. The salon UI is unaffected — the human user always sees Staff-attributed messages with their avatars.
- **Host content moved out of the system prompt (Phase C wire-up).** Scenario, user-character introduction, multi-character roster, own-status reminder, silent-mode rule, recent status changes, and join-scenario context now ship as Host-authored ASSISTANT messages in the chat transcript instead of being concatenated onto the per-turn system prompt.
  - **At chat creation** (`createInitialMessages` in `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts`): right after the SYSTEM message, the Host posts the scenario announcement (if a scenario is set), the user-character introduction (if a user character is configured), and — for multi-character chats — a welcome announcement for each LLM-controlled CHARACTER participant so each character learns about the others from the transcript.
  - **At participant add** (`processChatUpdates` in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts` and `handleAddParticipantAction` in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/participants.ts`): when a new participant has a non-empty `joinScenario` and `hasHistoryAccess === false`, the Host posts a private join-scenario whisper targeted at the joining participant via `targetParticipantIds`. Replaces the per-turn `## How You Entered This Conversation` insertion.
  - **At silent-mode transitions** (`handleParticipantUpdate` in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts`): when a participant transitions into or out of silent mode, the Host posts a private silent-mode entry or exit whisper carrying the full silent-mode rule directly to the affected character. Replaces the per-turn `## Silent Mode Active` block.
  - **System-prompt blocks dropped.** `lib/chat/context/system-prompt-builder.ts` no longer emits the `## Scenario`, `## User Character`, `## Other Participants in This Conversation`, `## Your Current Status`, `## Silent Mode Active`, or `## Recent Status Changes` blocks. `lib/chat/context-manager.ts` no longer appends `## How You Entered This Conversation` to the per-turn system prompt. The `otherParticipants`, `respondingCharacterStatus`, and `statusChangeNotifications` parameters remain on `buildSystemPrompt` for now to avoid call-site churn; they are unused and will be removed in Phase I cleanup.
  - **Tests updated.** `__tests__/unit/context-management.test.ts` was updated to assert that persona/user-character info and scenario text no longer appear in the per-turn system prompt, and that inter-character memories now ride on the new user message body rather than the system message.
- **Aurora content moved out of the system prompt (Phase D).** Outfit-change notifications, current outfit, and the available wardrobe roster now ship as Aurora-authored ASSISTANT messages in the chat transcript instead of being concatenated onto the per-turn system prompt.
  - **New writer** at `lib/services/aurora-notifications/writer.ts` exports `buildOpeningOutfitContent`, `buildOutfitChangeContent`, `postOpeningOutfitWhisper`, and `postOutfitChangeWhisper`. Aurora whispers do not need the dual persona/LLM voicing pattern that Commonplace Book recall does — the persona-voiced body is acceptable input for the LLM, and for opaque (`systemTransparency=false`) characters the `systemSender` attribution is stripped at context-build time but the body survives, so the content still reaches them as a generic assistant line.
  - **At chat creation** (`createInitialMessages` in `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts`): for each LLM-controlled CHARACTER participant with an equipped outfit, Aurora posts an opening whisper announcing the character's current attire and the alternatives in their wardrobe. Fires after the Host welcomes and before the first ASSISTANT greeting.
  - **On equip/unequip via the sidebar** (`app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/outfit.ts`): the `pendingOutfitNotifications` chat-field flow has been retired. Outfit changes now flow exclusively through the debounced Aurora wardrobe announcement (`enqueueWardrobeOutfitAnnouncement` → `handleWardrobeOutfitAnnouncement`). The debounced handler was refactored to use the new `postOutfitChangeWhisper` so its body now includes the available wardrobe alongside the current outfit.
  - **Orchestrator drain dropped.** `lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts` no longer reads or clears `chat.pendingOutfitNotifications`. The `outfitChangeNotifications` parameter on the context-builder options remains for now (unused) and will be removed in Phase I cleanup.
  - **System-prompt blocks dropped.** `lib/chat/context/system-prompt-builder.ts` no longer emits the `## ⚠️ Outfit Change Notice`, `## Current Outfit`, or `## Available Wardrobe` sections. The `wardrobeContext` and `outfitChangeNotifications` parameters remain on `buildSystemPrompt` (unused) for the same Phase I cleanup.
  - **Test updated.** `__tests__/unit/app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/outfit.test.ts` no longer asserts that the equip handler performs a bulk wardrobe lookup — the lookup moved into the debounced Aurora job.
  - **Deferred follow-ups** (still pending Phase D plumbing): mentioned-characters whisper (needs novelty tracking — schema field or a stable body-marker — to avoid re-announcing the same characters every turn), and physical-state delta whispers (no triggers exist yet for injury/transformation/age-up events).
- **Prospero project context moved out of the system prompt (Phase E).** The `## Project Context` block is no longer concatenated onto the per-turn system prompt. Project description and instructions now ride as Prospero-authored ASSISTANT messages in the chat transcript.
  - **Writer extended** at `lib/services/prospero-notifications/writer.ts` with `buildProjectContextContent` and `postProsperoProjectContextAnnouncement`. The body is persona-voiced ("Prospero opens his ledger to the project at hand…"); for opaque (`systemTransparency=false`) characters the `systemSender` attribution is stripped at context-build time but the body survives.
  - **At chat creation** (`createInitialMessages` in `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts`): when a project is attached and has description or instructions, Prospero posts a project-context whisper right after the SYSTEM message and before the Host announcements.
  - **Cadence-based refresh** (`lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts`): the previous per-turn `projectContext` injection has been replaced with a Prospero whisper post. When the message count is a non-zero multiple of `projectContextReinjectInterval` (default 5), a fresh whisper is posted into the transcript so the LLM keeps the project's particulars in mind. The just-posted whisper is pushed onto the in-memory `existingMessages` array so it is included in this turn's context.
  - **System-prompt block dropped.** `lib/chat/context/system-prompt-builder.ts` no longer renders the `## Project Context` / `### Project Instructions` block. The `projectContext` parameter on `buildSystemPrompt` is now unused (kept on the signature for Phase I cleanup) and the orchestrator passes `null` for it.
  - **Document store metadata added to the whisper.** The Prospero project-context whisper now lists every document store linked to the project — official store first, then alphabetical — with each store's display name, mount-point UUID, `mountType` (filesystem/obsidian/database), `storeType` (documents/character), and disabled flag. The body tells the LLM exactly which `mount_point` argument to pass to any `doc_*` tool and notes that `scope: "project"` addresses the official store directly. New `ProsperoDocumentStoreInfo` type and `loadProsperoProjectContext(projectId)` helper in `lib/services/prospero-notifications/writer.ts`; both call sites (`createInitialMessages` and the orchestrator cadence path) use the helper instead of fetching project fields manually. The whisper now fires whenever the project has any of: description, instructions, or ≥1 linked store (previously gated on description-or-instructions only) — so projects that exist solely for their document stores still get metadata pushed to the LLM.
