- **Librarian conversation summary moved out of the system prompt (Phase F).** The `## Previous Conversation Summary` block is no longer concatenated onto the per-turn system prompt. Whenever the cheap-LLM summarizer regenerates `chat.contextSummary`, the Librarian now deposits the fresh summary into the chat transcript as a synthetic ASSISTANT message, and the LLM picks it up from conversation history.
  - **Writer extended** at `lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts` with `buildSummaryContent` and `postLibrarianSummaryAnnouncement`.
  - **Wire-up** at `lib/chat/context-summary.ts`: after `repos.chats.update` writes the new summary and the existing `context-summary` event is appended, a Librarian summary whisper is posted with the same body. The chat-level `contextSummary` field is still maintained for other consumers (title generation, scene-state tracking, danger classification).
  - **System-prompt append dropped.** `lib/chat/context-manager.ts` no longer formats the chat's `contextSummary` via `formatSummaryForContext` and concatenates it onto `fullSystemContent`. The per-turn `summaryTokens` budget contribution is now zero.
  - **Deferred follow-ups** (still within Phase F's eventual scope): supersession of older Librarian summary whispers when a new one is posted (currently every regenerate adds a fresh whisper, leaving older ones in the transcript), and migrating `applyContextCompression` from the system-prompt prepend (`buildCompressedSystemMessage`) to a Librarian record-keeping whisper. Compression still ships its compressed history via the system prompt for now.
- **Timestamp moved out of the system prompt (Phase G).** When `timestampConfig.autoPrepend` is set and `shouldInjectTimestamp` returns true (`START_ONLY` + first user turn, or `EVERY_MESSAGE`), the Host now narrates the time as a transcript-resident ASSISTANT message ("The Host marks the time as …") instead of the auto-prepended `Current time: …` line that previously sat at the top of the per-turn system prompt.
  - **Writer extended** at `lib/services/host-notifications/writer.ts` with `buildTimestampContent` and `postHostTimestampAnnouncement`. Using the Host (rather than a `systemSender=null` neutral line as the original plan called for) avoids a salon-UI design call: the existing `getMessageAvatar` would have mis-attributed neutral messages to the first character. The Host's scene-setting role is a natural fit for narrating time. Revisit if a dedicated clock/timekeeper persona is wanted.
  - **Wired in** `lib/chat/context-manager.ts` right after the recent conversation messages are appended to `contextMessages` and before the new user message — the whisper is persisted into the transcript *and* pushed onto the in-memory `contextMessages` array so the LLM sees the timestamp on this turn (no one-turn lag).
  - **System-prompt block dropped.** `lib/chat/context/system-prompt-builder.ts` no longer renders the auto-prepend `Current time: …` line. The `{{timestamp}}` template-variable path is unchanged for character/template content that wants to inline the time directly.
- **Cleanup pass (Phase I).** With Phases A–G complete, the per-turn system-prompt builder no longer needs the parameters that fed the now-retired blocks. `lib/chat/context/system-prompt-builder.ts` `buildSystemPrompt` was converted from a 15-positional-parameter function to a single-options-object signature with only `character`, `userCharacter`, `roleplayTemplate`, `toolInstructions`, `selectedSystemPromptId`, `timestampConfig`, `isInitialMessage`, `timezone`, and `scenarioText`. The `WardrobeContext` and `ProjectContext` types and the `OtherParticipantInfo[]`, `respondingCharacterStatus`, `statusChangeNotifications`, `outfitChangeNotifications` parameters were dropped. Callers updated accordingly:
  - `lib/chat/context-manager.ts`: dropped the dead wardrobe-loading block (~45 lines of equipped-outfit lookups that fed the removed `wardrobeContext` parameter), the `projectContext` option on `BuildContextOptions`, and the `WardrobeContext` / `ProjectContext` re-exports.
  - `lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts`: dropped the `projectContext`, `statusChangeNotifications`, and `outfitChangeNotifications` options from `BuildMessageContextOptions` and the corresponding pass-through arguments to `buildContext`.
  - `lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts`: dropped the `projectContext: null` literal, the multi-character status-change-notifications projection (still computed for the `recordStatusChangeEvent` plumbing, not for the LLM), and the trailing comments referencing the now-retired surfaces.
  - `lib/tools/handlers/self-inventory-handler.ts`: updated `buildSystemPrompt` call site to the options-object form, dropping the `otherParticipants`, `projectContext`, `respondingCharacterStatus`, `wardrobeContext`, and `outfitChangeNotifications` arguments.
  - `__tests__/unit/context-management.test.ts`: updated `buildSystemPrompt` test calls to the options-object form.
  - `__tests__/unit/lib/services/chat-message-context.service.test.ts`: dropped the obsolete "should pass project context to buildContext" assertion (project context now flows via Prospero whispers, not the context-builder pipeline).
- **Phase H — precompiled identity stack.** Each chat now carries a per-participant cache of the character-static portion of the system prompt (`chats.compiledIdentityStacks`, JSON, keyed by participantId). The cached body — preamble + base prompt + personality + aliases + pronouns + physical descriptions + example dialogues, with `{{user}}` / `{{scenario}}` / `{{persona}}` resolved — feeds directly into the per-turn `buildSystemPrompt`, which wraps it with the chat-level roleplay template, tool instructions, and tool reinforcement. The LLM provider now sees a stable cache-friendly prefix across turns within a chat session.
  - **Schema** added at `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts` (`compiledIdentityStacks: JsonSchema.nullable().optional()`) on both `ChatMetadataSchema` and `ChatMetadataBaseSchema`. SQLite column added at `docs/developer/DDL.md` (chats table, `"compiledIdentityStacks" TEXT DEFAULT NULL`). Migration: `migrations/scripts/add-compiled-identity-stacks-field.ts` (id `add-compiled-identity-stacks-field-v1`), registered in `migrations/scripts/index.ts`. The field is excluded from `.qtap` exports — it's a derivable cache, and on import the read-through fallback in `buildSystemPrompt` rebuilds it on the first turn.
  - **New module** `lib/services/system-prompt-compiler/compiler.ts` exports `getCompiledIdentityStack`, `compileAllIdentityStacks`, and `compileIdentityStackForParticipant`. Errors never propagate — failures log and the read-through fallback covers them.
  - **Builder split.** `buildSystemPrompt` was refactored: a new `buildIdentityStack(options)` produces just the static portion, and `buildSystemPrompt` accepts an optional `precompiledIdentityStack` and uses it verbatim when supplied (the cache-hit path), otherwise calls `buildIdentityStack` (read-through fallback). The order of the per-turn additions was also adjusted so the static identity stack leads, with the dynamic roleplay template / tool instructions / tool reinforcement appended after it — this puts the stable bytes up front and the changing bytes at the end, maximizing provider prompt-cache hits.
  - **Compile triggers.** `compileAllIdentityStacks` runs in `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts` `handleCreate` after `repos.chats.create`. `compileIdentityStackForParticipant` runs in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts` (after `handleAddParticipant` succeeds in `processChatUpdates`, and after `selectedSystemPromptId` changes via `handleParticipantUpdate`) and in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/participants.ts` (after the action-dispatch add path and the soft-deleted reactivation path). On `controlledBy` flip (a participant becoming user-controlled or LLM-controlled) the whole map is recompiled because that affects `{{user}}` / `{{persona}}` for every other participant.
  - **Read path.** `lib/chat/context-manager.ts` looks up the cached stack for `respondingParticipant` via `getCompiledIdentityStack` and forwards it as `precompiledIdentityStack` to `buildSystemPrompt`. To make the cache lookup work for single-character chats too, the orchestrator → context-builder → context-manager pipeline now passes `respondingParticipant: characterParticipant` always (previously gated on `isMultiCharacter`).
  - **Known limitation.** Edits to the underlying character record (name, personality, aliases, pronouns, physical descriptions, example dialogues, `systemPrompts`) do NOT auto-invalidate cached stacks across chats — that fan-out is its own design pass. Until it lands, users editing a character mid-chat will keep seeing the stack from compile time. Workaround: read-through fallback ensures correctness when the cached entry is null/missing for a participant, so a future "rehydrate this chat" admin button can simply clear the map.
  - **Tests** added at `__tests__/unit/context-management.test.ts` covering the cache-hit path (precompiled stack used verbatim, character body NOT rebuilt), the cache-miss/fallback path (empty stack triggers fresh build), and the new ordering (identity stack → roleplay template → tool instructions → tool reinforcement).

### 4.3.1

#### Bug Fixes

- **SQLite journal mode default changed from WAL to TRUNCATE**: Quilltap data directories are commonly placed inside cloud-synced folders (iCloud Drive, Dropbox, OneDrive, Google Drive). WAL mode keeps `.db-wal` and `.db-shm` files alongside the main `.db`; if those files sync out of order with the main database — which all four providers can do, especially on dirty shutdown — the database can be corrupted or lose recent writes on the next open. Switching to `TRUNCATE` keeps the rollback journal in a single auxiliary file that is truncated to zero on every commit, eliminating the multi-file sync hazard. Existing databases auto-migrate on first open after upgrade (SQLite checkpoints any pre-existing WAL into the main file as part of the journal-mode transition). The change applies to all three databases — main (`quilltap.db`), LLM logs (`quilltap-llm-logs.db`), and mount index (`quilltap-mount-index.db`) — plus the meta-table connection used during startup.
- **`SQLITE_WAL_MODE` env var inverted**: Previously `SQLITE_WAL_MODE=false` was the opt-out; now `SQLITE_WAL_MODE=true` is the opt-in. Set this only when the data directory lives on a fast local SSD that is not synced to the cloud.
- **Internal**: `lib/startup/db-encryption-converter.ts` now leaves freshly-encrypted databases in TRUNCATE mode rather than WAL, matching the new resting state.

### 4.3.0

#### Refactors

- **Dead code cleanup — remove deprecated `attemptTokenLimitRecovery` alias and unexport internal `ToolCallRequest` type**: Removed the `@deprecated` `attemptTokenLimitRecovery` export alias in `lib/services/chat-message/recovery.service.ts` (never imported anywhere; `attemptRequestLimitRecovery` is the live function). Changed `ToolCallRequest` in `lib/tools/text-block-parser.ts` from `export interface` to a private interface since it is only used within that file. Updated `docs/developer/DEAD-CODE-REPORT.md` with full current knip findings (extensive new barrel re-exports from tool API growth since last report are all intentional).
- **Deep refactor — qt-* typography migration complete across all components**: Eliminated direct Tailwind heading/typography class usage (`text-xl font-semibold`, `text-2xl font-bold`, `text-lg font-semibold`, `text-sm font-medium`, `text-xs font-medium`, `text-lg font-medium`) across 54+ component files in `app/`, `components/`, replacing them with semantic `qt-*` equivalents (`qt-heading-2`, `qt-heading-3`, `qt-heading-4`, `qt-label`, `qt-text-label`, `qt-text-label-xs`, `qt-text-section`, `qt-page-title`). Also added `qt-heading-lg` and `qt-heading-sm` size-name aliases to `app/styles/qt-components/_content.css` to cover two components that were already referencing undefined classes. Updated `ErrorAlert` unit test to check for `qt-label` instead of the now-removed raw Tailwind classes.
- **DRY refactor — extract generic sub-array CRUD helpers in `CharactersRepository`**: The five groups of sub-entity operations (physical descriptions, clothing records, system prompts, scenarios — ~670 lines) each repeated the same load-character / find-item / mutate / save pattern. Extracted five private generic helpers (`addToSubArray`, `updateInSubArray`, `removeFromSubArray`, `getFromSubArray`, `getAllFromSubArray`). All 19 public method signatures are unchanged. Also removed trivial `addTag`/`removeTag` overrides that only called `super`, simplified `setFavorite`/`setControlledBy` to single-line delegations, replaced the hand-rolled UUID v4 in `AbstractBaseRepository.generateId()` with `crypto.randomUUID()`, and fixed one inconsistency in `UsersRepository` (`new Date().toISOString()` → `this.getCurrentTimestamp()`). Net: −181 lines with no behavior change.
- **DRY fix — extract `buildRequestContext` helper in `lib/api/middleware/auth.ts`**: The session-validation/user-lookup boilerplate was duplicated identically across all four exported context wrappers. Extracted into a single private `buildRequestContext()` function returning a discriminated union. No behavior change.
- **API routing standards are now enforced with a unit guardrail**: Added a route-convention test that scans `app/api/**/route.ts` and fails when handlers are outside `/api/v{version}/{entityname}`, except for the approved legacy paths (`/api/health`, `/api/plugin-routes/[...path]`, `/api/themes/*`). Also updated the release checklist wording in developer docs to match the enforced rule. (`__tests__/unit/api-route-versioning.test.ts`, `docs/developer/DEVELOPMENT.md`)
- **Mount-points API — move direct `fs` calls out of route handlers into `lib/mount-index/scanner.ts`**: Three route files were importing `fs/promises` directly and calling it at handler scope, violating the convention that only provider-layer modules touch the filesystem. Extracted `listFilesystemFolders` (recursive directory walk used when building the folder list for filesystem and obsidian mounts), `createFilesystemFolder` (path-traversal-guarded `mkdir`), and `verifyBasePath` (`access` probe returning a boolean) into `lib/mount-index/scanner.ts` as named exports. The three routes (`app/api/v1/mount-points/[id]/files/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/mount-points/[id]/folders/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/mount-points/route.ts`) now import and call those helpers instead of reaching for `fs` themselves; path-traversal guard logic and the escape-boundary check are preserved unchanged in the extracted functions. No behavior change.
- project-scenario integration in the new-chat dropdown**: New `ScenariosCard` component (`app/prospero/[id]/components/ScenariosCard.tsx`) renders alongside the existing Files / Document Stores / Settings / etc. cards on the project detail page. Lists every scenario with its name, filename, optional description, and a default-radio that calls the set-default endpoint; per-row buttons drive Edit (opens the new `ScenarioEditorModal`), Rename (inline prompt → POST?action=rename), and Delete (confirm → DELETE). New-scenario button opens the editor modal in create mode. Soft warnings from the API (e.g. multiple files marked default) surface as a banner above the list. New `ScenarioEditorModal` (`app/prospero/[id]/components/ScenarioEditorModal.tsx`) provides Name + Description + Default + Body fields, with the body wired to the reusable `MarkdownLexicalEditor` from PR 2. New `useProjectScenarios` hook (`app/prospero/[id]/hooks/useProjectScenarios.ts`) wraps the scenarios CRUD endpoints and keeps `scenarios + warnings` in sync after every mutation. Card-state hook (`useProjectCardState.ts`) gained a `scenarios` boolean so the Scenarios card respects the existing first-visit-expanded / subsequent-visits-collapsed pattern. — On the new-chat side, `useNewChat` now fetches `/api/v1/projects/[id]/scenarios` whenever a `projectId` is provided and exposes `projectScenarios: ProjectScenarioOption[]` on its return shape. The form state gained `projectScenarioPath: string | null`, seeded from the project default at mount; the request-body builder includes `projectScenarioPath` whenever no custom text or character `scenarioId` is set, matching the server precedence (`scenario > scenarioId > projectScenarioPath`). `NewChatForm.tsx` rewrote the scenario block as a single grouped `<select>` with two `<optgroup>` sections — "Project Scenarios" and "Character Scenarios" — plus the existing "Custom..." sentinel. Selecting an option clears the others (mutually exclusive). When the dropdown is currently using the project default and the LLM character also has a `defaultScenarioId`, an inline note renders the character's default name as a one-click switch button so the override is never silent. Both consumers of `useNewChat` (`app/salon/new/page.tsx` and `components/new-chat/NewChatModal.tsx`) thread the new `projectScenarios` prop through to `NewChatForm`. New `ProjectScenarioOption` type and `PROJECT_SCENARIO_PREFIX` constant in `components/new-chat/types.ts`. (`app/prospero/[id]/components/ScenariosCard.tsx`, `app/prospero/[id]/components/ScenarioEditorModal.tsx`, `app/prospero/[id]/components/index.ts`, `app/prospero/[id]/hooks/useProjectScenarios.ts`, `app/prospero/[id]/hooks/useProjectCardState.ts`, `app/prospero/[id]/hooks/index.ts`, `app/prospero/[id]/page.tsx`, `components/new-chat/types.ts`, `components/new-chat/hooks/useNewChat.ts`, `components/new-chat/NewChatForm.tsx`, `components/new-chat/NewChatModal.tsx`, `app/salon/new/page.tsx`)
- **Projects — REST CRUD for project scenarios under `/api/v1/projects/[id]/scenarios/...`**: New collection route at `app/api/v1/projects/[id]/scenarios/route.ts` exposes `GET` (list, with default-conflict warnings) and `POST` (create — body `{filename, name?, description?, isDefault?, body}`); both call the ensure helpers first so callers don't need a server restart to see the Scenarios folder. Item route at `app/api/v1/projects/[id]/scenarios/[scenarioPath]/route.ts` exposes `GET` (read), `PUT` (update — same body shape as create, no filename change), `POST?action=rename` (body `{newFilename}`, uses `moveDatabaseDocument`), and `DELETE` (uses `deleteDatabaseDocument`). The `[scenarioPath]` segment accepts the bare filename (with or without `.md`) for ergonomic URLs and prefixes `Scenarios/` server-side; `..` segments are rejected and nested paths under `Scenarios/` are forbidden (top-level only). Filenames are sanitized via the existing `sanitizeFileName` helper from `lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts`. Frontmatter is built via `serializeFrontmatter` from `lib/doc-edit/markdown-parser.ts` and includes only fields that have values — empty optionals don't leave noise in the YAML. When `isDefault: true` is set, `setProjectScenarioDefault` runs after the write to demote any sibling that was previously marked default. List/PUT/rename/delete all return the freshly listed `{scenarios, warnings}` so the client can avoid a follow-up GET. (`app/api/v1/projects/[id]/scenarios/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/projects/[id]/scenarios/[scenarioPath]/route.ts`)
- **Projects — server-side scenario plumbing: `Scenarios/` folder ensured per project, frontmatter-aware parser, chat creation accepts `projectScenarioPath`**: Three pieces ship together. (1) New `ensureProjectOfficialStore(projectId, projectName)` helper in `lib/mount-index/project-store-naming.ts` that finds-or-creates a project's `Project Files: <name>` store and writes its ID to `project.officialMountPointId`. Resolution order: existing FK if still valid → adopt an existing linked database-backed documents store via `pickPrimaryProjectStore` semantics → create a fresh store using `uniqueMountPointName` for collision handling. New `lib/mount-index/project-scenarios.ts` module (`PROJECT_SCENARIOS_FOLDER='Scenarios'`) provides `ensureProjectScenariosFolder`, `listProjectScenarios` (frontmatter-aware parsing — `name`, `description`, `isDefault`, sorted alphabetically with default-conflict resolution: alphabetical-first wins, surfaced soft warning naming offenders), `readProjectScenario`, `resolveProjectScenarioBody` (used by chat creation; accepts both `Scenarios/foo.md` and `foo` shorthand), and `setProjectScenarioDefault` (sequenced multi-file frontmatter rewrite via `updateFrontmatterInContent`). New startup module `lib/startup/ensure-project-scenarios.ts` iterates every project at boot to call both ensure helpers, wired as Phase 3.4 in `instrumentation.ts` between document mount-point scan and background schedulers. Project creation in `app/api/v1/projects/route.ts` POST calls the same ensure helpers inline so newly-created projects gain a store synchronously without waiting for a server restart. (2) `parseScenarioFile` in `lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts` now reads YAML frontmatter additively — `name` and `description` from frontmatter take precedence, falling back to the legacy first-`# heading` convention, then filename — so character vault `Scenarios/*.md` files keep working unchanged but can now opt into frontmatter for richer metadata. `CharacterScenarioSchema` in `lib/schemas/character.types.ts` gained an optional `description: z.string().max(500).optional()` field. (3) `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts` `createChatSchema` accepts a new `projectScenarioPath?: string` parameter; resolution chain extended to `scenario > scenarioId > projectScenarioPath`, where the project path is read from `project.officialMountPointId` via `resolveProjectScenarioBody`, parsed for frontmatter, and the body baked into `chat.scenarioText` exactly like the other paths. `processCharacterTemplates` already runs on `scenarioText` in `buildSystemPrompt`, so `{{char}}`/`{{user}}` substitution happens for free with no new wiring. Snapshot-on-create means chats survive later edits/renames/deletes of the source scenario file. (`lib/mount-index/project-store-naming.ts`, `lib/mount-index/project-scenarios.ts`, `lib/startup/ensure-project-scenarios.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `lib/schemas/character.types.ts`, `instrumentation.ts`, `app/api/v1/projects/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts`)
- **Editors — extracted `MarkdownLexicalEditor` as a reusable Lexical-based markdown editor**: Self-contained component (`components/markdown-editor/MarkdownLexicalEditor.tsx`) that wraps a LexicalComposer with the standard plugin set (RichTextPlugin, HistoryPlugin, ListPlugin, CheckListPlugin, TablePlugin, MarkdownShortcutPlugin) plus the existing `MarkdownBridgePlugin`/`FormattingCommandPlugin` and the `FormattingToolbar`, exposed via a clean `{value, onChange, disabled, roleplayTemplateId, remountKey}` props surface. Designed for forms (project scenarios, future settings panels) that need the same markdown editing affordances Document Mode provides without inheriting its chat-mode-specific integrations (line gutter, doc_focus tool plugin, source-mode toggle, scroll restoration). DocumentPane retains its own implementation; refactoring it to consume this component is a larger change deferred until there's a second consumer that needs the specialized integrations. (`components/markdown-editor/MarkdownLexicalEditor.tsx`)
- **Projects — added `officialMountPointId` column on `projects` and a backfill migration; replaces the `Project Files:` name-prefix heuristic with a real foreign key to the project's canonical document store**: New nullable TEXT column on the `projects` SQLite table, added by migration `add-project-official-mount-point-v1`, which then iterates every project and writes the matching mount point ID by joining `project_doc_mount_links` to `doc_mount_points`, preferring database-backed `documents` stores whose name starts with the `Project Files:` prefix (matching `isProjectOwnStoreName`) and falling back to the first eligible store, mirroring `pickPrimaryProjectStore`. Projects with no eligible store get `officialMountPointId = null` and a follow-up startup hook + project-creation hook (introduced separately) will create one. Migration depends on `convert-project-files-to-document-stores-v1` so the source mount points exist; idempotent — reruns skip projects that already have the FK populated. Schema field added as `UUIDSchema.nullable().optional()` on `ProjectSchema`. Import path strips `officialMountPointId` from incoming `.qtap` payloads since mount-point IDs from a source instance won't be valid in the destination — the destination's startup hook backfills it. Export schema (`public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`) and `docs/developer/DDL.md` updated. (`lib/schemas/project.types.ts`, `migrations/scripts/add-project-official-mount-point.ts`, `migrations/scripts/index.ts`, `lib/import/quilltap-import-service.ts`, `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`, `docs/developer/DDL.md`)
- **Tools — retired the file-write permission infrastructure that served the removed `file_management` tool**: Follow-up orphan cleanup after the `file_management` removal below. With that tool gone nothing grants or consumes file-write permissions anymore, so the whole approval flow (DB table, repository, schema, backup/restore plumbing, API route, UI prompt/modal, salon hook state) has been removed. Deleted `lib/database/repositories/file-permissions.repository.ts`, `lib/schemas/file-permissions.types.ts`, `app/api/v1/files/write-permissions/` (the entire route directory with `complete`/`revoke` actions), `app/api/v1/files/actions/write.ts` (the `/api/v1/files?action=write` handler, callable only by the departed tool), `components/chat/FileWritePermissionPrompt.tsx`, and `components/chat/FileWriteApprovalModal.tsx`. Scrubbed references from the repository container (`lib/database/repositories/index.ts`), `lib/schemas/types.ts` re-exports, `app/api/v1/files/shared.ts` (removed `writeFileSchema`, `ensureFileWritePermission`, `'write'` from `FILE_POST_ACTIONS`), `app/api/v1/files/handlers/post.ts`, `app/api/v1/files/actions/index.ts`, `app/api/v1/files/route.ts` docblock, `lib/backup/types.ts` (removed `filePermissions` from `BackupData`/`BackupManifest`/`RestoreSummary`), `lib/backup/backup-service.ts` (removed the `findByUserId` fetch and the `file-permissions.json` stage write), `lib/backup/restore-service.ts` (removed the parse/remap/delete/restore branches), `lib/tools/capabilities-report.ts` (dropped the `filePermissions` stat and its markdown table row), `scripts/migrate-to-single-user.ts`, and `app/salon/[id]/` (removed `FileWriteApprovalState` from `useModalState`, the `requiresPermission`/`pendingWrite` branch from `useSSEStreaming`, and the component renders from `ChatModals.tsx` and `VirtualizedMessageList.tsx`). New migration `drop-file-permissions-v1` drops the `file_permissions` SQLite table, mirroring the `drop-mount-points-v1` pattern; `docs/developer/DDL.md` no longer documents the table. Stale developer doc `docs/developer/FILE_LLM_ACCESS.md` deleted and its entry in `.claude/commands/update-documentation.md` removed. Test fixture at `__tests__/unit/app/api/v1/files/handlers/post.test.ts` pared down to its remaining "unknown action rejected" case. (`lib/database/repositories/index.ts`, `lib/schemas/types.ts`, `lib/backup/types.ts`, `lib/backup/backup-service.ts`, `lib/backup/restore-service.ts`, `lib/tools/capabilities-report.ts`, `scripts/migrate-to-single-user.ts`, `migrations/scripts/drop-file-permissions.ts`, `migrations/scripts/index.ts`, `app/api/v1/files/shared.ts`, `app/api/v1/files/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/files/handlers/post.ts`, `app/api/v1/files/actions/index.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useModalState.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useSSEStreaming.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/index.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/components/ChatModals.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/components/VirtualizedMessageList.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `docs/developer/DDL.md`, `.claude/commands/update-documentation.md`)
- **Tools — removed the `file_management` LLM tool and three redundant `project_info` actions**: The Scriptorium document tools (`doc_list_files`, `doc_read_file`, `doc_grep`, `doc_write_file`, `doc_str_replace`, etc.) have covered every workflow the `file_management` tool used to serve, so the older tool has been retired. Deleted `lib/tools/file-management-tool.ts` and `lib/tools/handlers/file-management-handler.ts` outright; disconnected it from `lib/chat/tool-executor.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/tool-execution.service.ts` (removed the `requiresPermission` / `pendingWrite` branch), `lib/tools/plugin-tool-builder.ts`, `lib/tools/text-block-parser.ts`, `lib/tools/text-block-prompt.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/pseudo-tool.service.ts`, `app/api/v1/tools/route.ts` (both `BUILT_IN_TOOL_SCHEMAS` and the `BUILT_IN_TOOLS` list), `components/chat/ToolMessage.tsx`, and `packages/plugin-utils/src/builtin-tools.ts` (bumped to `2.2.4` — requires `npm publish`). Also pruned `list_files`, `read_file`, and `search_files` from `project_info`; the tool now exposes only `get_info` (project overview, character roster, counts, linked Scriptorium store) and `get_instructions` (full project instructions). Updated tests in `__tests__/unit/tools-api.test.ts`, `__tests__/unit/builtin-tools.test.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/services/chat-message/pseudo-tool.service.test.ts`, `lib/tools/__tests__/text-block-prompt.test.ts`, and `__tests__/unit/components/chat/ToolMessage.test.tsx` (switched example payload from `file_management` to `doc_write_file`). The file-write permission infrastructure (`app/api/v1/files/write-permissions/route.ts` `complete` action, `FileWritePermissionPrompt`, `FileWriteApprovalModal`, the salon's `fileWriteApprovalState`) is now orphaned — left in place for a follow-up cleanup.
- **Scriptorium / Aurora — post-Librarian code cleanup**: Removed dead code and fixed several issues introduced in the refactor since commit `0e13b2f`:
  - `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts`: Removed local `getErrorMessage` function that duplicated the one exported from `@/lib/errors` — replaced with an import.
  - `app/aurora/[id]/edit/components/CharacterBasicInfo.tsx`: The `overlayManagedDisabled = false` constant was always `false` (vault-managed fields intentionally stay editable), so all `disabled={overlayManagedDisabled}` props and `{!overlayManagedDisabled && …}` guards were dead code. Removed the constant and unwrapped/simplified all callsites. `Add First Scenario` empty-state button now uses `[...formData.scenarios, newScenario]` for consistency with the header button.
  - `app/scriptorium/[id]/components/FileTable.tsx`: (1) Extracted `isBlobBacked(fileType)` helper to remove a three-way type-equality check repeated in three places. (2) Merged two consecutive `if` blocks in `toggleExpand` (one for `'blob'` and one for `'pdf' | 'docx'`) into a single call guarded by the helper. (3) Changed `<>` keyless fragments wrapping `<tr>` pairs to `<Fragment key={file.id}>` so React has a stable root key for each mapped row. (4) `FileDetailRow` is now keyed by `blob?.updatedAt ?? 'loading'` so its local `description` state resets when blob metadata loads rather than staying frozen at its empty-string initial value. (5) `loadBlobDetail` had `blobDetails` in its `useCallback` dependency array, causing the callback (and `toggleExpand` which depends on it) to re-create on every blob load — replaced with `blobFetchedRef` (`useRef(new Set<string>())`) so the already-fetched guard is a stable ref; the ID is added before the first `await` to prevent duplicate concurrent requests. (6) Renamed `uploadError` state to `operationError` since it is also set by delete and description-save failures.

#### Fixes

- **Scriptorium — `doc_read_file`, `doc_write_file`, `doc_str_replace`, and `doc_copy_file` no longer reject every existing file as a boundary escape when the data directory lives behind a symlink**: `lib/doc-edit/path-resolver.ts` was realpathing the *file* path (which expands symlinks) but comparing it against an unresolved `baseDir` (which does not), so on macOS instances rooted at `~/iCloud` (a symlink to `~/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs`) the containment check rejected every file that actually existed on disk with `Path escapes project boundary` / `Path escapes general storage boundary` / `Path escapes mount point boundary`. New files (writes to a not-yet-created path) slipped through because both sides fell back to `path.resolve` without expansion. `safeRealpath` now walks up to the deepest existing ancestor, realpaths it, and re-attaches the missing tail — so a write to a brand-new file resolves consistently with its parent. `resolveProjectPath`, `resolveGeneralPath`, and the filesystem branch of `resolveDocumentStorePath` now realpath both `baseDir` and the joined path before the boundary check, and the returned `basePath` is the realpath'd value. The traversal protections (rejecting `..` segments and absolute paths) still run up front and are unchanged. New regression suite at `__tests__/unit/lib/doc-edit/path-resolver.test.ts` builds a real symlinked tmp tree and asserts that an existing project file with a space in its folder name resolves correctly, that a not-yet-created project file resolves without a boundary error, that `..` and absolute paths are still rejected, and that the same fix applies to general scope. (`lib/doc-edit/path-resolver.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/doc-edit/path-resolver.test.ts`)

- **Imported characters now get a vault provisioned during the import**: Characters created via `executeImport` in `lib/import/quilltap-import-service.ts` (the path used by Aurora's "Summon from Lore" wizard, regular `.qtap` imports, and the seed-data import) were not having a character vault provisioned. The only callers of `provisionVaultInBackground` lived in the `POST /api/v1/characters` route handler, so import-created characters had no `characterDocumentMountPointId` until the next server restart, when `backfillCharacterVaults` would sweep them up. During that gap, the Scriptorium and any vault-aware tooling could not see them. `importCharacters` now awaits a new `provisionImportedCharacterVault` helper after each `repos.characters.create` call (both the duplicate path and the normal/overwrite path). Vault-provisioning failures are recorded as import warnings instead of aborting the import; the startup backfill remains the safety net since `ensureCharacterVault` is idempotent. (`lib/import/quilltap-import-service.ts`)

- **Initial-greeting LLM call now writes to `llm_logs`**: `generateGreetingMessage` in `lib/chat/initial-greeting.ts` had been calling `providerClient.streamMessage` directly with no `logLLMCall` wrapper, so the LLM call that produces a chat's auto-generated opening message never showed up in the LLM Logs view (and was invisible to token/cost tracking). The function now accepts optional `userId`/`chatId`/`characterId` from the caller, wraps the stream loop in try/finally, and writes one `llm_logs` row per attempt with type `CHAT_MESSAGE` — including stream errors and any partially-accumulated content. Each of the four retry attempts in `autoGenerateFirstMessage` (full context, no-memories, Concierge uncensored fallback, plain retry) now logs its own row. Logging failures are caught and warned; they never break greeting generation. (`lib/chat/initial-greeting.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts`)

- **Backup — character plugin data, conversation annotations, and user-installed themes were not backed up**: The ZIP backup system was missing three categories of user data. `character_plugin_data` rows (per-character plugin metadata such as Commonplace Book entries) were not collected or restored. `conversation_annotations` rows (per-message annotations added during roleplay via the Scriptorium annotation tools) were excluded. User-installed theme bundles (directories in `<data-dir>/themes/`, installed from registries or manually) were not copied into or out of backup archives. All three are now included: JSON data files `data/character-plugin-data.json` and `data/conversation-annotations.json` are written during backup and parsed (with backward-compatible fallback) during restore; a `themes/` directory mirrors `<data-dir>/themes/` (excluding `.cache/`) in the backup archive and is restored over the existing themes directory. UUID remapping in new-account mode correctly remaps `characterId` on plugin data records and `chatId`/`sourceMessageId` on annotation records. Manifest counts updated with `characterPluginData`, `conversationAnnotations`, and `userInstalledThemes` fields. (`lib/backup/backup-service.ts`, `lib/backup/restore-service.ts`, `lib/backup/types.ts`, `docs/BACKUP-RESTORE.md`, `help/system-backup-restore.md`)

- **Regression tests for recent bug fixes**: Added unit tests to lock down the five bugs fixed in the current dev cycle. New file `__tests__/unit/lib/repositories/folders-path-rename.test.ts` (10 tests) covers `FoldersRepository.updatePathPrefix` (renames the folder itself and all descendants via JS-side `startsWith`, returns correct count, ignores unrelated folders, handles null `projectId`), `findDescendants`, and `FilesRepository.findInFolderRecursive` — the methods that were broken by the anchored `$regex` bug. `__tests__/unit/lib/database/query-translator.test.ts` gained 6 tests for the new `$like` operator (pass-through, no wrapping, `$and` interaction) and a documentation test confirming `$regex` does not support anchors. `__tests__/unit/lib/backup/backup-parser.test.ts` gained 5 tests confirming `parseBackupZip` reads `character-plugin-data.json` and `conversation-annotations.json` when present and gracefully returns `[]` for both when absent. `__tests__/unit/context-management.test.ts` gained 1 test confirming `formatSummaryForContext` successfully truncates an oversized summary (guarding against the dynamic-`require` TypeError). New file `__tests__/unit/lib/services/chat-message/agent-mode-guardrail.test.ts` (10 tests) covers `buildAgentModeInstructions` instruction text and the ghost-wrap-up detection condition (6 cases). (`__tests__/unit/lib/repositories/folders-path-rename.test.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/database/query-translator.test.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/backup/backup-parser.test.ts`, `__tests__/unit/context-management.test.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/services/chat-message/agent-mode-guardrail.test.ts`)

- **Plugin package hygiene — `@quilltap/plugin-types` now explicitly declared in all plugins that use it**: Six plugins (`qtap-plugin-anthropic`, `qtap-plugin-google`, `qtap-plugin-grok`, `qtap-plugin-ollama`, `qtap-plugin-openai`, `qtap-plugin-openrouter`) imported `@quilltap/plugin-types` types without listing it in their own `package.json`, relying on the transitive `plugin-utils → plugin-types` chain. Added `"@quilltap/plugin-types": "^2.3.0"` to each plugin's `dependencies` so that external plugin developers following these as reference implementations see a correct, self-contained dependency declaration. No runtime behavior change — all imports were `import type` (erased at compile time). (`plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-anthropic/package.json`, `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-google/package.json`, `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-grok/package.json`, `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-ollama/package.json`, `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openai/package.json`, `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openrouter/package.json`)

- **qt-* compliance pass on all new UI components since 4.3-dev start**: Updated `qt-page-title` CSS to match the established `text-3xl font-semibold leading-tight` pattern used across all page `<h1>` headings (the previous definition `text-2xl font-bold tracking-tight` was never applied anywhere). Applied `qt-page-title`, `qt-section-title`, `qt-label`, `qt-body`, `qt-body-sm`, `qt-dialog-title`, and `qt-action` in place of raw Tailwind typography classes in: `app/scriptorium/page.tsx`, `app/scriptorium/[id]/page.tsx`, `app/scriptorium/[id]/components/FileTable.tsx`, `app/scriptorium/components/DocumentStoreCard.tsx`, `app/scriptorium/components/CreateDocumentStoreDialog.tsx`, `app/scriptorium/components/EditDocumentStoreDialog.tsx`, `app/prospero/[id]/components/ScenariosCard.tsx`, `app/prospero/[id]/components/DocumentStoresCard.tsx`, `components/new-chat/CharacterPickerPanel.tsx`, `components/new-chat/NewChatForm.tsx`, `components/new-chat/NewChatModal.tsx`. (`app/styles/qt-components/_typography.css`)

- **Aurora — vault-only wardrobe items no longer disappear when an LLM creates new ones**: When a character has the document-store overlay on, dropping a `Wardrobe/<title>.md` file into the vault (via Document Mode or by hand) creates a "vault-only" wardrobe item — the read overlay surfaces it with a deterministic UUID derived from the file path, but no row exists in the `wardrobe_items` table. Observed on Friday, chat `9de8d63d-895b-452c-a423-a087c842ae26`: the user authored `Wardrobe/Dressing Gown.md` for Gary, equipped it (now possible via the recent `findByIdForCharacter` fix), then asked Friday to dress him; the LLM called `create_wardrobe_item` four times for new items and the dressing gown vanished. Cause: `WardrobeRepository.create` triggers `syncCharacterVaultWardrobe`, which calls `projectArrayIntoVaultFolder` to project the DB items into `Wardrobe/`. The projection sweep deletes any file whose path isn't in the DB-derived list, so vault-only files (with no DB row) get wiped on every wardrobe write. Same hole on `update`/`archive`/`unarchive`/`delete`, and on the symmetric outfit-presets path. Fix: `performVaultWardrobeSync` now runs a new `ingestVaultOnlyWardrobeIntoDb` step before projecting, which reads the vault snapshot, finds items/presets whose IDs aren't yet in the DB, and inserts them with `WardrobeRepository.createFromVault` / `OutfitPresetsRepository.createFromVault` — both new public methods that wrap `_create` with explicit `id`/`createdAt`/`updatedAt` and skip the post-write sync trigger to avoid recursion. The DB row picks up the same deterministic UUID the read overlay was already returning, so the equip handler's `equippedOutfit` reference stays valid across the sync. The two new methods are scoped to vault-ingestion and don't change the outward surface of `create()`. Per-item failures in the ingestion loop log a warning and continue — losing one item to a validation error is better than aborting the sync and clobbering the whole vault on the projection step. Existing already-deleted vault files in chats hit by this bug aren't restored automatically; recreate the file in Document Mode and the next sync will preserve it. New regression tests in `__tests__/unit/lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.test.ts` cover the vault-only-survives-sync path and the no-op-when-already-in-DB path. (`lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/wardrobe.repository.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/outfit-presets.repository.ts`)
- **Salon — opening a missing document now shows a toast instead of the dev error overlay**: Clicking a Document Mode entry whose underlying file no longer exists used to throw inside `useDocumentMode.openDocument` and surface a Next.js red-screen "Console Error" overlay reading `{"error":"File not found: <path>"}` (observed when Friday's `Wardrobe/Dressing Gown.md` got swept by the now-fixed projection bug). Two changes. (1) `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts` returns 404 instead of 400 for the missing-file case in `open-document`, and uses `errorResponse(message, 404)` for the `read-document` ENOENT branch as well — `notFound()` would have appended " not found" producing the awkward "File not found: X not found". (2) `useDocumentMode.openDocument` now catches the failure, formats a friendly single-line message via a new `friendlyOpenDocumentError` helper (parses the JSON server response, recognizes `"File not found"`, falls back to the raw text), shows it via `showErrorToast`, and logs the raw error with `console.warn` so it doesn't trip Next's dev-overlay-on-`console.error` behavior. (`app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useDocumentMode.ts`)
- **Prospero — `update_outfit_item` tool now resolves vault-only wardrobe items**: The sibling fix to the salon equip-handler bug. `lib/tools/handlers/wardrobe-update-outfit-handler.ts` had four raw `repos.wardrobe.findById` calls that bypassed the document-store overlay: the preset archived-item check (line 127), the preset-application loop (line 150), the by-ID equip lookup (line 208), and the coverage-summary helper (line 457). When an LLM called `update_outfit_item` with `item_id` for a vault-resident item — or applied a preset whose slots referenced vault items — the lookup returned null and the tool either threw "Wardrobe item not found" or silently fell back to `updateEquippedSlot` without displacement, leaving stale slots behind. All four call sites now use `findByIdForCharacter(characterId, id)` (added in the prior salon-equip fix), which routes through the overlay and falls back to archetype lookups for shared items. `buildCoverageSummaryFromState` gained a `characterId` parameter so its per-slot lookups can join the overlay path; the three caller sites pass `context.characterId` through. The redundant ownership check that ran after the by-ID lookup (`item.characterId != null && item.characterId !== context.characterId`) was unreachable post-fix — `findByIdForCharacter` only returns items owned by this character or archetypes (characterId null) — and was removed. New regression test in `__tests__/unit/lib/tools/handlers/wardrobe-handlers.test.ts` exercises the vault-only equip path with `findById` mocked to null and verifies the tool succeeds via `findByIdForCharacter`. (`lib/tools/handlers/wardrobe-update-outfit-handler.ts`)
- **Salon — equipping a vault-only wardrobe item from the chat UI no longer 404s**: `WardrobeRepository.findById` and `findByIds` go straight to the `wardrobe_items` table and don't consult the document-store overlay, so items that exist only as `Wardrobe/<title>.md` files in a character vault (their UUIDs are derived from path, not stored in the DB) couldn't be resolved. The salon's `useOutfit` hook listed them via `findByCharacterId` (overlay-aware), but `POST /api/v1/chats/[id]?action=equip` validated incoming IDs with the raw `findById` and returned 404 — observed on Friday, chat `9de8d63d-895b-452c-a423-a087c842ae26`, character Gary, item `c52b1e29-6a6b-84a6-8084-d5b1d0bf4d7d`. The displacement helpers had the same blind spot: `equipWithDisplacement`/`unequipWithDisplacement` used `findById` to look up the item being displaced, so swapping out a vault-resident dress (`types: ['top', 'bottom']`) for another vault item left the bottom slot stuck. Added `WardrobeRepository.findByIdForCharacter(characterId, id)` and `findByIdsForCharacter(characterId, ids)` that go through `getOverlaidWardrobeItems` and fall back to a raw lookup for archetypes (characterId null) so shared items remain reachable. Updated the equip handler (both the initial validation and the outfit-change notification's title lookup) and the displacement helpers' `DisplacementRepos` interface to use the new methods; `findById`/`findByIds` themselves stay raw-DB for export and vault-populator paths that need the canonical row. Existing displacement tests updated for the new mock shape; new regression test in `__tests__/unit/app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/outfit.test.ts` covers the vault-only ID round-trip. The LLM-side `update_outfit_item` tool handler in `lib/tools/handlers/wardrobe-update-outfit-handler.ts` still calls `findById` directly at four sites and is a sibling bug not covered here. (`lib/database/repositories/wardrobe.repository.ts`, `lib/wardrobe/outfit-displacement.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/outfit.ts`)
- **Salon — Host now announces participant adds and removes that come through the consolidated PUT chat-update endpoint**: The Add Character dialog calls `PUT /api/v1/chats/{id}?action=add-participant` with `{ addParticipant: {...} }`, but `add-participant` (and `remove-participant`) are only registered on the POST action dispatch in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/post.ts`. PUT requests with those action params fell through to `handlePut` → `processChatUpdates` in `helpers.ts`, which called the lower-level `handleAddParticipant` / `handleRemoveParticipant` helpers directly and never fired `postHostAddAnnouncement` / `postHostRemoveAnnouncement` — so a character could join the chat with no Host message in the transcript (observed on Friday, chat `9de8d63d-895b-452c-a423-a087c842ae26`: Gary added at 21:38:15.701Z, only `[Chats v1] Chat updated` logged, no host-notifications activity). `processChatUpdates` now mirrors the POST handlers: the `addParticipant` branch resolves the just-added character via `repos.characters.findById(validatedData.addParticipant.characterId)` and posts the add announcement; the `removeParticipantId` branch resolves the participant's character name *before* the remove (since the row is gone afterward) and posts the remove announcement only when the character lookup succeeded. Status-change announcements via PUT were already covered because `handleParticipantUpdate` itself fires them regardless of which caller invokes it. (`app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts`)
- **Chat streaming — `truncateToTokenLimit is not a function` no longer crashes turns when the previous-conversation summary is oversized**: `formatSummaryForContext` in `lib/chat/context/memory-injector.ts` used a lazy `require('@/lib/tokens/token-counter')` inside the truncation branch. In the Next.js webpack ESM dev bundle the dynamic `require` on a `@/`-aliased path didn't surface the module's named exports, so `truncateToTokenLimit` came back `undefined` and the `TypeError` propagated up through `buildContext` → `buildMessageContext` → `processMessage` (observed on Friday, chat `c4b7db4a-0b4a-4a68-b9ef-fee817dcd1f8`, at `TurnOrchestrator` chain depths 2 and 4 — only triggered when a chat had accumulated enough summary text to exceed the available summary budget, which is why it showed up mid-conversation rather than at startup). Replaced with a static top-of-file `import { estimateTokens, truncateToTokenLimit } from '@/lib/tokens/token-counter'`; no circular-dependency reason existed to defer the import. The other two `require('@/...')` callsites in the repo (`lib/database/backends/sqlite/backend.ts` for `startup-state` and `lib/startup/version-guard.ts` for `migrations/lib/database-utils`) are startup/migration boundary cases deliberately structured that way and remain untouched. (`lib/chat/context/memory-injector.ts`)
- **Folder rename — descendant folder rows now follow the parent**: `FoldersRepository.updatePathPrefix` (`lib/database/repositories/folders.repository.ts:293`), called by the `rename-folder` action in `app/api/v1/files/folders/route.ts:323`, used an anchored `^prefix` `$regex` to pick up descendant folder rows. The SQLite `$regex` translator (`lib/database/backends/sqlite/query-translator.ts`) cannot express anchored matches — it only rewrites `.*` → `%` / `.` → `_` and wraps the pattern in `%…%`, so the `^` and the `escapeRegex` backslashes passed through as literal LIKE characters and the query always matched zero rows. Net effect on the rename endpoint: the renamed folder's own row was updated (that edit goes through a direct `folders.update` on the resolved ID just above the `updatePathPrefix` call), and every file's `folderPath` was rewritten (the route does that itself via a `findByProjectId`/`findGeneralFiles` fetch + JS filter at lines 331–346), but the descendant *folder* rows were never touched — so the `folders` table accumulated stale paths pointing at the pre-rename tree even though the files underneath them had already moved. `updatePathPrefix` now fetches via `findAllInProject` and filters with `path.startsWith(oldPathPrefix)` in JS, mirroring the file-side code that already sat beside it. Two sibling methods on the same failure mode — `findDescendants` on folders and `findInFolderRecursive` on files — had no callers in the app but carried the same broken query; both are now rewritten to the same fetch-all + `startsWith` shape so they don't quietly match nothing if a future caller reaches for them. The query translator itself isn't touched; the earlier `$like` operator is reserved for the mount-index folder enumeration where it gets paired with `$in` for a meaningful SQL narrow. (`lib/database/repositories/folders.repository.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/files.repository.ts`)
- **Aurora / Scriptorium — vault-backed `Prompts/*.md` and `Scenarios/*.md` now actually load and rewrite**: The character-properties overlay's folder-listing query (`findManyByMountPointsInFolder` in `lib/database/repositories/doc-mount-documents.repository.ts`) used an anchored `$regex` pattern — `^Prompts/[^/]+\.md$` — against the SQLite backend. The translator's `$regex` case (`lib/database/backends/sqlite/query-translator.ts`) only rewrites `.*` → `%` and `.` → `_` and wraps the whole pattern in `%…%`, so regex anchors (`^`, `$`) and character classes (`[^/]+`) passed through as literal LIKE characters and the query matched nothing. Two downstream symptoms on vault-mode characters: (1) the read overlay reported `promptsFolderMountCount: 0` / `scenariosFolderMountCount: 0` in the logs and skipped the `systemPrompts` / `scenarios` overlay at `character-properties-overlay.ts:608`/`:638`, so character pages and new-chat prompt-picker menus kept showing the stale pre-vault DB column instead of the current vault files — on Friday, Amy's renamed "Free Agent" → "Amy" prompt was invisible; (2) `projectArrayIntoVaultFolder` (same file, line 1424) uses the same function to enumerate existing vault files before deciding what to delete, so the write path wrote new files but never deleted the old ones — the vault accumulated stale `.md` entries (Free Agent.md hung around next to Amy.md). The sync-back-from-vault action also reported `syncedSystemPromptCount: 0` for the same reason, so the DB column couldn't even be refreshed from a corrected vault. Fix adds a `$like` operator to the query translator that emits `LIKE ?` without the substring wrap (caller supplies wildcards; no regex rewriting), declared on `ComparisonCondition` and `ComparisonOperator` in `lib/database/interfaces.ts` — then rewires `findManyByMountPointsInFolder` to fetch with a prefix `$like: 'Prompts/%'` and narrow the result set in JS (`startsWith(prefix)`, top-level only via absence of `/` after the prefix, extension match). No other callers to change — the fix propagates automatically to the overlay read path, the sync-back action, and the write-path projection. Existing `$regex` usages (memories search, folders/files path-prefix lookups, chat message search) are untouched; each of those has its own semantics and a couple may have analogous bugs but are out of scope here. After the fix, the next write to a vault-mode character's prompts/scenarios will naturally re-project the folder and clean up any stragglers. (`lib/database/backends/sqlite/query-translator.ts`, `lib/database/interfaces.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/doc-mount-documents.repository.ts`)
- **Lantern and Aurora image announcements now quote the prompt they were aiming for**: The synthetic chat messages posted after a story-background or character-avatar regeneration used to say only "The Lantern has projected a new backdrop behind the proceedings" or "Aurora has refreshed the portrait filed under *X*'s name" — no indication of what the system was actually trying to produce, which left characters (and the human reader) guessing whether the new image matched intent. The image's generation prompt is already persisted on the `files` row (`generationPrompt` column, set by `lib/background-jobs/handlers/character-avatar.ts` and `lib/background-jobs/handlers/story-background.ts` at file-creation time), so `postLanternImageNotification` in `lib/services/lantern-notifications/writer.ts` now fetches the file by ID before composing the announcement and passes the prompt into `buildContent`. When present, avatar announcements read "*...aiming for: \"{prompt}\". The previous likeness is retired with due ceremony; the new one is attached here, should anyone care to take a fresh look.*" and background announcements read "*The Lantern has projected a new backdrop behind the proceedings, aiming for: \"{prompt}\". The resulting image hangs just above, attached for your perusal.*" When the prompt is missing (older files, rare race, or lookup failure) the message falls back to the original prompt-less wording — the fetch is wrapped in its own try/catch that logs at `debug` and never disturbs the announcement itself. The `character-image` kind (the `generate_image` tool path) is intentionally left alone: the requesting character already supplied the description explicitly in-chat, so repeating it back adds noise. Three new unit tests cover the new prompt-bearing and fallback shapes for both avatar and background kinds. (`lib/services/lantern-notifications/writer.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lantern-notifications-writer.test.ts`)
- **Document Mode — renaming the file in the editor title now actually renames the file, and the Librarian announces it in the chat**: `DocumentPane` at `app/salon/[id]/components/DocumentPane.tsx` has click-to-edit title logic that fires `onTitleChange(newTitle)` on Enter/blur, but the parent `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx` never passed that prop, so the `handleTitleSubmit` condition (`editTitle.trim() && editTitle !== document.displayTitle && onTitleChange`) short-circuited and the submit was a silent no-op. The input closed, the span re-rendered `document.displayTitle` from the unchanged prop, and the name "reset back to what it was" — same failure whether the active document lived in a filesystem-backed document store, a project, or a database-backed character vault. The backend had no endpoint to rename a Document Mode document either: `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts` carried `open`/`close`/`read`/`write`/`active`/`recent` but no rename action. New `rename-document` action takes a `newTitle` string, treats it as the new basename with the old directory preserved, appends the old extension if the user didn't supply one ("backstory" becomes "backstory.md"), rejects path separators and `..` segments, dispatches on `mountType` — `moveDatabaseDocument` from `lib/mount-index/database-store.ts` for database-backed stores, `fs.rename` for filesystem — refuses to overwrite an existing destination (409 for both backends, via `DatabaseStoreError.code === 'CONFLICT'` or a pre-`fs.rename` `fs.access` check), triggers a background re-index via `scheduleDocumentStoreRefresh` when a filesystem document-store file moves, and updates the `chat_documents` row's `filePath` + `displayTitle` so the UI and future opens see the new name. A matching Librarian announcement — fourth kind alongside `opened-by-user`, `opened-by-character`, and `saved` — is posted into the chat on success so characters present on the floor know the volume has been rechristened and the new path it answers to; `lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts` gained `LibrarianRenameAnnouncement`, `buildRenameContent`, and `postLibrarianRenameAnnouncement` following the same never-propagate error semantics as the open/save writers. Client-side: a new `renameDocumentForChat` helper in `app/salon/[id]/hooks/documentModeApi.ts`, a `renameDocument` callback exposed by `useDocumentMode.ts` that flushes any pending autosave before calling the endpoint (so a rename doesn't lose an in-flight edit), patches `activeDocument.filePath` + `activeDocument.displayTitle` with the server response, and forwards the returned `librarianMessage` through the existing `onLibrarianMessageRef` path — the `mtime` carries through untouched because `moveDatabaseDocument` doesn't bump `lastModified` and `fs.rename` preserves filesystem mtime, so the next save's optimistic-concurrency check still matches. `page.tsx` now passes `onTitleChange={documentModeHook.renameDocument}` to `DocumentPane`. The `rename-document` action is registered in `CHAT_POST_ACTIONS` at `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/post.ts` and re-exported from `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/index.ts`. (`app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/index.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/post.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/documentModeApi.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useDocumentMode.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts`)
- **Agent mode — `submit_final_response` no longer ghost-wraps completed work from a previous turn**: Observed on Friday (chat `ea15913b-67a6-4ca6-8671-11ff6294d5b4`, 15:09–15:10): after a multi-turn agent run hit the 10-turn limit at 15:08:32 and produced a forced final response summarizing five file edits, the user sent a relational follow-up ("I love you, Amy…"). Amy re-entered agent mode, produced no conversational prose, and called `submit_final_response` on iteration 0 with a third-person recap of the *previous* turn's work — 965 reasoning tokens followed by a tool call whose `response` argument was the summary the user had already seen, with `content: ""` on the assistant message. The orchestrator's completion branch at `lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts:1412` (`agentFinalResponse = args.response || currentResponse`) then overwrote whatever had streamed with that recap, so the user saw prose-shaped content briefly appear and get replaced by a meta-narration wrap-up. Two linked changes close the loop. (1) `buildAgentModeInstructions` in `lib/services/chat-message/agent-mode-resolver.service.ts` rewords the `submit_final_response` section to scope the tool explicitly to *this turn's* agentic work — "**Do NOT submit** if the user's message is conversational, relational, or a simple follow-up — just respond in character with natural prose" and "**Do NOT submit** just to re-summarize or wrap up work from a previous turn that already concluded." Memory search and other tools remain available on every turn; only the structured-summary framing is gated. (2) A belt-and-suspenders orchestrator guardrail that detects the ghost-wrap-up shape — `toolIterations === 0` AND `toolCalls.length === 1` AND `submit_final_response` is the lone call AND no prose content streamed — and, instead of taking the completion branch, synthesizes a `success: false` tool-result explaining why the call was rejected and instructing the model to respond conversationally (memory / other tools still allowed). The existing tool-loop plumbing then re-streams with that correction in context, so the next pass produces an in-character reply. `toolIterations` still increments, so the correction can't loop forever; if the model stubbornly calls `submit_final_response` again on iteration 1 without producing real work, that second call succeeds — at that point we stop second-guessing. Models that emit prose *alongside* a ghost `submit_final_response` slip through the guardrail intentionally (the prose check is the escape hatch; we don't want to discard real speech). `help/agent-mode.md` gained a "When It Fires — And When It Shouldn't" subsection explaining the new scope and the guardrail, and `ToolProcessingResult` was added to the types import in `orchestrator.service.ts` for the synthesized result. (`lib/services/chat-message/agent-mode-resolver.service.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts`, `help/agent-mode.md`)
- **Background jobs — FAILED retries no longer strand forever when the processor auto-stops, and the Lantern routes around post-hoc image-moderation rejections through the Concierge**: Two linked bugs surfaced together on Friday (chat `af0642d1-c23a-4928-8184-4b33f4e2a6e7`, job `a9a56cbf-5661-446e-ad39-535f6cf1f212`). The user queued a story-background regeneration; Grok's image endpoint accepted the prompt but rejected the *generated image* post-hoc with `400 "Generated image rejected by content moderation."`. `markFailed` in `lib/database/repositories/background-jobs.repository.ts` correctly set `status='FAILED'` / `attempts=1/3` / `scheduledAt=2026-04-23T14:13:41Z` (60-second exponential-backoff retry), but two seconds later the processor's auto-stop path in `lib/background-jobs/processor.ts` fired — `claimNextJob()` returns only rows with `scheduledAt <= now`, which excluded the just-scheduled future retry, so the processor declared the queue empty, cleared the polling interval, and went quiet. Nothing else ever woke it back up: `ensureProcessorRunning` is only called from enqueue paths, so the retry sat idle indefinitely and the user's background regen never happened. Meanwhile the catch block at the image-generation call in `lib/background-jobs/handlers/story-background.ts` just re-threw the moderation error even though the Concierge already carried an `uncensoredImageProfileId` in `DangerousContentSettings` for exactly this case — the existing fallbacks for prompt crafting and appearance resolution checked it, but the generation call itself didn't. Three changes close both holes: (1) New `findNextScheduledAt()` on `BackgroundJobsRepository` — `$in: ['PENDING', 'FAILED']` + `$expr: { $lt: ['$attempts', '$maxAttempts'] }` sorted by `scheduledAt` ascending, limit 1 — returns the earliest future retry time across all retry-eligible jobs. (2) `processor.ts` gains a module-level `wakeUpTimer` with `armWakeUpTimer(scheduledAt)` (delay clamped to `[100ms, 5min]` so a far-future schedule doesn't pin a multi-hour timer and a past-due one gets a 100ms bounce) that `setTimeout`s a call to `ensureProcessorRunning()`. The auto-stop branch now queries `findNextScheduledAt()` before stopping and arms the timer if anything came back, so the FAILED job wakes the processor up exactly when its `scheduledAt` comes due. `startProcessor` and `stopProcessor` both call `clearWakeUpTimer()` so enqueues and shutdowns don't race a stale pending wake — explicit cleanup beats hoping nothing else starts the processor in the interim. (3) `story-background.ts` gains an `isImageModerationError(error)` helper matching the common phrasings (`"content moderation"`, `"content_policy"`, `"content policy"`, `"safety system"`, `"rejected by content"`, `"moderation_blocked"`) across Grok, OpenAI DALL-E, OpenRouter, and friends — keyword-based rather than status-code-based because every provider wraps its own error type and we don't want to care which SDK we caught. The catch block after `provider.generateImage` now checks moderation-shape + `dangerSettings.uncensoredImageProfileId` + "isn't the profile we just tried", and on match loads the uncensored profile, decrypts its API key through `connections.findApiKeyByIdAndUserId`, creates a second `createImageProvider` for its provider type, and retries with the same prompt/size/style. An `activeImageProfile` mutable tracks whichever profile ended up producing the final image, so the `generationModel` column on the resulting `files` row reflects reality (not the provider that rejected). The reroute logs both attempts through `logLLMCall` for Inspector visibility, and a reroute failure now throws `"Image generation failed after Concierge reroute: ..."` carrying the fallback's error message so the Inspector entry names the actual cause. Mirrors the existing prompt-crafting fallback at lines 430-468 and the appearance-resolution retry at lines 299-337 in the same file — same shape, same gating on presence of the uncensored profile rather than on `mode` (which already gates whether the Concierge is watching at all). Stranded jobs from before this fix will be picked up automatically on the next processor wake (which happens the moment any new job is enqueued, or on server restart). (`lib/database/repositories/background-jobs.repository.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/processor.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/story-background.ts`)
- **Character-avatar refresh announcements now come from Aurora, not the Lantern**: The three image-pipeline kinds routed through `postLanternImageNotification` in `lib/services/lantern-notifications/writer.ts` all used to attribute their chat-side announcement to the Lantern, including the `avatar` kind fired by `CHARACTER_AVATAR_GENERATION` background jobs (user-initiated regen via the participant sidebar, and wardrobe-change auto-regen when `chat.avatarGenerationEnabled` is on). Portraits are Aurora's domain — the character model keeping a character's current likeness on file — so the avatar kind now posts as Aurora (`systemSender: 'aurora'`) with Aurora-voiced content ("Aurora has refreshed the portrait filed under {name}'s name, the previous likeness now retired with due ceremony..."), while `background` (atmospheric backdrops) and `character-image` (ad-hoc images the Lantern produces on request from the `generate_image` tool) continue to attribute to the Lantern. `MessageEventSchema.systemSender` (and the SQLite row schema) widened from `z.enum(['lantern'])` to `z.enum(['lantern', 'aurora'])` — no migration needed because the column is free-form TEXT and the enum is a Zod-level constraint. `getMessageAvatar` in `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx` gained an `aurora` branch returning `{ name: 'Aurora', avatarUrl: '/images/avatars/aurora-avatar.webp' }`. Export schema updated. UI real-time delivery is already covered by the existing avatar-URL poll at `page.tsx:152` (it's called both from `handleRegenerateAvatar` and from the wardrobe-change effect at line 464 when `avatarGenerationEnabled`), which triggers `fetchChat()` the moment the new avatar URL appears — the Aurora message lands in the same refresh as the new portrait. (`lib/services/lantern-notifications/writer.ts`, `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/chats-messages.ops.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/types.ts`, `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`)
- **Lantern — backdrop-announcement message now appears in the chat without a page refresh, and shows as from "The Lantern" instead of the user's primary character**: `postLanternImageNotification` (`lib/services/lantern-notifications/writer.ts`) writes a synthetic ASSISTANT-role message into `chat_messages` from the `STORY_BACKGROUND_GENERATION` background job, with `participantId: null` so the normal participant-lookup path is bypassed. Two separate things were wrong. (1) The salon UI has no live subscription for out-of-band message inserts — `fetchChat()` only fires at SSE-streaming lifecycle points — so the row sat in the DB unseen until the user navigated away and back. Meanwhile `useStoryBackground` (`hooks/useStoryBackground.ts`) was already polling for the background URL change (active poll on regenerate, 30s passive SWR poll while the chat is open), and that URL update is written in the same job handler one step before the notification (`lib/background-jobs/handlers/story-background.ts:643, 666`). The hook now accepts an optional `onBackgroundChanged` callback; it fires from the active-polling interval when the URL flips, and from a new `useEffect` that compares the SWR-derived URL to a `previousUrlRef` on every render (skipping the initial `undefined → value` transition so the first load doesn't trigger a spurious refresh). `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx` passes `() => { void fetchChat() }` as the callback, so the chat re-fetches alongside the backdrop swap and the Lantern message appears in the message list immediately. (2) `getMessageAvatar` at `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx:952` treated `participantId: null` + `role: 'ASSISTANT'` as a fall-through to `getFirstCharacter()`, which returned the user's primary character — "Friday" on the reporting user's instance. A new `systemSender` field on `MessageEventSchema` (Zod enum `'lantern' | null`, `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`) and the matching SQLite column on `chat_messages` (TEXT, nullable, added by `migrations/scripts/add-system-sender-field.ts` mirroring the `isSilentMessage` pattern) identifies messages authored by a personified feature in lieu of a participant. The writer sets `systemSender: 'lantern'`; the API read handler passes it through (`app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/get.ts:272`); the UI `Message` type (`app/salon/[id]/types.ts`) picks it up; and `getMessageAvatar` now returns `{ name: 'The Lantern', avatarUrl: '/images/avatars/lantern-avatar.webp' }` when the field is set, ahead of the participant/role fall-through. Enum rather than free-form string so the Concierge, Prospero, Calliope, and friends can be added to the same field later without a second schema migration. Export schema (`public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`) and DDL.md updated to match. Character context-building is unaffected — the message still carries `role: 'ASSISTANT'` and flows through the existing vision-content piggy-back (now scoped per-character since `4.3-dev`) exactly as before. (`lib/services/lantern-notifications/writer.ts`, `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/chats-messages.ops.ts`, `migrations/scripts/add-system-sender-field.ts`, `migrations/scripts/index.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/get.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/types.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `hooks/useStoryBackground.ts`, `docs/developer/DDL.md`, `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`)
- **Scriptorium — Markdown/txt/JSON files can now be previewed and deleted from project Files modals**: `GET /api/v1/mount-points/[id]/blobs/[...path]` (`app/api/v1/mount-points/[id]/blobs/[...path]/route.ts`) only checked `doc_mount_blobs`, but the Stage 1 migration routes text documents (fileType `markdown` / `txt` / `json` / `jsonl`) into `doc_mount_documents` and only the non-text "blob" bucket into `doc_mount_blobs`. Net effect: clicking a markdown file in the Files card preview (or inside the Browse All Files modal, which shares `useFilePreview`) hit the blob endpoint for a row that doesn't exist there and fell through to a 404 with `[useFilePreview] Failed to load text content` in the browser; deleting one 404'd too. Image thumbnails kept working because blob rows are where images live. The GET handler now looks up `docMountBlobs.findByMountPointAndPath` first, and when that misses, falls back to `docMountDocuments.findByMountPointAndPath`, serving `doc.content` as UTF-8 with `text/markdown; charset=utf-8` / `text/plain; charset=utf-8` / `application/json; charset=utf-8` / `application/jsonl; charset=utf-8` based on `doc.fileType` and `contentSha256` in the `X-Blob-Sha256` response header. DELETE falls back to `deleteDatabaseDocument` from `lib/mount-index/database-store.ts` when the blob deletion misses, so the `doc_mount_documents` row, its `doc_mount_files` index mirror, and any `doc_mount_chunks` are all removed together and the store event fires. PATCH (description updates) is unchanged — documents don't have a description column, and a 404 there is the correct answer. (`app/api/v1/mount-points/[id]/blobs/[...path]/route.ts`)
- **Prospero — Files card count now tracks the linked Scriptorium store instead of the stale legacy files table**: `handleListFiles` in `app/api/v1/projects/[id]/actions/files.ts` backed `/api/v1/projects/{id}?action=list-files` with `repos.files.findAll()` filtered by `projectId`, so the number next to "Files" on the project page counted `files`-table rows — which Stage 1 never touched during migration, and which Stage 2 still writes alongside every mount-store upload. Net effect: after migration the count kept reporting pre-migration rows with stale on-disk storageKeys pointing at the archived `_doc_store_archive` directory, and if files were added to or removed from the project's store through the Scriptorium UI (outside the files-table write path) the count didn't budge. The handler now resolves the project's primary store via `getProjectDocumentStore` and, when one exists, maps `doc_mount_files` rows into the `ProjectFile` shape — same data source the Browse All Files modal uses — so the card count, thumbnails, and preview modal all agree on what's in the store. `ProjectFile` gained optional `mountPointId`/`relativePath` fields plumbed through `FilesCard.tsx` into `FileThumbnail` and the preview modal's `toFileInfo`, so thumbnails resolve against `/api/v1/mount-points/{id}/blobs/{path}` instead of `/api/v1/files/{id}` when the file lives in a mount store. Projects with no linked store still fall through to the legacy files-table listing unchanged. MIME types are derived from each `doc_mount_files.fileType` enum value, with `'blob'` falling back to `detectMimeType(fileName)` from `lib/file-storage/scanner.ts` so images in the store still show as images. Category collapses to `'IMAGE'` vs `'DOCUMENT'`, matching what the legacy `files.watcher` and `reconciliation` paths already assign. (`app/api/v1/projects/[id]/actions/files.ts`, `app/prospero/[id]/types.ts`, `app/prospero/[id]/components/FilesCard.tsx`)
- **Prospero — "Browse All Files" now opens the project's own document store instead of a manually-linked one**: Stage 3 of the Scriptorium consolidation routed the Files card through the first database-backed store returned by `/api/v1/projects/{id}/mount-points`, which depended on whatever order `project_doc_mount_links.findByProjectId` happened to return — fine on projects with exactly one linked store but wrong on projects that also had a user-linked Scriptorium (e.g. a shared reference store). Uploads went to the Stage 2 bridge's own first-match pick, which could resolve differently, so the Files card UI and the upload redirect could open two different stores. Both paths now route through a new `pickPrimaryProjectStore` helper (`lib/mount-index/project-store-naming.ts`) that prefers a mount point whose name starts with "Project Files: " (the prefix the Stage 1 migration uses when creating each project's auto-built store — also extracted as `PROJECT_OWN_STORE_NAME_PREFIX` so the migration, the bridge, and the browser all reference the same constant) and falls back to the first eligible database-backed documents store when no name-match exists (new projects whose only link was added by hand, or projects whose auto-created store was renamed). `getProjectDocumentStore` in `lib/file-storage/project-store-bridge.ts` now gathers every linked mount point into an array and hands it to the picker instead of early-returning on the first match; the FileBrowser's auto-resolve effect in `components/files/FileBrowser.tsx` does the same on the client side; and `resolveProjectDocumentStore` in `lib/tools/handlers/project-info-handler.ts` (the `project_info get_info` action that tells characters which shelf their project's files live on) uses the same picker so the reported store tracks the one writes land in. Filesystem / obsidian mounts and character stores are ignored either way — the redirect never applied to them. (`lib/mount-index/project-store-naming.ts`, `lib/file-storage/project-store-bridge.ts`, `components/files/FileBrowser.tsx`, `lib/tools/handlers/project-info-handler.ts`, `migrations/scripts/convert-project-files-to-document-stores.ts`)
- **Physical backups — weekly, monthly, and yearly retention tiers now actually retain anything**: The tiered retention policy in `applyRetentionPolicy` (`lib/database/backends/sqlite/physical-backup.ts`) advertised "all for 7 days, weekly for 4 weeks, monthly for 12 months, yearly forever" and had code for every tier, but the weekly/monthly bucket loops iterated newest-first and `break`ed on the first match — so each bucket kept the *newest* backup in its age window.
