On the next day's retention pass, an even fresher backup entered the same window and became the new "kept" one; the previous day's pick was then missing from the `keep` set and got deleted at the bottom of the function. Net effect: nothing ever aged past ~8 days, so users who started the app daily ended up with ~7 daily + 1 "weekly" that was really just an 8-day-old daily. Weeks 2/3/4, month buckets, and the yearly tier never accumulated anything because no backup survived long enough to reach them. Phase 2 and Phase 3 now iterate oldest-first, keeping the *oldest* backup in each bucket — which has the most runway to age into the next tier on subsequent passes, instead of being aged out of its bucket and deleted the same day. A new regression test simulates 40 consecutive days of daily backup + retention runs with a stateful fs mock and asserts that all four weekly buckets plus the month-1 bucket end up populated; this would have failed loudly against the old code, which left only the 7-day daily window. (`lib/database/backends/sqlite/physical-backup.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/database/physical-backup.test.ts`)
- **Lantern — generated images are now delivered to each character exactly once**: The vision-content piggy-back added in `4c76a5af` (`buildMessageContext` in `lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts`) walked the last 6 ASSISTANT messages on every turn and re-attached every image file ID it found to that turn's request. Because the synthetic Lantern notification (story background, avatar regeneration, or `generate_image` tool result) sits in that window for many turns after it's posted, every character that took a turn while it was still in window saw the same image attached again, and again, and in multi-character chats the same image often went out 4–6 times in a row — observed as characters fixating on or repeatedly commenting on the same picture. The walk now stops at the requesting character's own most recent ASSISTANT message: in multi-character chats by `participantId` match (each character's responses are tagged), in single-character chats by the structural signal that character responses don't carry attachments while Lantern notifications always do. Anything older than the character's last turn was already delivered and is skipped. A new joining character with `hasHistoryAccess === false` clamps the walk further with a `historyCutoff = participant.createdAt`, so they never receive images that were posted before they joined the chat. The `ASSISTANT_IMAGE_LOOKBACK = 6` cap survives as a safety bound for first-turn responses in long chats. The renamed `collectLanternImageFileIdsForCharacter` helper is exported and covered by 11 new unit tests at `__tests__/unit/lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.test.ts` (own-turn stop, multi-character cross-talk, dedupe across messages, lookback cap, history cutoff, single-character attachment heuristic, ignored entry types). (`lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.test.ts`)
- **Salon/Aurora — Search & Replace modal no longer trips "Maximum update depth exceeded" on chats with frequent re-renders**: both call sites pass an inline object literal to `SearchReplaceModal`'s `initialScope` prop (`{ type: 'chat', chatId }` in `app/salon/[id]/components/ChatModals.tsx`, `{ type: 'character', characterId: id }` in `app/aurora/[id]/view/page.tsx`), so each parent render produced a fresh reference. Inside `useSearchReplace`, `reset` listed `initialScope` as a `useCallback` dependency, which meant a new `reset` identity per render; the close-modal `useEffect` in `SearchReplaceModal` then re-fired on every render and, while `!isOpen`, called `reset()` → `setScope(initialScope || null)` with the new object — a real state change that re-rendered the hook. With `ChatPage` re-rendering frequently during streaming, React's max-update-depth detector tripped. The hook now captures `initialScope` in a ref (kept current via a small `useEffect`) and `reset` is declared with empty deps, giving it a stable identity regardless of how callers spell their props. Both call sites are unchanged. (`components/tools/search-replace/hooks/useSearchReplace.ts`)
- **Prospero — Characters card no longer logs a React "unique key" warning when a project roster has duplicate IDs**: `app/prospero/[id]/components/CharactersCard.tsx` set `key={char.id}` on each grid card, which is correct in principle, but the underlying `project.characterRoster` is a `string[]` and, although every write path dedupes (`POST /api/v1/projects/[id]?action=add-to-roster`, the chat-creation helpers in `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts` and `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts`, and `ProjectsRepository.addCharacterToRoster`), older data on disk can still carry repeated IDs — the server enricher in `app/api/v1/projects/[id]/actions/project-crud.ts` then resolves the same `characterId` twice via `findById` and emits two roster entries with identical `id`s, which React correctly flags. `visibleCharacters`'s `useMemo` now threads a `Set<string>` through the filter, dropping any entry whose `id` is falsy or already seen, so the duplicates (and any freak nullish id) can't reach the grid. Quick-hide filtering is unchanged for the entries that survive the dedupe. (`app/prospero/[id]/components/CharactersCard.tsx`)
- **Wardrobe — `update_outfit_item` with `item_id: "none"` (or `"null"`/`""`) now clears the slot instead of throwing "not found"**: LLMs frequently fill required-looking string fields with the string `"none"` when they mean "no value" — so a call like `{slot: 'top', item_id: 'none'}` was taking the equip branch in `lib/tools/handlers/wardrobe-update-outfit-handler.ts`, doing `repos.wardrobe.findById('none')`, and failing with `WardrobeUpdateOutfitError: Wardrobe item not found with ID "none"` instead of clearing the slot. A new `normalizeNoItemSentinel` helper trims-and-lowercases `item_id` and `item_title` and maps `"none"`, `"null"`, and `""` to `undefined`, routing the call through the existing unequip branch (`unequipWithDisplacement` on the requested slot) — identical to the behavior when the field is omitted entirely. Real item IDs and titles (including any that happen to contain the substring "none") are unaffected because the match is full-string, case-insensitive, and post-trim. Fires a debug log noting the normalization when it happens. (`lib/tools/handlers/wardrobe-update-outfit-handler.ts`)
- **Server — transient LLM-provider network hiccups no longer crash the whole process**: Observed on Friday (2026-04-22 16:12:45 UTC): a successful multi-character turn on GROK finished, post-turn fan-out enqueued a burst of INTER_CHARACTER_MEMORY / MEMORY_EXTRACTION / CONVERSATION_RENDER jobs, an outbound fetch() to a Cloudflare-fronted provider (IP `2606:4700::6812:373`) got its socket cut mid-stream with undici's `TypeError: terminated` (cause: `SocketError: other side closed`, `UND_ERR_SOCKET`, 7173 bytes written / 1694 read), and ~2.5 minutes of log silence followed before `combined.log` shows `[JobQueue] Processor started` with fresh config and `Initializing MCP connection manager` — i.e. the dev server actually died and restarted. The smoking gun was `setupSQLiteShutdownHandlers` in `lib/database/backends/sqlite/client.ts`: its `process.on('unhandledRejection', ...)` handler closes the SQLite connection, releases the instance lock, and calls `process.exit(1)` *unconditionally* for any rejection — originally wired that way so a genuinely bad state wouldn't corrupt SQLite at shutdown, but the blast radius is every transient socket close from every outbound fetch to every LLM provider, image API, or MCP server, since any of those can leak a `terminated` rejection past a generator's `for await` boundary if the body consumer doesn't wrap it in try/catch. Fix: the `unhandledRejection` handler now classifies rejections. A new `isRecoverableNetworkRejection` helper matches against a `RECOVERABLE_NETWORK_CODES` set covering undici stream errors (`UND_ERR_SOCKET`, `UND_ERR_CLOSED`, `UND_ERR_ABORTED`, `UND_ERR_BODY_TIMEOUT`, `UND_ERR_HEADERS_TIMEOUT`, `UND_ERR_CONNECT_TIMEOUT`, both content-length-mismatch variants) and POSIX socket errors (`ECONNRESET`, `ECONNREFUSED`, `ECONNABORTED`, `EPIPE`, `ETIMEDOUT`, `EHOSTUNREACH`, `ENETUNREACH`, `ENOTFOUND`, `EAI_AGAIN`), walks both `error.code` and `error.cause.code` since undici's `TypeError: terminated` carries the interesting code on its `cause` not itself, and falls back to matching `reason.name === 'TypeError' && reason.message === 'terminated'` for older undici versions whose cause chain is missing. Matching rejections log at `warn` level with the error message, code, and cause code, and the process keeps running. Non-matching rejections hit the original exit path unchanged — the "something is genuinely wrong" case (type errors in repository code, assertion failures, etc.) still takes the server down cleanly rather than silently corrupting state. `uncaughtException` is untouched because sync throws past this point usually mean V8-level corruption, not a Cloudflare edge closing a socket. (`lib/database/backends/sqlite/client.ts`)
- **Wardrobe — gifts and edits now show up immediately on characters that read from the document vault**: The overlay that landed in `23557cc9` treats `wardrobe.json` as authoritative whenever a character has `readPropertiesFromDocumentStore` on and a linked mount point — `getOverlaidWardrobeItems` / `getOverlaidOutfitPresets` discard the DB loader's result entirely when the vault is valid. But every write path — the gift tool's `create_wardrobe_item`, the direct `POST /api/v1/characters/[id]/wardrobe`, and every preset mutation — only wrote to the DB via `repos.wardrobe.create` / `repos.outfitPresets.*`, so the new row became invisible on the next read (observed on Friday: a silk kimono gifted to Amy wrote `wardrobe_items` row `891c9418-…` at 15:07:12.682Z, and the refetch 62 ms later read the vault's pre-gift 7369-byte / 11-item snapshot and returned it verbatim). The one-time startup task `refreshVaultWardrobe` in `lib/startup/refresh-vault-wardrobe.ts` was the only thing that ever projected DB state into `wardrobe.json`, and it's gated by a `wardrobe_json_refreshed_v1` flag in `instance_settings` so it never fires twice on the same DB — meaning any drift that accumulated between startups was permanent until the flag was cleared by hand. Fix: a new `syncCharacterVaultWardrobe(characterId)` helper in `lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts` reads the full DB state (`findByCharacterIdRaw` on both `wardrobe` and `outfitPresets`) and rewrites `wardrobe.json` via `writeDatabaseDocument`, no-oping for archetype rows (`characterId === null`) and non-overlay candidates. Writes are serialized per character via a `Map<string, Promise<void>>` chain so two concurrent syncs can't each read a stale DB snapshot and race-overwrite each other's result. Wired into `WardrobeRepository.create`/`update`/`archive`/`unarchive`/`delete` and `OutfitPresetsRepository.create`/`update`/`delete`/`removeItemFromPresets` — the last one collects the set of affected `characterId`s as it iterates and syncs each unique one once at the end, rather than one sync per modified preset. Vault-write failures log at `error` level but don't propagate: the DB write is already committed, and a thrown error would only tempt the caller into a retry that creates a duplicate DB row. To recover existing drifted vaults after upgrade, `DELETE FROM instance_settings WHERE key='wardrobe_json_refreshed_v1'` and restart — `refreshVaultWardrobe` then rewrites every linked character's `wardrobe.json` from the DB. The `quilltap db` CLI opens the DB read-only for one-shot SQL; use `--repl` mode (piping the DELETE via stdin works fine when the dev server isn't holding the write lock). (`lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/wardrobe.repository.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/outfit-presets.repository.ts`)
- **New Chat form — Starting Scenario "Custom..." no longer hides the textarea on initial render**: In `components/new-chat/NewChatForm.tsx`, the Starting Scenario dropdown's `value` prop used `state.scenarioId ?? CUSTOM_SCENARIO_VALUE`, so both `null` and any unmatched id visually fell back to "Custom..." (the browser renders the first `<option>` when a controlled `<select>`'s value matches no option). But `showCustomTextarea` gated the textarea on a strict `state.scenarioId === null`. When `char.defaultScenarioId` pointed at a scenario that wasn't in the character's current `scenarios` array — stale default, deleted preset, or the modal's second effect leaking `char.defaultScenarioId ?? prev.scenarioId` across character switches in `components/new-chat/hooks/useNewChat.ts` — the dropdown visually showed "Custom..." but `showCustomTextarea` stayed `false`, so there was no textarea to type into below the dropdown and no preset card either (since `singleCharacterScenarios.find(s => s.id === stale)` returned `undefined`). Flipping to a real scenario and back worked because `handleScenarioSelectChange(CUSTOM)` explicitly sets `scenarioId: null`, at which point both conditions agreed again. Both conditions now derive from the same source of truth — whether a valid preset is actually selected: `showCustomTextarea = !singleCharacterScenarios || !selectedPreset` and `value={selectedPreset?.id ?? CUSTOM_SCENARIO_VALUE}`, so the dropdown's display and the textarea's visibility can't drift apart regardless of what stale id the scenarioId carries. (`components/new-chat/NewChatForm.tsx`)
- **Salon — "Maximum update depth exceeded" during SSE streaming, take three**: Follow-up to the `useOutfit` stable-deps fix in `23557cc9` and the `storyBackgroundsEnabled` fix in `b0e551ff`. The commit message on take two called out the *"three `setState`s per SSE chunk"* as the amplifier that lets any cascading dep-rotation tip React 19 past its update-depth tripwire. Resurfaced again in an eight-participant chain chat: the chain magnifies everything — every turn boundary whiplashes `setStreaming(false)` / `setWaitingForResponse(true)` in `onTurnStart` and the next content chunk flips them straight back — and a first attempt that only guarded those transition flags behind a `hasStartedStreaming` local (so they fire once per turn instead of once per chunk) still left `setStreamingContent` firing on every chunk, which tripped the same limit one line down. Two changes together: (1) the `hasStartedStreaming` flag stays (gates `setWaitingForResponse(false)` and `setStreaming(true)` to once per turn, reset on `turnStart`). (2) `setStreamingContent` is now rAF-coalesced: each chunk writes the accumulated content into a `streamingContentBufferRef` and schedules a `requestAnimationFrame` flush if one isn't already pending. The flush calls `setStreamingContent` at most once per animation frame, so the render rate is capped at the display refresh rate regardless of how fast chunks arrive — during a fast burst, 50 chunks in a frame collapse to a single state update. A new `resetStreamingContent` helper (replaces every `setStreamingContent('')` reset in the hook) cancels any pending rAF before clearing state, so a stale buffered flush can't stomp a reset at turn/chain/error/abort boundaries. A cleanup `useEffect` cancels the pending frame on unmount. End-to-end effect: in an eight-way chain where chunks can arrive faster than React can render them, the reconciler sees tens of state updates per second instead of hundreds, which gives any remaining effect-chain enough wall-clock time to unwind each render cycle before the next update lands. Doesn't paper over a genuine infinite loop if one still exists upstream, but widens the margin the same way takes one and two did — just at the volume knob instead of the dependency graph. (`app/salon/[id]/hooks/useSSEStreaming.ts`)
- **Salon — intermittent "Maximum update depth exceeded" during SSE streaming, take two**: Follow-up to the `storyBackgroundsEnabled` stable-deps fix in `b0e551ff`. The remaining cascade was in `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useOutfit.ts`: `fetchWardrobeForCharacter` listed `wardrobeCache` (React state) as its `useCallback` dep, so every `setWardrobeCache` call — one per character's wardrobe fetch — rotated the callback's identity, which rotated `refreshOutfit`'s identity, which rotated the mount effect inside `useOutfit` and the outfit effect at `page.tsx:398` depending on it. With three `setState`s firing per SSE chunk (`setWaitingForResponse(false)` / `setStreaming(true)` / `setStreamingContent(fullContent)` at `useSSEStreaming.ts:215`), any race where an outfit fetch completed mid-stream tipped the chain past React 19's update-depth tripwire — intermittent, because the cache stabilizes after the first fetch round and the loop only blew up when streaming started before the initial round settled. Fix: mirror the wardrobe cache into a `wardrobeCacheRef` and drop the state dep from `fetchWardrobeForCharacter`. The state copy still drives renders; the ref carries reads inside the callback so its identity is empty-deps stable. `refreshOutfit` consequently stabilizes too, so the outfit effect's `outfit.refreshOutfit` dep no longer shifts under streaming. (`app/salon/[id]/hooks/useOutfit.ts`)
- **Salon — wardrobe-change Notify button now inserts a `wardrobe`-fenced code block instead of roleplay-narration delimiters**: The "Notify" button that appears above the gutter tools when a character's outfit or wardrobe has changed (via the sidebar equip controls or a gift) previously wrapped the change description in the current roleplay template's narration delimiters (`*…*`, `[…]`, etc.) — which told the model to treat the change as narration prose rather than structured state. The handler in `app/salon/[id]/components/ChatComposer.tsx` now wraps the list in a triple-backtick fenced code block with `wardrobe` as the language tag, so the model sees the change as structured data. The `describeOutfit()` normalization in `lib/wardrobe/outfit-description.ts` is unchanged — empty slots still render as "naked", "topless", "bottomless", "barefoot", "no accessories", the fully-empty case still collapses to "completely naked and unadorned", and multi-slot items still group to a single line. One implementation detail worth flagging: the old path called `prependText`, which creates a single Lexical text node and then backslash-escapes any backticks when the editor serializes back to markdown — so the naive change produced a block starting with literal backslashed backticks in the sent message. The new code routes the combined markdown through `setMarkdown` instead, so the fence parses into a real `CodeNode` and survives serialization intact. The previously-threaded `narrationDelimiters` dependency was dropped from the insertion callback since it's no longer consulted there (it's still passed to `FormattingToolbar` for the unchanged roleplay-annotation buttons). (`app/salon/[id]/components/ChatComposer.tsx`)
- **Connection profile Auto-Configure now falls back across providers instead of dying when the default profile's provider is unavailable**: When the default connection profile's provider returned an error (observed on Friday: Anthropic 400 `invalid_request_error` — "You have reached your specified API usage limits. You will regain access on 2026-05-01 at 00:00 UTC."), `autoConfigureProfile` in `lib/services/auto-configure.service.ts` re-threw immediately and the route handler at `app/api/v1/connection-profiles/route.ts:567` masked the cause with a generic `"Failed to auto-configure profile"` — so the modal's toast said nothing actionable and the user had to log-dive to find the quota message. Two linked changes close the loop: (1) a new `pickAutoConfigureCandidates(allProfiles, defaultProfile)` helper builds an ordered list — default first, then for each *other* provider the highest-`modelClass` profile (Deep > Extended > Standard > Compact), skipping profiles with no `apiKeyId` unless they're OLLAMA. The per-profile analysis step (send-to-LLM + parse + cheap-LLM JSON cleanup) is now extracted into `analyzeWithProfile`, and the main loop iterates candidates sequentially, collecting `{ provider, modelName, error }` tuples on each failure and breaking on the first success. If every candidate fails, the thrown error now summarises every attempt (`"Auto-configure failed on all 4 candidate provider(s). ANTHROPIC (claude-sonnet-4-6): 400 ...; OPENAI (gpt-5-nano): ...; ..."`). Candidate list logs at debug and each attempt logs at info with `isDefault` + the chosen fallback provider if one succeeds. (2) `handleAutoConfigure` in the route now returns the underlying error message via `serverError(error.message)` instead of the hard-coded generic string, so the UI toast finally shows what actually went wrong. Grouping by provider (not cycling by tier) because quota/auth failures are per-provider — trying two Anthropic profiles when the first 429'd would just burn time. `cleanupWithCheapLLM`'s `defaultProfile` parameter was renamed to `currentProfile` since it's no longer guaranteed to be the default, and `getApiKey` now returns `''` for OLLAMA (no key needed) and includes the profile name in its "no API key" and "could not retrieve" errors. (`lib/services/auto-configure.service.ts`, `app/api/v1/connection-profiles/route.ts`)
- **OpenRouter plugin (1.0.33) — image attachments now reach vision-capable models instead of being silently dropped**: The previous per-profile `supportsImageUpload` flag (4.3-dev) opened the *upload-side* gate on OpenRouter profiles pointed at vision-capable models like `z-ai/glm-5v-turbo`, but the OpenRouter plugin itself still hardcoded `supportsFileAttachments = false` and its three send paths (`sendMessage`, `streamMessage` via SDK `callModel`, `streamWithTools` via direct fetch) all built request messages by mapping each `LLMMessage` to `{ role, content: m.content }` — never consulting `m.attachments[]`. End-to-end effect: with `supportsImageUpload=1`, the chat-attachment fallback at `lib/chat/file-attachment-fallback.ts` correctly *skipped* the cheap-LLM image-description summarizer (it thought the model would see the image natively), but the plugin then *also* skipped the image, so the model received the user's text-only message and behaved as if no attachment existed (observed in chat 58027ede on Friday: a user message announcing a Lantern photo plus an attachment row with file `48188506-...`, followed by an assistant turn that asked for the picture to be sent). Three changes to `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openrouter/provider.ts`: (1) new `buildMessageContent(m)` helper emits OpenAI Chat Completions vision content parts (`{ type: 'text', text }` + `{ type: 'image_url', image_url: { url } }`) when the message carries `image/{jpeg,png,gif,webp}` attachments — uses `attachment.url` if present, otherwise builds a `data:${mime};base64,${data}` URL — and falls back to the plain string when there are no images. (2) `streamMessage` now routes through the direct Chat Completions fetch path whenever the request has tools *or* image attachments; the SDK's `callModel`/OpenResponses input format (via `fromChatMessages`) doesn't round-trip `image_url` parts reliably, so multimodal traffic goes straight to OpenRouter's `/v1/chat/completions` endpoint where the OpenAI vision schema is the wire format. (3) The old `streamWithTools` is renamed `streamViaChatCompletions` and the `tools`/`tool_choice` block is now conditional, so a single direct-fetch path serves both tool-enabled and image-enabled (and tool+image) requests. New `collectAttachmentResults` (replaces `collectAttachmentFailures`) puts image attachments in `sent[]` and reserves `failed[]` for non-image MIME types (PDFs, text — still not implemented) and the rare image row missing both `data` and `url`. Class-level `supportsFileAttachments` flipped to `true`, `supportedMimeTypes` now lists the four supported image types, and the manifest's `attachmentSupport` block matches with a description that points users at the per-profile flag. (`plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openrouter/provider.ts`, `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openrouter/manifest.json`, `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openrouter/package.json`)
- **System prompt — Current Outfit no longer repeats the same item description once per slot**: A wardrobe item that occupies multiple slots (an "outfit" entity covering top + bottom + footwear + accessories, or a dress covering top + bottom) is stored as the *same* item ID under each slot it claims, and `describeOutfit` in `lib/wardrobe/outfit-description.ts` was emitting one bullet line per slot — so a single all-slot "Working Outfit" rendered as four identical bullets, with the entire title-and-description copy/pasted four times into the system prompt. The renderer now bucket-collects slots by their formatted string value and emits one line per unique value, with the participating slot names joined: `- **top, bottom, footwear, accessories:** Working Outfit (...)` for the full-cover case, `- **top, bottom:** silk dress` plus separate footwear/accessories lines for a multi-slot dress, and unchanged behavior when every slot holds a different item. The empty-slot fallbacks (`topless`, `bottomless`, `barefoot`, `no accessories`) are unique strings and never group accidentally; the `naked` collapse for `top === null && bottom === null` is preserved as a special case ahead of the grouping pass. New unit tests cover the full-collapse and partial-multi-slot cases. (`lib/wardrobe/outfit-description.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/wardrobe/outfit-utils.test.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — recent-access bonus in the protection score now actually fires, because the retrieval path finally updates `lastAccessedAt`**: Direct DB inspection of Friday's 17,726-memory corpus found only 13 rows with a non-null `lastAccessedAt`, and zero within the last 30 days — meaning the recent-access component of the blended protection score was structurally dead. The repository had an `updateAccessTime(characterId, memoryId)` method, and the Memories search API route was calling it fire-and-forget per hit, but every in-app retrieval path skipped it: the chat context builder (`lib/chat/context-manager.ts:776`), proactive recall (`lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts:844`), first-message context (`lib/chat/first-message-context.ts:139`), and the `search_scriptorium` tool handler (`lib/tools/handlers/search-scriptorium-handler.ts:91`) all called `searchMemoriesSemantic` and then walked off without bumping access time. That left the recent-access signal — the third leg of the protection-via-usage stool, worth 0.10 of the blended score for anything accessed in the last 90 days — starved of input for every character whose user didn't poke around in the Memories UI. Two changes close the loop: (1) new `MemoriesRepository.updateAccessTimeBulk(characterId, memoryIds)` that does one `updateMany` call with `{characterId, id: { $in: ids }}` instead of N per-memory `findById + update` round-trips, fine for the 20-60 hits a typical semantic search returns. (2) `searchMemoriesSemantic` now fires a fire-and-forget `bumpAccessTimes(characterId, results)` on both the vector-hit path and the text-fallback return, so every in-app retrieval path inherits the fix without further edits. The old per-memory `Promise.all(updateAccessTime)` block in `app/api/v1/memories/route.ts` is now redundant and has been removed — `searchMemoriesSemantic` is the single source of truth. `findSimilarMemories`/`findSimilarMemoriesWithEmbedding` deliberately do *not* bump access time; those paths are for write-time duplicate detection in the Memory Gate, not retrieval into LLM context. On an instance with steady chat activity, the 90-day recent-access column will now become meaningful evidence — and the blended protection score can do its intended job of separating "memory the LLM rated highly but the character never actually uses" from "memory the character actually reaches for." (`lib/database/repositories/memories.repository.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-service.ts`, `app/api/v1/memories/route.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — protection score no longer lets LLM rating alone keep a memory immortal, and the watermark backoff now recognizes sweeps that deleted a single-digit number as ineffective**: Follow-up to the 30-day half-life + zero-deletion-backoff fix. On the Friday instance, after that change, a sweep deleted 1 memory on one run and 6 on the next — practically zero against a 12,700-over-cap corpus, but the `deleted === 0` backoff trigger didn't catch single-digit deletions, so the watermark kept re-enqueueing housekeeping after every chat turn. Direct database inspection of Friday's 17,726 memories revealed why: **97% are less than thirty days old**, so the half-life had almost nothing to bite (a 12-day-old 0.7-importance memory scores `0.7 × 0.76 = 0.53`, already over the 0.5 protection threshold on content alone). Two linked tweaks close the loop: (1) `DEFAULT_PROTECTION_CONFIG` gains a new `maxContentContribution: 0.40` field in `lib/memory/memory-weighting.ts`. `calculateProtectionScore` now clamps the content component at that value, so a fresh 0.8-importance memory contributes 0.40 from content (not 0.80) and — with the default count-of-1 reinforcement bonus of 0.08 — lands at 0.48, just *under* protection. The memory has to earn the remaining 0.02+ from usage evidence (one graph link at 0.025, one extra reinforcement at ~0.05, or recent access at 0.10) to cross the threshold. Honors the blended-score design goal that LLM-rated importance is one opinion among several, not a final verdict. (2) `shouldSkipWatermarkSweep` in `lib/memory/housekeeping-outcome-cache.ts` now treats a sweep as ineffective when `deleted < max(10, floor(excess × 0.01))`, where `excess = totalBefore − cap`. On a 17,700-memory corpus with a 5,000 cap, the threshold is `max(10, 127) = 127`, so deleting 1 or 6 memories still triggers the 1-hour backoff. `HousekeepingResult` grew a `capUsed: number` field so the outcome cache can evaluate effectiveness against the exact cap the sweep ran with (per-character override, global cap, or housekeeping default of 2000), not a guess. Signal verification on Friday's corpus before making this change: reinforcement column populated on 15.7% of memories (max count 91), graph links populated on 51.3% (max 100 links) — confirmed these pathways are healthy enough to carry protection for memories that deserve it. `lastAccessedAt` is populated on only 13 of 17,726 rows, a separate retrieval-path bug worth filing, but the content cap still works because ~half the corpus has graph links to lean on. The `clamps the final score at 1.0` test was re-aimed at the new realistic default ceiling of 0.85 (content 0.40 + reinforcement 0.25 + graph 0.10 + access 0.10); the `Math.min(1, …)` at the end of `calculateProtectionScore` remains a safety net for future configs whose components might sum above 1. (`lib/memory/memory-weighting.ts`, `lib/memory/housekeeping-outcome-cache.ts`, `lib/memory/housekeeping.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/memory-housekeeping.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/memory-weighting.test.ts`, `docs/developer/features/memory_management.md`, `help/memory-housekeeping.md`)
- **Commonplace Book — housekeeping no longer runs after every chat turn on heavy characters, and actually deletes things when it does**: On the Friday instance with ~19.5k memories on one character, the blended protection score's content half-life of 365 days meant a 1-day-old memory at LLM-rated importance 0.7 scored ~0.70 — well above the 0.5 protection threshold. Every fresh memory was immortal until it aged out over year-scale timelines, which made the cap-enforcement pass a no-op: on a 19,550-memory character the sweep ran for the full 15-minute job timeout and deleted zero rows. Worse, the post-extraction watermark check (`maybeEnqueueHousekeeping` in `lib/memory/memory-service.ts`) fired after every memory write, so every chat turn enqueued another 15-minute no-op sweep that pinned the main thread and blocked the *next* chat turn's context build. Two linked changes: (1) `DEFAULT_PROTECTION_CONFIG.contentHalfLifeDays` drops from **365 to 30** in `lib/memory/memory-weighting.ts`. A 1-day-old memory at importance 0.7 still scores ~0.70 — recent information is still protected by content alone — but a 30-day-old memory at the same rating drops to ~0.35, at which point the usage bonuses (reinforcement, graph degree, recent access) have to actually fire for the memory to stay protected rather than the LLM's one-shot guess carrying it forever. The retrieval half-life was already 30 days in `DEFAULT_WEIGHTING_CONFIG`; protection now matches. (2) A new per-process outcome cache (`lib/memory/housekeeping-outcome-cache.ts`) records the `deleted` count from each completed sweep; `maybeEnqueueHousekeeping` consults it and skips the enqueue when the previous sweep for the same character deleted zero memories within the last hour. Watermark enqueues that would have produced another no-op sweep log `[Housekeeping] Skipping watermark sweep — previous sweep deleted zero within backoff window` at debug level and return without queueing. The scheduled daily sweep is unaffected — it still runs regardless of the backoff, since the whole point of the daily sweep is to re-check. `MANUAL`-sourced memories remain a hard override against deletion independent of any of this. Updated tests at `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/memory-weighting.test.ts` for the new half-life (stale-low-importance and rescued-by-signals tests still pass unchanged thanks to the blend design), developer breakdown at `docs/developer/features/memory_management.md`, and user-facing help at `help/memory-housekeeping.md` so the "one-year half-life" phrasing becomes "thirty-day half-life". (`lib/memory/memory-weighting.ts`, `lib/memory/housekeeping-outcome-cache.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-service.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/memory-housekeeping.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/memory-weighting.test.ts`, `docs/developer/features/memory_management.md`, `help/memory-housekeeping.md`)

- **Memory Housekeeping — giant-character sweep no longer gets stuck in a timeout-retry loop or blocks first page load**: On a Friday instance with one character carrying 19,523 memories, every scheduled housekeeping sweep ran past the job processor's hard 180-second timeout. The job got marked FAILED, the queue scheduled a retry 2–4 minutes later (exponential backoff, default `maxAttempts: 3`), and every retry re-ran the whole sweep from scratch — including across server restarts, because `PROCESSING` jobs get re-claimed on startup. In practice this meant that shortly after every boot, the main thread was pinned re-running a sweep that was going to time out again, making first page loads unresponsive (including `/api/v1/session`, `/api/v1/quick-hide-tags`, and `/api/v1/help-chats/*` surfacing as browser-side `TypeError: Failed to fetch`). Six fixes: (1) `MEMORY_HOUSEKEEPING` now has its own 15-minute timeout in `lib/background-jobs/processor.ts`, long enough for a realistic worst-case sweep over tens of thousands of memories even with event-loop yields. The default 3-minute timeout stays for other job types and the 10-minute timeout stays for embeddings. (2) `enqueueMemoryHousekeeping` now sets `maxAttempts: 1` by default — housekeeping is retry-hostile (every retry re-does the whole sweep, and a sweep that hit a transient failure is better off waiting for the next daily scheduled pass than thrashing the thread three times), and the scheduler re-enqueues naturally anyway. (3) `runHousekeeping` in `lib/memory/housekeeping.ts` now pre-checks whether any unprotected-and-undeleted memory exists before entering the cap-enforcement pass; when every remaining memory is protected (common on well-reinforced characters), it skips the O(n) scoring + O(n log n) sort entirely. On Friday this avoids doing 19,523 `calculateEffectiveWeight` calls plus a 19,523-element sort for a deletion loop that would have skipped every candidate. (4) The initial memory read is now paginated via a new `findByCharacterIdInBatches` on `MemoriesRepository` (250 rows per page, sorted by `id` for a stable boundary). Previously `findByCharacterId` loaded all 19,523 rows through Zod in one synchronous chunk, which pinned the main thread for tens of seconds before pass 1's `setImmediate` yields could even start helping. With batched loading, HTTP requests and lock heartbeats get a turn between pages, and each synchronous Zod-validation chunk stays under ~150 ms. (5) The housekeeping scheduler's startup grace in `lib/background-jobs/scheduled-housekeeping.ts` is now 5 minutes (was 30 seconds), giving the Next.js dev server time to finish compiling and the first page load time to complete before the sweep starts competing for the main thread. (6) The startup tick now skips itself entirely when a scheduled `MEMORY_HOUSEKEEPING` job completed within the last 20 hours — dev-restart friendly, since the 24-hour `setInterval` still fires on its own cadence for long-running instances. New `BackgroundJobsRepository.findRecentByType` helper backs the check. Callers with an explicit higher `maxAttempts` in the enqueue options are unaffected. (`lib/background-jobs/processor.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/queue-service.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/scheduled-housekeeping.ts`, `lib/memory/housekeeping.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/memories.repository.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/background-jobs.repository.ts`)
- **Salon — chat-list enrichment no longer fires hundreds of overlay queries on boot**: Every first request that hit `enrichChatsForList` (home page, Salon sidebar, chat picker) called `getCharacterSummary` per participant, which went through `characters.findById` → `applyDocumentStoreOverlayOne` → `applyDocumentStoreOverlay([character])` → **8 SQLCipher queries per call**. On a Friday instance with 287 chats and two overlay-candidate characters (Sunny, Friday), that came out to 538 overlay calls × 8 = ~4,300 synchronous encrypted queries back-to-back, ~3 seconds of main-thread stall right after the 30-second housekeeping grace period expired — felt in the UI as "the server stopped responding." Also ran `files.findById` per character-defaultImage and per story background, and `projects.findById` per chat, layering more N+1 on top. `enrichChatsForList` now pre-collects every distinct characterId, fileId, and projectId across the batch up front and runs one `findByIds` per repository: one overlay call covering all participating characters, one union-ed files query covering every defaultImage + every storyBackgroundImage, one projects query. The results flow through a new optional `ChatListPreloaded` parameter down through `enrichChatForList` → `enrichParticipantSummary` → `getCharacterSummary`, which short-circuit their per-row reads when the maps are present. Single-chat callers (`enrichParticipantDetail`, direct `getCharacterSummary` invocations) pass no preload and keep their existing behavior. Net effect on Friday: ~538 overlay calls → 1, ~287 project lookups → 1, ~N file lookups → 1. (`lib/services/chat-enrichment.service.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — housekeeping no longer stalls the event loop on characters with tens of thousands of memories**: A single Friday character carried 19,523 memories and every housekeeping sweep — scheduled *or* reactive — was pinning the main thread long enough to visibly freeze the Salon. Four compounding issues in `lib/memory/housekeeping.ts` and `lib/memory/memory-weighting.ts`: (1) `calculateEffectiveWeight` emitted a `logger.debug` with seven `.toFixed()` calls on every invocation — the cap-enforcement pass calls it once per remaining memory, so ~20k context-object constructions per run even with debug off. Removed. (2) `memoriesToDelete` was an array, and three hot spots called `.includes()` or `.filter(... !includes)` against it inside per-memory loops — O(n²) against 19k = ~380M comparisons in the worst case. Swapped to a `Set<string>` used throughout (the merge pass already had a local `deleteSet`; the retention and cap passes didn't). (3) The protection score — a multi-signal blended calc — was computed twice for most memories: once inside `shouldDeleteMemory` during the retention pass, then again inside the cap-enforcement pass's `isProtectedMemory` re-check. Pass 1 now stores results in a `protectedMap` that pass 3 reuses. (4) Neither of the two big loops yielded to the event loop at all. Each now `await new Promise(setImmediate)`s every 500 items, so HTTP requests, streaming SSE, and other queued jobs get a turn during a long sweep. Net effect for a 19k-memory character: housekeeping still takes the same wall-clock time, but no longer blocks anything else from running while it does. `shouldDeleteMemory` now takes `isProtected` as an arg (private function, sole caller is the retention loop). (`lib/memory/housekeeping.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-weighting.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — *Run housekeeping now* no longer fails validation**: The button on the Memory Housekeeping card posted to `POST /api/v1/memories?action=housekeep`, but that endpoint's Zod schema requires `characterId` and the card sent an empty body — so every click bounced as a validation error before a single log line could fire. The synchronous per-character handler was the wrong target for a button whose copy (and the help file) promises a background sweep across every character. Added a new `POST /api/v1/memories?action=housekeep-sweep` that wraps `enqueueMemoryHousekeeping(user.id, { reason: 'manual' })` — the existing queue helper already accepts an empty payload as "sweep every character owned by userId" and dedupes against in-flight jobs for the same `(userId, characterId)` pair. The card now hits the new action, so the toast's "Housekeeping job enqueued — it will run in the background" claim is finally true. (`app/api/v1/memories/route.ts`, `components/tools/memory-housekeeping-card.tsx`)
- **Salon — Auto-generated first messages no longer cut off on GLM (and other reasoning models) via OpenRouter**: Two problems compounded in `lib/chat/initial-greeting.ts`. First, the greeting call carried a hard-coded `maxTokens ?? 160` fallback — any connection profile that didn't set `maxTokens` explicitly capped the opener at 160 tokens regardless of the provider's own defaults. Reasoning-capable models like GLM-4.5 / 4.6 spend tokens on hidden "thinking" before producing visible output, so the 160 cap frequently left only a nub of text (or empty content that tripped the content-filter-detection fallback). The `?? 160` is gone; when the profile has no `maxTokens`, the provider's own default (e.g. OpenRouter's 4096) applies. Second, the greeting path went through the provider's non-streaming `sendMessage()` while every other chat turn goes through `streamMessage()`, meaning the greeting used a separate code path with separate quirks. `generateGreetingMessage` now consumes `streamMessage()` and concatenates the chunks server-side; the returned shape (`content`, `contentFilterDetected` — derived from the final chunk's `usage.completionTokens`) is unchanged, and the four-attempt retry / Concierge-reroute chain in `autoGenerateFirstMessage` is untouched. **Follow-up**: the greeting is still assembled server-side and returned as a finished string from `POST /api/v1/chats`; streaming it to the Salon chunk-by-chunk — the way subsequent assistant messages stream — is a pending UI change that will require skipping the inline greeting during chat creation and triggering an SSE turn client-side. (`lib/chat/initial-greeting.ts`, `__tests__/unit/chat-initial-greeting.test.ts`)
- **Salon — Document-mode chats that opened the legacy `physical-prompts.md` no longer error on load**: If a Salon user opened the pre-rename `physical-prompts.md` file in document mode, the `chat_documents` row for that session still pointed at the old filename after the `.md` → `.json` rename shipped, and reopening the chat surfaced a `File not found` error. The vault physical-file startup migration now also sweeps `chat_documents`, rewriting any row whose `filePath` still reads `physical-prompts.md` to `physical-prompts.json` (via a new `ChatDocumentsRepository.renameFilePath()` helper). Idempotent — rerunning is a no-op. (`lib/startup/migrate-vault-physical-files.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/chat-documents.repository.ts`)
- **Salon — "Maximum update depth exceeded" during SSE streaming**: The `storyBackgroundsEnabled` sync effect in `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx` listed the whole `chatControls` return object as a dependency. `useChatControls` returns a plain object literal, so its identity changes on every render. During SSE streaming, each content chunk fires `setWaitingForResponse(false)` / `setStreaming(true)` / `setStreamingContent(fullContent)` from `readSSEStream`, and on each of the resulting renders the effect re-fired, scheduled another `setStoryBackgroundsEnabled` update, and tripped React 19's update-depth tripwire — surfaced in the console at `useSSEStreaming.ts:215` even though that setState was innocent. The effect now destructures `setStoryBackgroundsEnabled` (a stable `useState` setter) and depends on it directly, so the dependency array is fully stable across rapid streaming renders. (`app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`)
- **Salon Document Mode — non-Markdown files now open in a plain monospaced editor instead of a Markdown-normalizing Lexical shell**: Opening `properties.json` (or any non-`.md`/`.markdown` file) from a document store in the Salon used to mount the full Lexical editor with `MarkdownBridgePlugin` and `MarkdownShortcutPlugin`, which serialized every content change back through a Markdown round-trip. For JSON and other structured formats that meant phantom dirty flags after a successful save (Lexical's re-serialization differed from what was written to disk, so a 30 s debounce-autosave would fire with a stale mtime and 409). `DocumentPane` now branches on file extension: Markdown files keep the Lexical path with formatting toolbar; everything else renders a monospaced `<textarea>` with no Lexical composer at all — `onContentChange` moves raw bytes straight between the DOM and `useDocumentMode.contentRef`. The matching change in `useDocumentMode.applyDocumentState` only sets `absorbNextContentChangeRef = true` for Markdown docs, so a plain-text file's first keystroke is treated as a real edit rather than silently adopted as the saved baseline. Status bar now reads "Plain text" instead of "Markdown" for non-Markdown files. (`app/salon/[id]/components/DocumentPane.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useDocumentMode.ts`, `help/scriptorium.md`)
- **Salon Document Mode — character vaults now open from the Salon instead of returning "File not found"**: `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts` threaded only `projectId` into `resolveDocEditPath`, never the chat's participant character IDs. For a character vault that is not independently linked to the active project, `collectAccessibleMountPointIds` consequently saw `character: none` and the resolver rejected every path with `Mount point not found or not accessible` — surfaced in the Salon as `File not found: properties.json` (or whatever path the user clicked) at `parseJsonResponse` in `documentModeApi.ts`. `getChatContext` now pulls every `characterId` off `chat.participants` and `resolveDocumentRequest` passes them through. `PathResolutionContext` grew an optional `characterIds: string[]` alongside the existing `characterId`, and `collectAccessibleMountPointIds` unions both sources before looking up the character's `characterDocumentMountPointId`. Read, write, open, and close handlers all go through the same path and are therefore fixed together. Added a test in `__tests__/unit/app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.test.ts` asserting participant character IDs are forwarded when opening a document_store file. (`lib/doc-edit/path-resolver.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts`)
- **Partial streamed responses are no longer discarded when the upstream connection drops mid-turn — now covering every streaming call site in the orchestrator**: First pass only wrapped the initial `streamMessage` loop at `processMessage` line 1150. In practice, five other loops (tool-unsupported retry, tool-call continuation, agent-mode force-final, text-tool continuation, text-block continuation) can all emit chunks into `streamingState.fullResponse` and then fail mid-stream; an agent-mode turn that triggered tool calls and then lost the Gemini connection on the second stream hit line 1495 (no try/catch) and re-threw without preservation. Refactored the preservation logic into a single closure `preservePartialOnError(error)` defined once at the top of `processMessage` (captures `repos`, `chatId`, `character`, `characterParticipant`, `preGeneratedAssistantMessageId`, `streamingState`) and called from every stream catch block, including the tool-unsupported retry. The closure is idempotent via a `partialPreserved` flag so a single `processMessage` call only writes one preservation message even if nested try/catches unwind through multiple layers. For the two text-tool/text-block continuation loops, the catch reconstructs `streamingState.fullResponse = strippedResponse + continuationResponse` before preserving so the saved message reflects what the user actually watched stream. (`lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts`)
- **Partial streamed responses are no longer discarded when the upstream connection drops mid-turn**: When a provider stream threw — e.g. Gemini's `GoogleProvider.streamMessage` raising `fetch failed` three minutes into a response — the orchestrator's catch block at `orchestrator.service.ts:1305` re-threw without persisting `streamingState.fullResponse`, so everything the user had already watched stream into the Salon vanished along with the error. The non-recoverable error path now checks `streamingState.hasStartedStreaming` and, when partial content was accumulated, normalizes the content-block format, strips the character-name prefix (matching the normal `finalizeMessageResponse` path), appends `{{OOC: stream ended abruptly (<error>)}}`, and writes the result to the DB via `saveAssistantMessage` before re-throwing. The TurnOrchestrator still catches, stops the chain, and pauses the chat, but now there's a saved message the user can edit, delete, or resume from. If nothing streamed before the failure, nothing is preserved — no empty OOC-only shell messages. The delimiter matches the canonical form documented at `help/roleplay-templates-settings.md:325` (`{{OOC: ...}}`); the stale `((OOC here))` examples in `help/roleplay-templates.md` were updated to match. (`lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts`, `help/roleplay-templates.md`)
- **"Agent completed task" banner no longer hangs the Salon when openrouter.ai is slow**: Message finalization used to `await estimateMessageCost()` before emitting the SSE `done` event. For any non-OpenRouter provider (Gemini, Anthropic, OpenAI, Grok, …), cost estimation falls through to `getOpenRouterPricingForModel()`, which calls `fetchOpenRouterPublicPricing()` — an unconditional `fetch('https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/models')` with no timeout. When openrouter.ai is slow or unreachable, that `fetch` stalls on Node's default socket behavior (observed: ~66 seconds in the wild); meanwhile the client sits on the `agent_completed` (or other interim) status event with nothing to clear it, since `useSSEStreaming` only clears `responseStatus` on `done` or `error`. Three layered fixes: (1) the public pricing `fetch` now carries `AbortSignal.timeout(3000)` so it fails fast; (2) failures are negatively cached for 5 minutes (`openRouterPublicFetchFailureAt`) so repeated cost estimates during an outage don't each pay the timeout; (3) cost estimation and token tracking have been moved off the critical path in `finalizeMessageResponse` — the `done` event is emitted first, then `estimateMessageCost` + `trackMessageTokenUsage` run fire-and-forget with their own error handler. The UI now unblocks immediately on turn completion regardless of openrouter.ai's state. (`lib/llm/pricing-fetcher.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/message-finalizer.service.ts`)
- **Character vault backfill no longer blocks startup / stalls the event loop**: Phase 3.2 of `instrumentation.ts` used to `await backfillCharacterVaults()` before continuing, and the backfill itself iterated every unlinked Aurora character tightly — each one ~20-30 synchronous SQLCipher writes — with no yields. On an instance with dozens of unlinked characters, that's hundreds to a couple thousand sync writes back-to-back, which pins the Node event loop long enough to make the running dev server appear hung ("still does things, but comes to a stop"). Phase 3.2 is now fire-and-forget (matches the pattern already used for `scanAllMountPoints` right below it), so the server becomes responsive immediately while vaults materialize in the background. Inside the backfill itself, `await new Promise(setImmediate)` between characters yields to the event loop so the background work doesn't monopolize the main thread either. New vaults are still picked up on the next mount-point scan pass. (`instrumentation.ts`, `lib/startup/backfill-character-vaults.ts`)
- **Database-backed document stores no longer show a spurious "Error — Base path not accessible" on every startup**: `scanAllMountPoints` unconditionally ran `fs.access(mountPoint.basePath)` before dispatching to `scanMountPoint`. Database-backed stores have no filesystem path, so the check failed, the scan was skipped, and `scanStatus` was written as `'error'` with `lastScanError='Base path not accessible: '`. The Scriptorium card then rendered the red *Error* badge indefinitely. The startup runner now skips the accessibility check when `mountType === 'database'` and lets `scanMountPoint` handle the rescan via `rescanDatabaseMountPoint`; on success `updateLastScanned` sets status back to `'idle'` and the badge clears on the next render. (`lib/mount-index/scan-runner.ts`)
- **`doc_create_folder` (and its Phase 3.4 siblings) now dispatches correctly instead of 404'ing through the plugin registry**: `lib/chat/tool-executor.ts` kept its own `BUILT_IN_TOOLS` Set used to gate plugin routing, and it listed only the Phase 3.3 doc tools. When the LLM (or the user) invoked `doc_create_folder`, `doc_move_file`, `doc_delete_file`, `doc_delete_folder`, `doc_move_folder`, or any of the blob tools, the name wasn't recognized as built-in; because plugins were loaded, the executor routed the call to `toolRegistry.executeTool()`, which logged `Tool 'doc_create_folder' not found in any registered plugin` and returned failure before the correct `isDocEditTool` branch ever ran. Unified the two lists: `BUILT_IN_TOOLS` now spreads `DOC_EDIT_TOOL_NAMES` from `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts` (single source of truth), so adding a new `doc_*` tool requires only one edit. (`lib/chat/tool-executor.ts`)
- **`doc_list_files` with `folder: "/"` against a database-backed store no longer returns empty**: `listDatabaseFiles` treated any truthy `folder` as a specific subfolder and ran a prefix match. Stored paths are kept slash-less (`test-root/file.md`), so `folder === "/"` produced the prefix `"/"`, matched nothing, and reported zero files. The folder input is now stripped of leading and trailing slashes before comparison, so `""`, `"/"`, and `"//"` all fall into the "list root" branch and subfolder lookups like `"test-root"` or `"test-root/"` behave identically. Filesystem-backed stores were already fine via `path.join`. (`lib/mount-index/database-store.ts`)
- **Clearer errors when a file tool targets a folder (or vice-versa) on database-backed stores**: `doc_move_file` and `doc_delete_file` used to return a bare "file not found" even when the path resolved to a folder row; `doc_move_folder` and `doc_delete_folder` did the mirror thing for file paths. Each now checks the opposite entity on mismatch and returns a message like `"Path is a folder, not a file: test-root/a/b. Use doc_move_folder to rename or move folders."` New `databaseFolderExists` helper in `database-store.ts`. (`lib/mount-index/database-store.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts`)
- **`doc_delete_folder` / `doc_move_folder` on database-backed stores no longer claim "Folder not found" for paths with a trailing slash**: two different normalizers were in play. `lib/mount-index/folder-paths.ts` strips trailing slashes before inserting into `doc_mount_folders.path` (e.g. `test-root/a/b`), but `lib/mount-index/database-store.ts`'s `normaliseRelativePath` used `path.normalize` which preserves them — so `doc_delete_folder test-root/a/b/` looked up `path = 'test-root/a/b/'` and missed the row. `normaliseRelativePath` now strips the trailing slash too, matching the write-side form. Files/documents/blobs don't carry trailing slashes so nothing else changes. (`lib/mount-index/database-store.ts`)
- **`doc_create_folder` no longer hits a `UNIQUE constraint failed` on the second nested-path call**: same root cause as the `folders.parentFolderId` fix, but in `DocMountFolderSchema.parentId` (`lib/schemas/mount-index.types.ts`). `ensureFolderPath` walks segments root-first and calls `findByMountPointAndPath` to check whether each ancestor already exists. For a root-level ancestor, the stored `parentId` is `NULL`; the SQLite hydrator maps that to `undefined`; and the schema's `.nullable()` (without `.optional()`) then rejected it — so the lookup silently returned `null` via safeQuery fallback. The code assumed the folder didn't exist yet and tried to INSERT, which tripped the `idx_doc_mount_folders_mp_parent_name` UNIQUE index, and the catch-branch re-lookup hit the exact same validation failure. Fixed by making `parentId` `.nullable().optional()` to match every other nullable field in `mount-index.types.ts`. Repro: `doc_create_folder test-root/` (succeeds), then `doc_create_folder test-root/a/` (used to fail, now succeeds idempotently). (`lib/schemas/mount-index.types.ts`)
- **`folders` collection no longer throws `expected string, received undefined` on `parentFolderId` during reads**: the SQLite hydration layer at `lib/database/backends/sqlite/backend.ts:453` converts SQL `NULL` to JS `undefined` for scalar columns (the comment there incorrectly claims this is safe for all schemas). `FolderSchema.parentFolderId` was declared `UUIDSchema.nullable()` — which accepts `null` but rejects `undefined` — so every read of a root-level folder record (all `/story-backgrounds/`, `/character-avatars/`, etc. rows have null parents) failed Zod validation and the repo returned `null`. Dropped find/create calls chained behind that silent failure. `parentFolderId` is now `UUIDSchema.nullable().optional()`, matching the pattern already used by `projectId` in the same schema. No DDL change; existing rows and writes still store SQL NULL. (`lib/schemas/folder.types.ts`)
- **Production build no longer fails with "Module not found: fs/promises" in the Salon bundle**: `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useDocumentMode.ts` is a client hook, but it imported `formatAutosaveNotification` from the `@/lib/doc-edit` barrel. That barrel re-exports `path-resolver` and `reindex-file`, which pull in `fs/promises`, `child_process`, and the SQLite instance lock — all server-only. Turbopack traced the chain into the client graph and aborted with ten module-not-found errors across the Salon and plugin routes. The hook now imports `formatAutosaveNotification` directly from `@/lib/doc-edit/unified-diff` (pure string logic, no Node built-ins), and `npm run build` completes cleanly. (`app/salon/[id]/hooks/useDocumentMode.ts`)
- **`.qtap` export/import is now streaming NDJSON so large exports no longer crash on the V8 string ceiling**: the old pipeline built a single `QuilltapExport` object in memory and called `JSON.stringify(..., null, 2)`, which threw `RangeError: Invalid string length` once a character with ~14k memories pushed the output past V8's ~512 MB max string. The import side had a mirror problem — `await file.text()` plus `JSON.parse` on the whole file plus a hard 100 MB upload cap. The `.qtap` format is now a newline-delimited JSON stream (`{"format":"qtap-ndjson","version":1,"manifest":{...}}` on line 1, tagged per-entity records on each subsequent line, a footer with authoritative counts at the end). Document-store blob bytes are split into ~4 MB base64 chunks so no single record ever approaches the string limit. Export writes the stream straight into the HTTP response; import peeks the first 2 KB to decide between NDJSON and the legacy monolithic path, reads the stream line-by-line, and reassembles the legacy-shape export object the existing import service already understands. Legacy `.qtap` files still import as long as they fit in V8's string budget (~450 MB); anything larger must be re-exported from a current build. Proxy upload cap raised from 500 MB to 10 GB. Frontend now hands the response straight to `response.blob()` instead of re-serializing JSON (which was a matching client-side wall), and skips the full client-side parse for NDJSON files — only the envelope line is parsed. Verified end-to-end with a 1.2 GB export of a character carrying 14,435 memories. (`lib/export/types.ts`, `lib/export/ndjson-writer.ts`, `lib/import/ndjson-reader.ts`, `lib/import/quilltap-import-stream.ts`, `app/api/v1/system/tools/route.ts`, `components/tools/import-export/hooks/useExportData.ts`, `components/tools/import-export/hooks/useImportData.ts`, `next.config.js`, `help/system-import-export.md`)
- **`.qtap` export/import now round-trips project↔mount-point links**: the export payload for document stores did not include the `project_doc_mount_links` join rows, so a project that referenced a Scriptorium mount point lost that reference after a round-trip. The export now collects links for every exported mount point (`ExportedProjectDocMountLink`), and the import remaps both project and mount-point IDs through the existing `idMaps` before re-creating each link. New `documentStoreProjectLinks` count in `QuilltapExportCounts` surfaces the number of links exchanged. Schema updated at `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json` with a new `$def` and optional `projectLinks` array. (`lib/export/quilltap-export-service.ts`, `lib/import/quilltap-import-service.ts`, `lib/export/types.ts`)
- **Scan on database-backed document stores now actually rechunks**: `rescanDatabaseMountPoint` previously only emitted `document-written` events, which fed `enqueueEmbeddingJobsForMountPoint` — but that function only enqueues jobs for *existing* null-embedding chunks. After an import (which creates documents and files but zero chunks) or any direct content change outside the doc-edit pipeline, Scan did nothing and the store stayed unsearchable. The rescan now delegates to `reindexSingleFile()` for any document whose file-record `sha256` has drifted from the document's `contentSha256` (or whose file has no chunks at all), creating fresh null-embedding chunks before emitting the write event. (`lib/mount-index/database-store.ts`)
- **Mount-index database now included in the 24-hour physical backup sweep**: the automatic SQLCipher backup previously covered only `quilltap.db` and `quilltap-llm-logs.db` and silently skipped `quilltap-mount-index.db` — where the Scriptorium keeps every chunk, embedding, and (for database-backed stores) the actual document bodies and blobs. A new `createMountIndexPhysicalBackup()` runs alongside the existing two on startup, uses the same 24-hour interval and retention policy (7 days all, weekly for 4 weeks, monthly for 12 months, yearly forever), and writes to `quilltap-mount-index-YYYY-MM-DDTHHmmss.db` inside `data/backups/`. Restore instructions added to `help/database-protection.md`. (`lib/database/backends/sqlite/physical-backup.ts`, `lib/database/backends/sqlite/backend.ts`)
- **Document Mode — fix open/read/write on database-backed stores**: `handleOpenDocument`, `handleReadDocument`, and `handleWriteDocument` were passing the bare `resolved.absolutePath` string to `readFileWithMtime` / `writeFileWithMtimeCheck`. For database-backed stores that string is empty, so the helpers took the filesystem branch and hit `ENOENT: no such file or directory, open ''`. They now pass the full `ResolvedPath` object, letting the helpers dispatch to `readDatabaseDocument` / `writeDatabaseDocument`. Fixes "Failed to open document" in Document Mode against a database-backed Scriptorium store. (`app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts`)
- **Document Mode save/read races with LLM**: Fixed `Failed to read document content` and `Failed to save document {}` errors triggered by races between the 30s autosave debounce and LLM document tool calls
  - Autosave is now cancelled when the LLM begins editing and skipped while an LLM edit is in flight — eliminates the mtime conflict when the LLM rewrites the file out from under the user
  - Save 409 responses now silently adopt the server's latest content (or just refresh local mtime if the user has unsaved edits) instead of surfacing a scary error
  - `onToolResult` now reloads document state after `doc_write_file`, `doc_move_file`, and `doc_delete_file` (previously only reloaded after open/close), keeping the editor's cached content and mtime in sync with what the LLM wrote to disk
  - Server-side `handleReadDocument` no longer swallows every error as "File not found" — distinguishes missing-file errors (404) from real failures (500) and logs the underlying cause
- **Document Mode false "Unsaved" status after LLM edit**: After the LLM edited a document via tool, the status line incorrectly flipped to "Unsaved" because Lexical's post-remount re-serialization of the refreshed content differed trivially from the disk bytes (whitespace/list formatting normalization). The hook now treats the first content change after a server-driven state load as an external sync and adopts Lexical's normalized output as the saved baseline, so the status correctly shows "Saved" until the user actually types.
- **Scriptorium `read_conversation` tool**: Removed 50,000 character truncation limit that was cutting off the end of long conversations when delivered to LLM participants
- **Document Mode `doc_focus` highlight**: Fixed highlight overlay not appearing — overlay was positioned at pre-scroll viewport coordinates (off-screen) because it was created before smooth scroll completed; now defers to `scrollend` event
- **Document Mode `doc_focus` highlight**: Increased default highlight opacity from 0.35 to 0.95 for better visibility during the 2.5s fade
- **Document Mode `doc_focus` targeting**: Fixed eye icon and highlight overlay resolving their target independently (two lookups that could disagree due to DOM/Lexical node index mismatch); now resolves the Lexical node key once and uses `editor.getElementByKey()` for both consumers
- **Document Mode gutter**: Fixed false change markers appearing on document open by comparing block text content against block text content (instead of raw markdown vs. plain text)
- **Document Mode gutter eye**: Eye icon now positions at the exact pixel offset of the highlighted text, not the top of the containing block — fixes misalignment when highlighting text inside lists
- **Document Mode highlight**: Fixed highlight overlay being invisible — Lexical's MutationObserver was removing overlays appended to the editor root. Overlay is now a fixed-position element on document.body, outside Lexical's DOM tree
- **Document Mode highlight**: Fixed highlighted text vanishing (surroundContents corrupting Lexical's managed DOM) by switching to a non-destructive overlay approach
- **Document Mode highlight**: Fixed case-sensitive text matching — highlight search now uses case-insensitive matching, consistent with block resolution
- **Claude 4.6 compatibility**: Fixed multi-character chat identity anchoring for Claude 4.6 models (Sonnet 4.6, Opus 4.6) which no longer support assistant message prefill. When a model doesn't support prefill, the system prompt is used to instruct the model to self-identify instead.
- Fixed document editor checkboxes not rendering: `CHECK_LIST` transformer was ordered after `UNORDERED_LIST` (whose regex consumed the line first), and Lexical's built-in `match[3] === 'x'` comparison was case-sensitive so `[X]` rendered as unchecked
- Fixed document editor tables not converting between markdown source and rich text: added custom multiline-element transformer for GFM pipe-delimited table syntax with column alignment support
- Fixed chat participant status changes (absent/remove) not updating in the UI under Electron due to Chromium caching stale GET responses; added `cache: 'no-store'` to all chat-related fetch calls in the Salon view
- **Embedding generate OOM fix**: The `EMBEDDING_GENERATE` handler for memories now writes directly to the database via `VectorIndicesRepository` instead of loading the entire character vector store into memory. Previously, generating an embedding for a single memory would load *all* vectors for that character (e.g. 12,000+ entries × 1,536 dimensions ≈ 150+ MB) just to insert one row — causing V8 heap exhaustion and crashes in Electron when processing large instances.
- **Docker/Lima/WSL heap limit raised to 4 GB**: `--max-old-space-size` bumped from 2048 to 4096 in `Dockerfile`, `Dockerfile.ci`, and `lima/wsl-init.sh`
- **Background job queue now respects priority**: `claimNextJob()` sorts by `priority DESC, createdAt ASC` instead of arbitrary order — the `priority` column existed but was never consulted
- **Chat-related embeddings prioritized over batch operations**: Memory and conversation chunk embeddings now enqueue at priority 10, while mount chunk and help doc embeddings enqueue at priority 0, preventing large document store scans from starving real-time chat responsiveness
- **Google plugin (1.1.22)**: Fixed tool/function calling with Google Gemini SDK — uppercase schema `type` fields for API compatibility, switched `userAgentExtra` to `httpOptions.headers` for newer SDK versions, re-enabled function calling for Gemini 3 models, and improved function call extraction from raw responses
- **Memory search dimension mismatch fallback**: When the search embedding profile produces different dimensions than the stored vector index, `searchMemoriesSemantic` now detects the mismatch before calling vector search and falls back to text-based search instead of silently returning zero results
- **Text search fallback broadened to per-word matching**: The text-based memory search fallback now searches for individual significant words (filtering stop words) when the full query phrase doesn't match, so multi-word queries find relevant memories even without exact substring matches
- **Removed per-chat embedding profile override**: The `embeddingProfileId` field in `cheapLLMSettings` was removed — the system now always uses the single default embedding profile for all search operations, preventing mismatches between the profile used to build the vector index and the one used at search time
- **Tasks Queue UI**: The paused-jobs count was never shown in the queue stats panel because the API response omitted the `paused` field — it is now included.
- **Tasks Queue UI**: Jobs of type `SCENE_STATE_TRACKING`, `CHARACTER_AVATAR_GENERATION`, and `CONVERSATION_RENDER` appeared as raw type identifiers instead of human-readable names; they now display correctly.
- **Tasks Queue UI**: Non-LLM background jobs (embedding generation, vocabulary refit, re-index, avatar generation, conversation render, and story background generation) were incorrectly contributing 500 estimated tokens each to the queue token estimate; they now correctly contribute 0.
- **Tasks Queue UI**: The `ProcessorStatus` type now includes `embeddingInFlight` and `embeddingConcurrency` to match what the API actually returns.
- **Embedding model swap dimension mismatch**: Full re-embed (EMBEDDING_REINDEX_ALL) now clears each character's vector index before enqueuing new jobs, so switching to a model with different dimensions (e.g. 1536 → 4096) no longer fails every job with "Vector dimension mismatch"
- **Stale embedding jobs on re-embed**: Re-embed now cancels all pending/failed/orphaned EMBEDDING_GENERATE jobs from the previous run before enqueuing fresh ones, preventing zombie jobs from competing for processor slots
- **Slow re-embed enqueue**: Reindex handler now batch-inserts all embedding jobs in chunks of 200 (single SQLite transactions) instead of 3 sequential DB calls per entity — enqueue phase drops from minutes to seconds for large instances
- **Orphaned PROCESSING jobs blocking new work**: On startup, all PROCESSING jobs are now killed (DEAD) instead of reset to PENDING, since no job can legitimately be mid-flight at server start. Prevents stale retries from blocking fresh batch-inserted jobs. Embedding concurrency also guards against over-claiming via early bail when slots are full, with proactive back-fill when a slot frees.
- **Embedding BLOB Registration**: Fixed race condition where memory embeddings could be stored as JSON text instead of Float32 BLOBs, causing dimension mismatches during vector search. BLOB columns for `memories`, `vector_entries`, and `conversation_chunks` are now registered at database initialization time rather than lazily in individual repositories.

- **Debug logging cleanup**: Removed 14 `console.debug` calls added during 4.3-dev work that are no longer needed: `DocumentFocusPlugin` (useEffect fired, clearing focus, resolved target node, eye position, scroll path), `DocumentChangeTracker` (baseline captured, block diff, no root element, DOM measurement), `useDocumentMode` (handleDocFocus), `useNewChat` (creating chat), `clipboard-utils` (Clipboard API success/fallback/Electron IPC — also cleaned up the unused `browserErr` catch binding). The structured `logger.debug(...)` calls on the server side (mount points, document mode API, conversation render, etc.) are retained; they are gated by `LOG_LEVEL`. (`app/salon/[id]/components/DocumentFocusPlugin.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/components/DocumentChangeTracker.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useDocumentMode.ts`, `components/new-chat/hooks/useNewChat.ts`, `lib/clipboard-utils.ts`)

- **Per-phase timing instrumentation on chat-turn context build**: After Phases 1 and 2 of the memory retrieval performance plan, the Friday instance (~20k memories on one character) still showed multi-minute main-thread pins between the compression-cache-hit log line and any subsequent context-build log line, with zero activity in between to tell us which phase was slow. Added `logger.debug`-level wall-clock timings at the phases we have reason to suspect: the parallel compression + proactive-recall `await Promise.all` in `lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts`, the `buildMessageContext` call right after, and inside `buildContext` in `lib/chat/context-manager.ts` — `buildSystemPrompt`, the `countMessagesTokens` conversation pass, the per-character memory retrieval + format block (reports which path was taken: pre-searched, semantic-search, or skipped), and the inter-character memory retrieval block (multi-character chats only). `searchMemoriesSemantic` itself also emits a single `[Memory] Semantic search timings` line per call, breaking total wall time into embed, vector-search, and hydrate-plus-rank components. All logs are `debug` — invisible at the default `info` level, so there's no noise cost in normal operation, and a user chasing a stall can flip the log level at runtime to see where a chat turn is actually spending its time. The pattern matches the existing `[ContextManager]` and `[Memory]` log prefix convention so the entries sort together in log viewers. (`lib/memory/memory-service.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts`, `lib/chat/context-manager.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — vector search no longer sorts the entire index on every query**: On the Friday instance, the Phase 1 fix (`perf(memory): hydrate only matched memories in semantic search paths`) removed SQLCipher + Zod as the per-turn cost but exposed the next bottleneck: `CharacterVectorStore.search` in `lib/embedding/vector-store.ts` was pushing all 20k entries into a flat `VectorSearchResult[]`, then calling `Array.prototype.sort` with a user comparator, then slicing to `limit`. A `sample(1)` against a pinned `next-server` (100% CPU, silent log for 2+ minutes on a fresh chat turn) showed the entire main-thread stack under `Builtins_ArrayPrototypeSort` → `Builtins_ArrayTimSort` → `Builtins_MergeAt` → `Builtins_SortCompareUserFn` — the cost of a JS-comparator sort at 20k × called-per-agent-mode-sub-turn was pinning the event loop for minutes. `search` now routes to one of two paths: for small corpora (< 1000 entries or `limit * 4 >= entries.size`), the original linear scan + sort is retained — the heap's bookkeeping isn't worth it under that threshold; above it, a new hand-rolled bounded min-heap of size `limit` keeps only the top-K candidates during the scan, skipping the `VectorSearchResult` allocation entirely for any entry whose score can't beat the current worst. The heap is two parallel arrays (scores + results) so the hot `sift` comparison reads a primitive number, which matters because sift runs O(log k) per candidate across n entries. Output contract is unchanged: same top-K by score descending, same metadata, same dimension-mismatch fallback; tie-break order between entries with identical scores is not stable across paths (and was never contractually stable — V8's sort is stable but the heap's isn't, and neither matters for ranking semantics). Two parity tests added: a 5000-entry pseudorandom-unit-vector test asserting the heap and linear paths return identical score sequences, and a small-corpus test confirming the linear fallback still runs below the threshold. (`lib/embedding/vector-store.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/embedding/vector-store.test.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — semantic memory retrieval no longer decrypts the whole corpus per chat turn**: Three hot paths in `lib/memory/memory-service.ts` — `searchMemoriesSemantic` (line 515), `findSimilarMemories` (line 711), and `findSimilarMemoriesWithEmbedding` (line 749) — were each calling `repos.memories.findByCharacterId(characterId)` to hydrate the top-K vector matches. That function decrypts and Zod-validates *every* memory row for the character in one synchronous pass, just to pluck ~60 hits out of a Map. On a character with ~20k memories, every chat turn paid 20k `MemorySchema.parse` calls and 20k SQLCipher row decrypts on the main thread — visible in the Salon as freezes during LLM turns and `Failed to fetch` on `/api/v1/session` and other concurrent requests. Each call site now does `findByIds(vectorResults.map(r => r.id))` instead, mirroring the pattern the Memory Gate write path (`lib/memory/memory-gate.ts:161`) has used since 4.3. Per-turn retrieval cost now scales with *hit count* rather than corpus size: on a 20k-memory character, the worst of the three reads drops from 20k decrypted-and-validated rows to ~60. No change to returned memory set, ranking, filter semantics, or dimension-mismatch fallback behavior. `generateMissingEmbeddings` (line 781) and `rebuildVectorIndex` (line 852) still do full scans — they legitimately need the whole corpus (the former filters for null embeddings; the latter rebuilds the whole index) and are cold paths not on the chat turn hot path. (`lib/memory/memory-service.ts`)
