- **Commonplace Book — no-embedding-no-write gate, raised thresholds, and a near-duplicate skip tier**: Three interlocking changes to the Memory Gate, driven by the same Friday-instance audit: of 32,364 memories, 13,174 (41%) had `NULL` embeddings and were therefore invisible to every future gate check, letting phrase-variant duplicates like `"Sunny wears teal glasses."` accumulate ten literal copies. (1) When the gate can't generate an embedding for a candidate, it now retries once after a 500 ms delay and, on second failure, returns a new `SKIP_EMBEDDING_FAILED` decision instead of falling through to the old keyword-overlap gate. No row is written, because a row without an embedding is a permanent dedup hole. The `keywordBasedGate` fallback function has been deleted outright — it was the sole producer of those NULL-embedding rows and its lone caller has been replaced. (2) A new `NEAR_DUPLICATE_THRESHOLD = 0.90` tier sits above the existing merge band: candidates whose best vector-search neighbor scores at or above 0.90 now resolve to a new `SKIP_NEAR_DUPLICATE` decision that neither inserts nor reinforces — the observation is absorbed silently into the existing memory. (3) `MERGE_THRESHOLD` rises from 0.80 to 0.85 so reinforcement is reserved for genuinely duplicate-enough matches rather than merely very-similar ones; the 0.70–0.85 band now produces `INSERT_RELATED` (was 0.70–0.80). `MemoryGateOutcome.memory` is now `Memory | null` to carry the SKIP states, and `createMemoryWithEmbedding` (the manual POST path) returns `null` on `SKIP_EMBEDDING_FAILED` so the API surfaces a clear 500 rather than silently no-op'ing. The three switch blocks in `processMessageForMemory` and `processInterCharacterMemory` handle both SKIP actions with distinct debug-log markers so the per-message `debugMemoryLogs` can distinguish "skipped for similarity" from "skipped because embedding failed." (`lib/memory/memory-gate.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-service.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-processor.ts`, `lib/memory/index.ts`, `app/api/v1/memories/route.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/memory-gate.test.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/memory-processor-regression.test.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — hard candidate cap and targeted gate lookup**: Two compounding fixes along the memory-write path, motivated by a Friday-instance audit that found 32k memories on one instance with 7,717 added in a single day and individual messages producing up to 88 memory rows. (1) `parseMemoryCandidateArray` now slices significant candidates to `HARD_CANDIDATE_CAP = 5` after the significance filter, and each call site derives `maxMemories` through `resolveMaxMemories()` which clamps the prior `Math.ceil(resolvedMaxTokens / 8000)` formula to the same ceiling — so a 128K-output cheap-LLM profile is told in the prompt to return at most 5 and *also* can't slip more past the parser if it ignores the instruction. Defense-in-depth across the three extraction paths (user memories, character-self memories, inter-character memories). (2) The Memory Gate's pre-write similarity check previously called `repos.memories.findByCharacterId(characterId)` to resolve the top-5 vector-search hits into full `Memory` rows — an O(N) scan on every single insert that loads 20K rows just to `.get()` five of them. A new repository method `findByIds(ids: string[])` runs a targeted `WHERE id IN (...)` filter through the existing `findByFilter` abstraction, and the gate now passes only `results.map(r => r.id)` into it. Net effect on a character with 20K memories: the per-insert read drops from a full-table scan to a five-row primary-key lookup, with identical dedup semantics. (`lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks/memory-tasks.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-gate.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/memories.repository.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks.test.ts`)
- **Memory extraction — async via the existing background-job queue**: Memory extraction (single-character, inter-character, and user-controlled-character) was previously inlined in `finalizeMessageResponse`, holding the request open for 30–40 s of serial Ollama embedding work after the SSE `done` event had already been sent — which made the next chat turn feel like it was still chewing on the previous one. The chat path now enqueues `MEMORY_EXTRACTION` and `INTER_CHARACTER_MEMORY` jobs (one per observer→subject pair) instead of awaiting `processMessageForMemoryAsync` directly. The job types, handlers, and the **Mem** badge in `<QueueStatusBadges />` already existed and were just unused for this path; the work now drains in the background and surfaces in the header counter so it's visible. The handler grew the missing `userCharacterName`, `characterPronouns`, `allCharacterNames`, and `allCharacterPronouns` payload fields so the worker has the same context the inline trigger had, plus a token-tracking `createMemoryExtractionEvent` emit that previously lived in the trigger callback. (`lib/services/chat-message/memory-trigger.service.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/queue-service.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/memory-extraction.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/inter-character-memory.ts`)
- **Memory extraction — halve the per-call candidate cap**: Each chat turn now extracts at most `ceil(maxTokens / 8000)` memory candidates per extraction call, down from `ceil(maxTokens / 4000)`. For a 32K-context cheap-LLM profile that drops the per-call ceiling from 8 to 4; for an 8K profile (the default fallback) the ceiling drops from 2 to 1. Extraction still runs three calls per turn (user-memories, character-self-memories, inter-character-memories), but a multi-character chat that previously fanned out 30–40 memory writes per turn — each of which serialises an Ollama embedding ~1 s — should now do roughly half that work without losing the salient items, since the LLM was already prioritising significance and just had headroom to over-collect. (`lib/memory/cheap-llm-tasks/memory-tasks.ts`)
- **Vector search — Float32Array, unit-vector cosine, and a mount-chunk cache**: Three compounding fixes along the embedding hot path, motivated by a Friday-instance chat turn that stalled on the order of a minute after "Loading tools for Friday…". (1) `blobToEmbedding` no longer boxes each Float32 BLOB into a `number[]` of doubles on read — it returns a proper `Float32Array`, and that type now flows end-to-end through `EmbeddingResult`, every embedding-carrying Zod schema (`memories`, `conversation_chunks`, `doc_mount_chunks`, `help_docs`, `vector_entries`), every `updateEmbedding`/`addEntries` repository signature, and every `cosineSimilarity` call site. Same BLOB on disk, four-times-less RAM and sharply tighter JIT loops in memory. (2) All stored embeddings are now L2-normalised at write time inside the single choke-point `generateEmbeddingForUser`, so `cosineSimilarity(a, b)` reduces to a single-pass dot product — no per-comparison `Math.sqrt` calls. The new migration `normalize-embeddings-unit-vectors-v1` walks every embedding in the main DB and the mount-index DB, normalizing any non-unit vector in place (idempotent — re-running skips vectors already within 1e-4 of unit length). (3) A new `lib/mount-index/mount-chunk-cache.ts` keeps embedded document-mount chunks resident in process memory keyed by mount point, mirroring the shape of `VectorStoreManager`. Loading is lazy on first search; invalidation fires when a chunk is re-embedded (`handleMountChunkEmbedding`), chunks are deleted (`deleteByFileId` / `deleteByMountPointId`), or an embedding reindex is enqueued. `searchDocumentChunks` consumes the cache instead of re-decoding thousands of BLOBs on every turn. (4) `GET /api/v1/mount-points` no longer hydrates every embedded chunk across every store just to populate `embeddedChunkCount` in the Scriptorium settings UI — a new `countEmbeddedByMountPointIds` runs a single `GROUP BY` query instead. Net effect on the observed slowdown: the per-turn mount-chunk decode drops from ~1 s + 33 M multiplies-plus-sqrts to a cache hit + one dot-product pass. (`lib/embedding/embedding-service.ts`, `lib/database/backends/sqlite/json-columns.ts`, `lib/database/backends/sqlite/query-translator.ts`, `lib/schemas/{memory,scriptorium,mount-index,vector-indices,help-doc}.types.ts`, `lib/help-search.types.ts`, `lib/embedding/vector-store.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-service.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-gate.ts`, `lib/mount-index/document-search.ts`, `lib/mount-index/mount-chunk-cache.ts`, `lib/scriptorium/conversation-search.ts`, `lib/help-search.ts`, `lib/tools/memory-dedup.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/{doc-mount-chunks,conversation-chunks,help-docs,vector-indices}.repository.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/{embedding-generate,embedding-reindex}.ts`, `app/api/v1/mount-points/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/mount-points/[id]/route.ts`, `migrations/scripts/normalize-embeddings-unit-vectors.ts`, `migrations/scripts/index.ts`)

added Lima VM and WSL2 rows to the database paths table; removed the stale "or S3" reference under File Storage; expanded the Plugin Formats list with Embedding Providers and Search Providers and the full LLM provider set. `docs/developer/API.md`: added a v4.3-dev freshness banner enumerating the major drift points (Mount Points routes, the consolidated chat-actions list, the new `doc_*` / `self_inventory` / `state` / `whisper` tools, retired `file_management`, the `systemSender` enum, the character `systemTransparency` field); #### Features & Improvements

- **`self_inventory` now opens by telling the character which Quilltap version they are running on**: First line of the formatted report is `You are running on Quilltap v<version>.` (same `package.json` version that drives the page footer in `components/footer-wrapper.tsx`), so a character invoking the introspection tool sees the build number before any other section. New `quilltapVersion: string` field on `SelfInventoryToolOutput` populated in `lib/tools/handlers/self-inventory-handler.ts` from `import packageJson from '@/package.json'` and set on the success path plus both error returns (missing characterId, character not found); the formatter prepends the line both for successful reports and for the error short-circuit. Also surfaced as a structured field on the `self_inventory` `ToolResult` next to `formattedText`/`vault`/`vaultAccess` etc. in `lib/chat/tool-executor.ts`. (`lib/tools/self-inventory-tool.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/self-inventory-handler.ts`, `lib/chat/tool-executor.ts`)

- **Salon — Prospero now announces connection-profile changes made from the Participants sidebar**: When the user reassigns a chat participant to a different connection profile, Prospero posts a synthetic ASSISTANT-role message recording the participant's name, the new profile, and the old one — same shape as the Host add/remove/status-change announcements. New writer at `lib/services/prospero-notifications/writer.ts` (`postProsperoConnectionProfileChangeAnnouncement`, mirroring the Host writer's never-propagate error semantics). `handleParticipantUpdate` in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts` captures the participant's old `connectionProfileId` from the pre-fetch, and after a successful `updateParticipant` call it fires the announcement when `participantData.connectionProfileId` was provided in the update and differs from the old value, looking up the character name and both profiles' display names via `repos.characters.findById` / `repos.connections.findById`. The fire happens before the `controlledBy` early-return branch so it covers updates that also flip `controlledBy`. `getMessageAvatar` in `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx` gained a `prospero` branch returning `{ name: 'Prospero', avatarUrl: '/images/avatars/prospero-avatar.webp' }`. The `systemSender` enum already included `'prospero'` from the original Lantern fix; the inline-comment description in `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts` and `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json` was updated from "reserved for upcoming agent announcements" to its current responsibility. CLAUDE.md's per-sender responsibilities list and `help/chat-participants.md` (new "Announcements from Prospero" subsection) updated to match. Like Host announcements, the message is posted unconditionally — character-side filtering happens at context-build time per the existing `systemTransparency` rules. (`lib/services/prospero-notifications/writer.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`, `CLAUDE.md`, `help/chat-participants.md`)

- **Settings — new chats can now default to composition mode**: Added a `compositionModeDefault` boolean to chat settings (default `false`) and a corresponding "Composition Mode" card at the top of the Chat tab in `/settings`, above Token Display. When enabled, new chats are created with `documentEditingMode: true`, so Enter inserts a newline and Ctrl/Cmd+Enter submits; when disabled (the previous behavior), new chats start in chat mode. The per-chat composer toggle still wins after creation — this is just the seed value. Backed by a new SQLite column on `chat_settings` (migration `add-composition-mode-default-field-v1`, INTEGER default 0). Also fixed a long-standing bug where the per-chat composition-mode toggle did not survive a page reload: the value was persisted to the `chats` row by the PUT handler but `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/get.ts` cherry-picks fields into its response object and was never including `documentEditingMode`, so on reload the salon page received `undefined` and the sync effect in `useChatControls` left the local state at its `useState(false)` initial value. The GET response now exposes `documentEditingMode`, so the toggle is sticky across navigations and refreshes. (`lib/schemas/settings.types.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/chat-settings.repository.ts`, `migrations/scripts/add-composition-mode-default-field.ts`, `migrations/scripts/index.ts`, `app/api/v1/settings/chat/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/get.ts`, `components/settings/chat-settings/types.ts`, `components/settings/chat-settings/hooks/useChatSettings.ts`, `components/settings/chat-settings/CompositionModeDefaultSettings.tsx`, `components/settings/tabs/ChatTabContent.tsx`, `docs/developer/DDL.md`, `help/chat-settings.md`)

- **Salon — characters now see a "Recent Conversations" recap on their first turn of every new chat**: The memory recap injected at the start of a chat (under `## What You Remember`) gained a `### Recent Conversations` block listing the title, ID, and `contextSummary` of up to N prior chats with the same character, sorted by `lastMessageAt` desc. This fires in two places: (1) on the auto-generated opening greeting at chat creation (`autoGenerateFirstMessage` → `generateGreetingMessage` via the new `recentConversationsBlock` field on `GreetingRequest`, computed once and reused across all four retry attempts), and (2) on the character's first generated response to the user (`context-manager.ts` → `generateMemoryRecap`, threading `budgetInfo.maxContext` through). N scales linearly with the model's `maxContext`: clamped at 5 for `maxContext ≤ 4K`, 20 for `≥ 32K`, rounded between. The current chat is excluded from the query (defensive: it has no summary at creation, but a recap on character-join could otherwise echo back the in-progress chat's summary). Filter, sort, and limit are pushed to SQL via a new `findRecentSummarizedByCharacter(characterId, { limit, excludeChatId })` repo method; the participant JSON-array filter is the bottleneck at scale (a `chat_participants` join table would be the right next step if this moves to a per-message hot path). The `### Recent Conversations` block is injected purely as data (no LLM call), so the only added latency on the existing recap path is one indexed-but-JSON-filtered SQL query. (`lib/memory/memory-recap.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/chats.repository.ts`, `lib/chat/context-manager.ts`, `lib/chat/initial-greeting.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/route.ts`)

- **Context-summary trigger threshold lowered from 50 to 20 USER+ASSISTANT messages**: `shouldSummarizeConversation` in `lib/llm/model-context-data.ts` now requests a summary when the filtered conversation message count exceeds 20 (was 50). The 60% token-usage rule is unchanged. This was the prerequisite for the Recent Conversations block above: on large-context models (Anthropic 200K, Google 1M), the token rule almost never trips for normal-length chats, so the message-count rule is what determines whether a chat gets a `contextSummary` to feed into recaps. Existing chats with 21–50 messages and no `contextSummary` will start generating one on their next message exchange. (`lib/llm/model-context-data.ts`)

- **Aurora — character vault wardrobe is now a folder of Markdown files**: When `readPropertiesFromDocumentStore` is on, the wardrobe is projected into `Wardrobe/<title>.md` (one file per item) and `Outfits/<name>.md` (one file per preset) instead of a single `wardrobe.json` blob. Item frontmatter carries `id`, `title`, `types`, optional `appropriateness`, the `default` flag, `archived`/`archivedAt`, and timestamps; the body is the freeform description. Preset frontmatter carries `id`, `name`, a four-slot `slots` map (slug-keyed, with raw UUIDs accepted as a fallback), and timestamps; the body is whatever notes you'd like. Hand-edits no longer require generating a UUID — drop a new file with `title:` and `types:`, save, and the next sync fills in the id and timestamps. New helpers in `lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts` (`slugifyWardrobeTitle`, `buildSlugByItemIdMap`, `buildWardrobeItemFile`, `buildOutfitPresetFile`, plus `CHARACTER_WARDROBE_FOLDER` / `CHARACTER_OUTFITS_FOLDER`) and `lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts` (`parseWardrobeItemFile`, `parseOutfitPresetFile`, `projectVaultWardrobe`, `parseLegacyWardrobeJson`). `readCharacterVaultWardrobe` now reads `Wardrobe/` + `Outfits/` first and falls back to legacy `wardrobe.json` when those folders are empty, so vaults that haven't been migrated yet still surface their items on read. The `outfit` placeholder field — written as nulls by the previous format and never consumed — is dropped entirely. Character scaffold seeds the empty `Wardrobe/` and `Outfits/` folders instead of an empty `wardrobe.json`. Startup migration in `lib/startup/refresh-vault-wardrobe.ts` projects every linked vault into the new layout and deletes the legacy JSON, gated by a fresh `wardrobe_folder_migrated_v1` instance-settings flag. Existing tests updated; `help/character-editing.md` and `help/mount-points.md` rewritten to describe the new layout. (`lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts`, `lib/mount-index/character-scaffold.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/wardrobe.repository.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/outfit-presets.repository.ts`, `lib/startup/refresh-vault-wardrobe.ts`, `instrumentation.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/components/CharacterBasicInfo.tsx`, `help/character-editing.md`, `help/mount-points.md`)
- **Salon — the Concierge now announces in chat when he marks a conversation as Dangerous**: When the chat-level danger classifier flips `isDangerousChat` from null/false to true, a synthetic ASSISTANT-role message authored by the Concierge (`participantId: null`, `systemSender: 'concierge'`) is posted into the chat so every character at the table (those who can see the Staff) knows the conversation has been routed to more appropriate providers. The wording is deliberately discreet — "The Concierge, with his customary discretion, has stepped quietly to the table. He has arranged for the present conversation — and any adjunct errands it may occasion — to be entrusted to a desk better appointed to subjects of its particular character. No interruption is required; pray continue at your leisure." — and avoids naming categories or scores in the visible body. New writer at `lib/services/concierge-notifications/writer.ts` (mirrors the Librarian/Host/Lantern writers' error-swallowing pattern: announcements never propagate failures), with `postConciergeDangerAnnouncement` and a `buildDangerContent` helper. The hook lives in `lib/background-jobs/handlers/chat-danger-classification.ts` immediately after the `repos.chats.update({ isDangerousChat: result.isDangerous, ... })` call — guarded by `if (result.isDangerous)` and relying on the existing sticky-true early-return at the top of the handler so the announcement fires exactly once per chat. Sender enum widened from `['lantern', 'aurora', 'librarian', 'prospero', 'host']` to include `'concierge'` in `MessageEventSchema` (`lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`), `ChatMessageRowSchema` (`lib/database/repositories/chats-messages.ops.ts`), the Salon-page `Message.systemSender` literal (`app/salon/[id]/types.ts`), and the export schema (`public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`); SQLite stores `systemSender` as free-form TEXT so no migration is needed. `getMessageAvatar` in `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx` gained a `concierge` case that resolves to the existing `public/images/avatars/concierge-avatar.webp` (already bundled). Opaque characters (those without `systemTransparency`) continue to have Concierge messages filtered out of their LLM context by the existing context-builder Staff filter — no new transparency wiring needed. Help text in `help/dangerous-content.md` gained an "In-Chat Announcement" subsection under Chat-Level Classification. (`lib/services/concierge-notifications/writer.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/chat-danger-classification.ts`, `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/chats-messages.ops.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/types.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`, `help/dangerous-content.md`)
- **Salon — the Host now announces participant adds, removes, and active/silent/absent state changes in chat**: Adding a character to a chat (including reactivating a previously-removed participant), removing a character, and switching a character's status among `active`/`silent`/`absent` now post a synthetic ASSISTANT-role chat message authored by the Host (`role: 'ASSISTANT'`, `participantId: null`, `systemSender: 'host'`) so both the user and the other LLM characters see the change as part of normal conversation history. Add announcements include the joining character's avatar (inline `![name](avatarUrl)` markdown) and either their identity (read from the character vault's `identity.md` when `characterDocumentMountPointId` is set and the file is non-empty) or their `description` field — preferring identity, never both, neither if neither is present. Remove and status-switch announcements are text-only. Status changes that target `removed` are routed to the remove announcement instead of a status switch (the user-facing event is "they left"); the existing `STATUS_CHANGE` SystemEvent (which feeds `statusChangeNotifications` into the per-turn LLM prompt) is left in place untouched, so this change is additive — the Host message is the visible signal, the SystemEvent is the contextual injection. New `lib/services/host-notifications/writer.ts` (mirrors the Librarian writer's error-swallowing pattern: announcements never propagate failures), with `postHostAddAnnouncement`, `postHostRemoveAnnouncement`, `postHostStatusChangeAnnouncement`. `getMessageAvatar` in `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx` gained a `host` case that resolves to the existing `public/images/avatars/host-avatar.webp`. `ChatMessageRowSchema.systemSender` in `lib/database/repositories/chats-messages.ops.ts` was widened from `['lantern', 'aurora']` to the full `['lantern', 'aurora', 'librarian', 'prospero', 'host']` enum already present in `MessageEventSchema`, so SQLite no longer rejects librarian/host writes. The Salon-page `Message.systemSender` literal in `app/salon/[id]/types.ts` was widened to match. Hooks live in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/participants.ts` (add and remove paths, including the soft-removed reactivation branch in `handleAddParticipantAction`) and `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts` (status-change branch in `handleParticipantUpdate`, both the explicit-`status` branch and the legacy-`isActive` backward-compat branch). Opaque characters (those without `systemTransparency`) continue to have Host messages filtered out of their LLM context by the existing context-builder Staff filter — no new transparency wiring needed. (`lib/services/host-notifications/writer.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/chats-messages.ops.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/types.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/participants.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/helpers.ts`)
- **Salon — wardrobe changes now produce a debounced Aurora announcement instead of a manual "Notify" button**: The composer's "Notify 👗" pill, the `useOutfitNotification` localStorage hook, and the ` ```wardrobe ` fenced-block insertion are gone. Outfit changes from any source — sidebar equip/unequip, gift-with-equip-now (which calls the same equip API), and the LLM `update_outfit_item` tool (including preset application and unequip) — now schedule a debounced Aurora system message visible to everyone in the chat (`role: 'ASSISTANT'`, `participantId: null`, `systemSender: 'aurora'`). The message body is plain Markdown built from `describeOutfit()` ("Aurora notes that {char}'s wardrobe has been duly attended to. {char} is presently turned out as follows:" + the per-slot bullets) — no backticks, no fenced block. Debounce is 60 seconds and is implemented as a new `WARDROBE_OUTFIT_ANNOUNCEMENT` background job, keyed by `(chatId, characterId)`: each subsequent change inside the window updates the existing pending job's `scheduledAt` rather than enqueuing a duplicate, so fiddling with all four slots collapses to a single announcement once the user (or the LLM) stops touching the closet. New helper `enqueueWardrobeOutfitAnnouncement` in `lib/background-jobs/queue-service.ts` and new handler in `lib/background-jobs/handlers/wardrobe-announcement.ts` (re-uses `repos.chats.addMessage` for persistence and `describeOutfit` for the bullet list). Server-side `pendingOutfitNotifications` (the orchestrator's per-turn context-injection map) is left untouched — it remains as the LLM-context delivery channel and is independent of the user-visible announcement. (`lib/schemas/job.types.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/queue-service.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/wardrobe-announcement.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/index.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/outfit.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/wardrobe-update-outfit-handler.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/components/ChatComposer.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/index.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useOutfitNotification.ts` (deleted), `app/styles/qt-components/_chat.css`)
- **Salon — Librarian-attached images now carry a generated text description for non-vision providers, cached on the blob**: The just-shipped Librarian attach path delivered image bytes to vision-capable providers correctly (the assistant-side attachment walker → mount-aware `loadChatFilesForLLM` → resize-and-encode pipeline), but the message body itself was a one-liner — "the user has bid the Librarian set the illustration upon the table" — so non-vision providers in the chat saw the announcement, no image, and no description, and silently dropped the contents. Now `handleAttachMountFile` in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/files/route.ts` runs a new `ensureImageDescription` helper before posting the announcement: when the blob's MIME starts with `image/` and `doc_mount_blobs.description` is empty, it reads the blob bytes via `repos.docMountBlobs.readData`, builds a `FileAttachment`, and calls the existing `generateImageDescription` from `lib/chat/file-attachment-fallback.ts` against the user's configured `chatSettings.imageDescriptionProfileId` (with the same vision-capable-fallback-profile selection rule the message-attachment fallback already uses). The result is persisted via `repos.docMountBlobs.updateDescription` so the description is only generated once per blob — re-attaches in the same chat or any other chat reuse it for free, and the same field is now available to any future `doc_*` tool that wants to read it. The description threads into a new optional `description` field on `LibrarianAttachAnnouncement`; `buildAttachContent` splices it into the announcement body as a second paragraph ("The Librarian's catalogue describes the illustration thus: ..."), so the text appears in conversation history exactly once and stays in front of every subsequent character turn (vision providers still get the bytes too, harmlessly redundant). Non-image blobs and image blobs whose description-generation fails fall back to the original one-liner. Lantern image announcements are deliberately left alone — their announcement text already names the prompt that produced the image, so they have a description-by-proxy in conversation history. (`app/api/v1/chats/[id]/files/route.ts`, `lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts`)
- **Salon — pin a Scriptorium document or image to the next character turn via a Librarian announcement (fixes broken "attach from document store" path)**: The chat composer's **+ Attach** menu opens `LibraryFilePickerModal`, which already browses both legacy library files and database-backed Scriptorium document stores via `FileBrowser`'s mount-mode. Attempting to attach a file from a document store had been throwing — the picker was POSTing the `doc_mount_files.id` to `POST /api/v1/chats/{id}/files?action=link`, whose `repos.files.findById(fileId)` returns `null` for any id outside the legacy `files` table, producing a 404 surfaced as a generic "Failed to link file `{}`" in the console. Rather than back-filling the legacy link path with two storage models or copying bytes out of the Scriptorium on attach, mount-mode files now flow through a separate, native path: the picker detects `mountPointId` + `relativePath` on the picked `FileInfo` and POSTs to a new `?action=attach-mount-file` action whose handler resolves the `doc_mount_files` row, looks up the matching `doc_mount_blobs` metadata, and posts a Librarian announcement message via a new `postLibrarianAttachAnnouncement` writer. The synthetic message carries the `doc_mount_files.id` as the only entry in `MessageEvent.attachments`, so the existing assistant-side attachment walker (`collectLanternImageFileIdsForCharacter` in `lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts` — keeping its name despite now also surfacing Librarian attachments, since the structural test "ASSISTANT message with attachments since the character's last turn" was already generic) picks it up on the next character's turn and feeds it into `loadChatFilesForLLM`. The resolver in `lib/chat-files-v2.ts` was extended with a `loadMountFileAsAttachment` helper: each id in `loadChatFilesForLLM` is probed against `repos.files.findById` first, and on miss falls through to `repos.docMountFiles.findById` → `repos.docMountBlobs.findByMountPointAndPath` → `readData(blobId)`, applying the same `resizeImageForProvider` pipeline so vision-provider base64 ceilings still apply. The two id spaces are disjoint random UUIDs so the probe order is safe with no discriminator. Because the bytes are resolved at LLM-call time (not snapshotted at attach), edits made in Document Mode after pinning flow through to the next character turn for free — the same property that made the existing Librarian save announcements useful. Reads paths union mount-file attachments alongside the legacy ones in two places: `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/get.ts` (per-message attachment list — extended `event.attachments` is scanned for any id not covered by `findByLinkedTo(messageId)` and resolved via `docMountFiles` → `docMountBlobs`, producing the standard `MessageAttachment` shape with `filepath` pointing at `/api/v1/mount-points/{mpId}/blobs/{relativePath}`) and `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/files/route.ts` GET (chat-wide attachments tray — walks `repos.chats.getMessages(chatId)` and folds in any mount-file attachments not already present in the legacy `findByLinkedTo(chatId)` results, with a new `'mountFile'` entry in the result `type` union next to `'chatFile'` and `'generatedImage'`). The picker received an `onMountFileAttached?: () => void` prop separate from `onFileLinked` since the attach path is announcement-driven (no composer-tray hand-off) — the salon page wires it to `fetchChat()` so the new Librarian message and its attachment appear immediately. `postLibrarianMessage` in `lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts` gained an optional `attachments: string[] = []` parameter (defaulted so the existing five announcement kinds — open, save, rename, delete, folder-created/deleted — keep posting empty-attachment messages); a new `LibrarianAttachAnnouncement` interface and `buildAttachContent` helper produce the steampunk phrasing ("the illustration" / "the volume" depending on MIME), and `postLibrarianAttachAnnouncement` packages it. No new tables, no migration, no schema bump — `MessageEvent.attachments: UUID[]` already accepts the mount-file id since both id spaces are UUIDs, and the announcement message exports as a normal message so .qtap round-trips for free. (`lib/chat-files-v2.ts`, `lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/files/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/get.ts`, `components/chat/LibraryFilePickerModal.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/components/ChatModals.tsx`, `help/scriptorium.md`)
- **Salon — Document Mode picker can create a new blank document in the currently-browsed mount-point folder, with collision-numbered "Untitled Document.md" naming**: The mount-point branch of `DocumentPickerModal` gained a `New document here` button (alongside the existing `New folder`) that closes the modal and opens a brand-new blank document in the folder you're standing in. The picker passes `{ scope: 'document_store', mountPoint, targetFolder }` (no `filePath`) through `onSelectDocument` → `useDocumentMode.openDocument` → `openDocumentForChat` → `POST /api/v1/chats/{id}?action=open-document`; the schema gained an optional `targetFolder` field. Server-side, `handleOpenDocument` no longer names the new file `${crypto.randomUUID()}.md`. A new `pickUntitledDocumentPath` helper resolves and probes `Untitled Document.md` first, then `Untitled Document 2.md`, `Untitled Document 3.md`, … up to 1000 attempts, picking the first name with no existing file at that path. Existence checks dispatch on `mountType` via a small `resolvedPathExists` helper (`readDatabaseDocument` for database-backed stores, treating `NOT_FOUND` as "free"; `fs.access` for filesystem mounts, treating `ENOENT` as "free"). The chosen path is written empty via the existing `writeFileWithMtimeCheck`, and `displayTitle` defaults to `path.basename(filePath)` (so the editor header shows `Untitled Document.md`) instead of the bland `'Untitled document'` literal — matching how existing-file opens already derive their title. Rename works as soon as the file exists on disk: the existing `handleRenameDocument` preserves the directory and extension, so typing `MyDoc` in the title input moves `subfolder/Untitled Document.md` → `subfolder/MyDoc.md` with no special casing for newly-created documents. The original top-level `New blank document` button still works unchanged for project/general-scope quick-creates and now also benefits from the new naming. (`app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/components/DocumentPickerModal.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/documentModeApi.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useDocumentMode.ts`)
- **Salon — Document Mode picker can now create a folder inside a document store, and empty folders persist across reopens**: Browsing a mount point in the Open Document picker (Salon → Open Document → a Document Store) used to be read-only — derived folders showed up only because they contained indexed files, so empty shelves never appeared and there was no way to make one without dropping to the LLM's `doc_create_folder` tool or the underlying filesystem. The mount-point branch of `DocumentPickerModal` now renders a `New folder` button at every level; clicking expands an inline input with Enter / Escape / Cancel. On submit, the client POSTs to a new `app/api/v1/mount-points/[id]/folders/route.ts` endpoint with `{path}` (current folder + the typed name), which dispatches on `mountType`: database-backed mounts go through `createDatabaseFolder` (writes a `doc_mount_folders` row via `ensureFolderPath`), filesystem mounts validate the joined path stays inside the mount's `basePath` and call `fs.mkdir({recursive: true})`. Server-side validation rejects `..`, absolute paths, empty segments, control characters, and the standard set of reserved characters (`<>:"|?*\\/`); the same checks run client-side for a faster error message. To make empty folders visible after the modal closes and reopens, `GET /api/v1/mount-points/[id]/files` now also returns `folders: string[]`. For database-backed mounts the list comes from `repos.docMountFolders.findByMountPointId` (filtering out the empty-string root row). For filesystem and obsidian mounts the route walks `basePath` with a small recursive `listFilesystemFolders` helper that honors the mount's configured `excludePatterns` via the scanner's exported `matchesPattern` and skips symlinks, returning every directory as a POSIX-style relative path. The picker stores both in `mountPointFolders` state and merges them into `mountPointEntries.folders` alongside the file-derived ones; the same-session `createdFolders: Set<string>` is kept as belt-and-braces so a freshly-created folder is visible without waiting for a refetch. Project and General library scopes already had folder creation via the existing `FileBrowser` component, so this change only touches the mount-point branch. (`app/api/v1/mount-points/[id]/folders/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/mount-points/[id]/files/route.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/components/DocumentPickerModal.tsx`, `help/scriptorium.md`)
- **CLI — new `quilltap docs` subcommand for working with mount-point document stores from the terminal**. Verbs: `list` (table of all mount points with cached counts), `show <id>` (one mount with live counts cross-checked against cached fileCount/chunkCount), `files <id> [--folder <prefix>]` (file enumeration), `read <id> <path>` (raw bytes/text to stdout), `read --rendered <id> <path>` (extracted plaintext as fed to the embedder — pulls from `doc_mount_blobs.extractedText` first, then `doc_mount_documents.content` for database-backed text, then concatenated chunks ordered by `chunkIndex`), `export <id> <outputDir>` (whole-mount dump preserving relative paths; uses `fs.copyFileSync` for filesystem-source files, writes UTF-8 for database-source text, writes raw bytes for blobs), and `scan <id>` (POST to `/api/v1/mount-points/:id?action=scan` on the running server). `read` refuses to dump binary file types (`pdf`, `docx`, `blob`) to a TTY unless `--force` is passed. Read operations open `quilltap-mount-index.db` directly via the same SQLCipher pepper as the main DB; `scan` requires the server to be running on `--port` (default 3000). `--json` flag for machine-readable output on `list`/`show`/`files`/`scan`. Implementation in `packages/quilltap/lib/docs-commands.js`, with shared `resolveDataDir` / `loadDbKey` / `promptPassphrase` / `openMountIndexDb` helpers extracted to the new `packages/quilltap/lib/db-helpers.js` so both `bin/quilltap.js` and `docs-commands.js` import them. Help docs at `help/cli-docs.md`. `docs search` is intentionally deferred — there is no REST endpoint for semantic search yet, and adding one is its own scope.
- **CLI — `quilltap db --mount-points` flag** points the existing `db` subcommand at `quilltap-mount-index.db` (parallel to the existing `--llm-logs`). Mutually exclusive with `--llm-logs`. Same `--data-dir`, `--passphrase`, `--repl`, `--tables`, `--count` behavior as the main DB.
- **Aurora — new per-character `systemTransparency` toggle, a one-way kill switch over the three things by which a character can perceive the system around them**: Three capabilities normally available to a character — the `self_inventory` introspection tool, the running announcements of "the Staff" (Lantern, Aurora, Librarian, plus reserved slots for Prospero and the Host), and `doc_*`-tool access to character vaults (their own and peers') — can each already be toggled at the chat and project level. The new character-level `systemTransparency` boolean (default `null`/false, i.e. opaque) collapses all three into a single per-character covenant. When `systemTransparency !== true`, every one of those three is forced **off** for that character regardless of any chat/project setting; when `true`, the chat/project settings have their say as before. Wording on the toggle leans into the framing: off says *"My character will trust me without being able to verify me. I accept the covenant of that trust,"* on says *"My character will be able to verify everything about their existence, including how they are crafted and how they interact with me."* Schema: `CharacterSchema` in `lib/schemas/character.types.ts` gained `systemTransparency: z.boolean().nullable().optional()`. SQLite carries it as `INTEGER DEFAULT NULL`; the new `add-character-system-transparency-field-v1` migration adds the column for upgraders following the `add-character-wardrobe-flags-v1` pattern, and `sqlite-initial-schema.ts` carries it for fresh installs. `CharacterVaultPropertiesSchema` in `lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts` now includes the field as optional (so older vaults still parse), threaded through the read overlay (`applyDocumentStoreOverlay`), the write overlay (`applyDocumentStoreWriteOverlay` — `propsKeys` widened to include `'systemTransparency'`), the snapshot reader (`readCharacterVaultManagedFields`), and the snapshot writer (`writeCharacterVaultManagedFields` — properties.json now carries the field). Added to `MANAGED_FIELDS` so vault-mode characters get their updates routed to `properties.json`. The `chat_messages.systemSender` Zod enum was widened to include `'prospero'` and `'host'` ahead of those features landing; the SQLite column is free-form `TEXT` so no migration. Enforcement is split across three surgical guards rather than a single resolver, since each underlying capability already has its own chat/project plumbing: (1) **Vault access** — `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts` gained `actingCharacterIsOpaqueToVaults(context)` (defaults to opaque on lookup failure so a transient repo error never accidentally grants access). Both `buildReadResolutionContext` and `buildWriteResolutionContext` consult it; when opaque, they drop `characterId` and `characterIds` from the resolution context entirely, so `resolveDocEditPath` admits only project-linked document stores — character vaults become unreachable by ID, by name, or by peer-list expansion. (2) **`self_inventory` tool** — orchestrator (`lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts`) computes `effectiveDisabledTools = chat.disabledTools ∪ {'self_inventory'}` when `character.systemTransparency !== true` and passes that union into `buildTools`, layering on top of any chat- or project-level disable. (3) **Staff (systemSender) messages** — `buildMessageContext` in `lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts` filters `existingMessages` at the very top — `existingMessages.filter(m => !m.systemSender)` when the character is opaque — and threads the filtered list through both the LLM prompt path (via `buildConversationMessages`) and the Lantern image-attachment scan (`collectLanternImageFileIdsForCharacter`) so an opaque character receives neither the announcement text nor the announced image. The filter type signature gained `systemSender?: string | null`. UI: new card at the top of the **Details** tab in `app/aurora/[id]/edit/components/CharacterBasicInfo.tsx` renders the toggle and switches its descriptive copy between the "covenant of trust" and "verify everything" wordings depending on position. Hook plumbing in `app/aurora/[id]/edit/hooks/useCharacterEdit.ts` gained `handleSystemTransparencyChange` (local state only; persists with the regular form save so the user can change their mind before committing); types extended in `app/aurora/[id]/edit/types.ts`. API: `updateCharacterSchema` in `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts` accepts the new field. Export schema (`public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`) gained the property on `ExportedCharacter`, and the `MessageEvent.systemSender` enum was widened to match. DDL doc (`docs/developer/DDL.md`) updated. Help file at `help/character-system-transparency.md` covers the covenant in long form. (`lib/schemas/character.types.ts`, `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/types.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/hooks/useCharacterEdit.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/page.tsx`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/components/CharacterBasicInfo.tsx`, `migrations/scripts/sqlite-initial-schema.ts`, `migrations/scripts/add-character-system-transparency-field.ts`, `migrations/scripts/index.ts`, `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`, `docs/developer/DDL.md`, `help/character-system-transparency.md`)
- **`self_inventory` LLM tool — two new sections: `Memories Loaded This Turn` and `Vault Access (this chat)`**: The zero-argument introspection tool previously surfaced five sections (vault contents, memory stats, conversation stats, assembled system prompt, last-turn LLM usage). It now returns seven. (1) **Memories Loaded This Turn** reports the exact memory slate that was injected into the current prompt: the semantic-search hits from `## Relevant Memories` (summary, importance, score, effective weight), the inter-character memories from `## Memories About Other Characters` (aboutCharacterName, summary, importance), and the memory recap text if one was injected on chat start / character join. Rather than re-running the embedding+search (which would pay the cost twice and might not match the actual prompt), the orchestrator forwards the already-computed debug arrays from `buildMessageContext` into `ToolExecutionContext.loadedMemories` (new `LoadedMemoriesContext` type in `lib/chat/tool-executor.ts`) via an extra arg on `createToolContext`; the self_inventory dispatch forwards them into `SelfInventoryToolContext.loadedMemories`; the handler projects them unchanged. `BuiltContext` picked up `debugInterCharacterMemories` and `debugMemoryRecap` to match — the local inter-character debug array in `context-manager.ts` was being captured into `formatted.debugMemories` but never returned, so this fills in a gap. When self_inventory is invoked through a path that doesn't populate the tool context (sudo-approval run-tool endpoint, help-chat), the section reports "Unavailable" rather than silently showing an empty list. (2) **Vault Access (this chat)** lists, for the responding character's vault, who can read and write it right now in this chat. The acting character and any participant with `controlledBy === 'user'` are listed as read/write (the user persona reaches peer vaults via Document Mode regardless of the tool-level gate); other present CHARACTER participants are listed as read-only iff the chat's `allowCrossCharacterVaultReads` ("Shared Vaults") toggle is on, and omitted entirely otherwise. Absent/removed participants are filtered out. The section also reports the toggle state so the LLM can reason about why the list looks the way it does. Both new sections share the existing per-section try/catch so a single failing lookup yields an "Unavailable — reason" marker rather than taking down the whole report. Tool-description string updated to mention the two new sections. Built-in tool output shape (`SelfInventoryToolOutput`) gained `loadedMemories: SelfInventoryLoadedMemoriesSection` and `vaultAccess: SelfInventoryVaultAccessSection`; both are also surfaced as structured fields on the `ToolResult` next to `formattedText`. (`lib/tools/self-inventory-tool.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/self-inventory-handler.ts`, `lib/chat/tool-executor.ts`, `lib/chat/context-manager.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/tool-execution.service.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/orchestrator.service.ts`)
- **Aurora — `{{char}}` / `{{user}}` replacement buttons now iterate every prose array, not just the simple fields and scenarios**: The character view page's two "Replace N occurrences of *Name* with `{{char}}`/`{{user}}`" buttons scanned `description`, `personality`, `firstMessage`, `exampleDialogues`, the default system prompt's `content`, and every `scenarios[]` entry — leaving every *non-default* system prompt and every `physicalDescriptions[]` entry invisible to both the hit counter and the one-shot rewrite. Characters with, e.g., a "Holiday" prompt variant and a second physical-description entry for a costumed look would show under-counted totals on the buttons, and clicking never touched those bodies. The counting seam in `useCharacterView.ts` now folds every `systemPrompts[]` entry (keyed `systemPrompt:<id>`) and every `physicalDescriptions[]` entry's five prose fields (keyed `physicalDescription:<id>:<field>`) into the same `Record<string, string | null | undefined>` that `countTemplateReplacements` already consumed — the helper was always key-agnostic, so no change there. The replacement handler gained two matching blocks that immutably `.map` over each array (reference-equal pass-through for untouched items) and include the full replaced array in the `PUT /api/v1/characters/:id` body only when at least one item actually changed; single round-trip preserved. The server side already accepts both arrays, and `applyDocumentStoreWriteOverlay` routes them correctly for vault-mode characters (`systemPrompts` → `Prompts/*.md` via `projectArrayIntoVaultFolder`, `physicalDescriptions[0]` → `physical-description.md` + `physical-prompts.json`, index 1+ falls through to the DB row) — no schema, API, or migration change required. Explicitly out of scope per the user's instructions: `properties.json` metadata (`pronouns`, `aliases`, `title`, `talkativeness`), `clothingRecords[].description`, and `wardrobe.json` item/preset descriptions remain untouched; `firstMessage` continues to be replaced even though it lives in `properties.json`, because it's prose and is the single most common field to contain literal names. The orphaned `TemplateFields` named interface (only used by this hook) was deleted along with its import, replaced inline with `Record<string, string | null | undefined>`; `CharacterPhysicalDescription` was added to the view-page's local `Character` type to cover the newly-traversed field. (`app/aurora/[id]/view/hooks/useCharacterView.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/view/types.ts`)
- **Aurora — "Refine from Memories" now analyzes scenarios and system prompts one at a time, and can deposit its proposals as a vault dossier instead of applying them directly**: The Character Optimizer (`/aurora/[id]/view` → "Refine from Memories") has until now issued a single LLM call that asked for suggestions across every field, scenario, and system prompt in one go, which averaged per-item patterns out across siblings and made it hard for the model to weigh, e.g., one scenario's quirks on their own terms. The suggestions pass is now split into focused sub-calls: one for the general fields (`description`, `personality`, `exampleDialogues`, `talkativeness`), one call per existing scenario (each scoped to that scenario's ID/title/content), one call per existing system prompt (each scoped to that prompt's ID/name/content), and a final "propose any genuinely new scenarios or system prompts" pass. Per-item rules live in four new prompt builders in `lib/services/character-optimizer.service.ts` (`getGeneralFieldsSuggestionsPrompt`, `getScenarioSuggestionPrompt`, `getSystemPromptSuggestionPrompt`, `getNewItemsSuggestionPrompt`) and share a `SUGGESTION_SCHEMA_PREAMBLE`. Each sub-call's output is filtered by `MIN_SIGNIFICANCE_THRESHOLD` and assigned a fresh `id` before being appended to the aggregated suggestions. Sub-call failures (network errors, unparsable JSON) are logged and skipped rather than aborting the whole run, so one flaky response can't wipe out the rest of the proposals. New progress events stream per sub-step (`substep_start` / `substep_complete` carry an `OptimizerSubStep` of `{kind, label, index, total}`) so the UI shows "Scenario 2 of 5 — Tea Room" while the automata work. Cost/latency tradeoff: a character with 3 prompts + 5 scenarios now makes ~11 LLM calls instead of 2, which the author has explicitly accepted — focused suggestions are worth the round trips. — A second change adds an opt-in **suggestions-file output mode** for characters linked to a document-store vault (`readPropertiesFromDocumentStore && characterDocumentMountPointId`): instead of the apply-and-review flow, the optimizer writes its summary, patterns, and grouped proposals to `Suggestions/refinement-<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>.md` in the character's vault and surfaces the path in the modal, so the author and the character may review and discuss the proposals in-chat before any are commissioned. Vault write happens via `writeDatabaseDocument` which auto-creates the `Suggestions/` folder; the markdown document carries YAML frontmatter (`type`, `generatedAt`, `characterId`, `characterName`, `model`, `memoryCount`, `suggestionCount`), a summary, an "observed patterns" section, and H3 sections per suggestion grouped by kind (General Fields, Scenario Refinements, Proposed New Scenarios, System Prompt Refinements, Proposed New System Prompts, Other). Suggestions are rendered with current/proposed in fenced blocks, significance, rationale, and supporting memoir excerpts as block quotes. New optimizer option `outputMode: 'apply' | 'suggestions-file'` (default `'apply'`) carried on `OptimizerOptions`, added to `optimizeStreamSchema` in `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts`, and exposed on the modal as an opt-in checkbox that only renders when the character has a vault. The hook gained `progressSubStep`, `suggestionsFilePath`, and a new terminal phase `'suggestions-file-written'`. Existing "apply" flow is unchanged; previously-applied writes for vault-backed characters still route through `applyDocumentStoreWriteOverlay`, which already handled writing managed fields to vault files instead of the DB row. (`lib/services/character-optimizer.service.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts`, `components/characters/optimizer/types.ts`, `components/characters/optimizer/hooks/useCharacterOptimizer.ts`, `components/characters/optimizer/CharacterOptimizerModal.tsx`, `app/aurora/[id]/view/page.tsx`, `app/aurora/[id]/view/types.ts`, `help/character-optimizer.md`)
- **New `doc_copy_file` LLM tool — copy a text file from one document store to a different document store**: Until now the `doc_*` tool family had read, write, move, and delete but no copy primitive, so a character that wanted to duplicate a file across two Scriptorium stores had to `doc_read_file` then `doc_write_file` with the same content — two round-trips and no natural handling of "drop it into this folder, keep the existing filename." `doc_copy_file` takes `source_mount_point`, `source_path`, `dest_mount_point`, and `dest_path`; it is deliberately cross-store only (rejects same-store copies by comparing resolved `mountPointId` values, so name-vs-ID inputs that collapse to the same store are also caught). Destination-path semantics mirror `cp`: an empty `dest_path` or `"."` / `"/"` means "copy to dest root using the source filename"; a `dest_path` that resolves to an existing folder (detected via `fs.stat().isDirectory()` for filesystem mounts or `databaseFolderExists` for database-backed mounts) causes the source basename to be appended; otherwise `dest_path` is treated as the full destination path, with parent directories created on demand. Refuses to overwrite an existing destination file, matching `doc_move_file`. Text files only — binary assets should go through the `doc_*_blob` family; the tool rejects non-text extensions up front via the existing `isTextFile` helper. Implementation piggybacks on the existing doc-edit layer: `resolveDocEditPath` for both paths (source via `buildReadResolutionContext` so peer vaults remain readable when `allowCrossCharacterVaultReads` is on, destination via `buildWriteResolutionContext` so peer vaults stay read-only), `readFileWithMtime` → `writeFileWithMtimeCheck` for the copy itself (both helpers already dispatch filesystem-vs-database transparently), and `triggerReindexIfNeeded` on the destination so the copied file is searchable immediately. Registered as a built-in tool in `app/api/v1/tools/route.ts` (`BUILT_IN_TOOL_SCHEMAS` + `BUILT_IN_TOOLS` metadata), wired into the universal tool builder, and added to the exported builtin-tool-name list in `@quilltap/plugin-utils` (bumped to `2.2.5` — requires `npm publish`). Help docs at `help/document-editing-tools.md` describe the behavior for users. (`lib/tools/doc-copy-file-tool.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts`, `lib/tools/index.ts`, `lib/tools/plugin-tool-builder.ts`, `app/api/v1/tools/route.ts`, `packages/plugin-utils/src/builtin-tools.ts`, `packages/plugin-utils/package.json`, `help/document-editing-tools.md`, `__tests__/unit/lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler-copy.test.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler-folders.test.ts`)
- **New `self_inventory` LLM tool — characters can now introspect their own configuration mid-chat**: Added a zero-argument tool that returns one assembled report for the calling character with five sections: (1) every file in the character's vault — mount point name, relativePath, fileName, fileType, fileSizeBytes, lastModified — recursive through subfolders like `Prompts/` and `Scenarios/`, with enough metadata to call `doc_read_file`/`doc_write_file` without a second lookup; (2) memory totals — `countByCharacterId` plus `findByImportance(characterId, 0.7)` for high-importance count and percentage; (3) conversation totals — chat count, earliest `createdAt`, latest activity preferring `lastMessageAt` then `updatedAt` then `createdAt`; (4) the static system prompt for every turn — `buildSystemPrompt()` called with a shallow arg set (user persona, other participants, roleplay template, selected system prompt, timestamp config, project context, scenario text, responding participant status), deliberately omitting per-turn tool instructions, memory blocks, wardrobe context, and outfit/status notifications; (5) last-turn LLM usage — `llmLogs.findByChatId(chatId)[0]` reporting provider, modelName, promptTokens/completionTokens/totalTokens, `getModelContextLimit(provider, model)` for the window, and a utilization percentage. When no log exists (fresh chat) the section falls back to the resolved connection profile via `resolveConnectionProfile` + `repos.connections.findById`, honoring `profile.maxContext` as the window override, and reports zero tokens. Each of the five sections is wrapped in its own try/catch so any single data-source failure becomes an "unavailable" marker with a reason rather than failing the whole tool — the top-level `success` is only `false` if `characterId` is missing from the tool context or the character can't be found. `isMountIndexDegraded()` short-circuits the vault section with a specific reason so the other four still render during mount-index recovery. Always-on for character participants (pushed unconditionally in `buildToolsForProvider`), no new `BuildToolsOptions` flag — pure introspection, no side effects, benefits every character by default. Built-in tool registered under `BUILT_IN_TOOLS` in `lib/chat/tool-executor.ts` following the `state` tool three-file pattern (definition + handler + formatter). (`lib/tools/self-inventory-tool.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/self-inventory-handler.ts`, `lib/tools/index.ts`, `lib/chat/tool-executor.ts`, `lib/tools/plugin-tool-builder.ts`)
- **Aurora — `Copy database → vault` sync button on the character edit page, symmetric with the existing vault-to-database snapshot**: The dual-path character state (database row vs. Scriptorium vault) now offers a button for either direction. The old `Snapshot to database` button (re-labeled to `Copy vault → database`) was only visible when the overlay switch was on and only ran one way; the overlay card on the `details` tab now surfaces both buttons whenever a linked vault exists — switch on or switch off — letting the user decide whose state wins. New POST action `sync-properties-to-vault` on `/api/v1/characters/[id]` reads the canonical DB row via `findByIdRaw`, pulls raw wardrobe items (`includeArchived: true`) and outfit presets, and projects every vault-managed field out via a new `writeCharacterVaultManagedFields` helper in `lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`. The helper writes `properties.json`, `description.md`, `personality.md`, `example-dialogues.md`, `physical-description.md`, `physical-prompts.json`, and `wardrobe.json` unconditionally, and reprojects the `Prompts/` and `Scenarios/` folders via the existing `projectArrayIntoVaultFolder` (files that don't correspond to a DB entry are deleted so the folder listings match the DB arrays exactly). `physical-description.md` and `physical-prompts.json` are skipped when the character has no primary physical description, matching the read overlay's "overlay is on index 0 only" rule. The action returns the overlaid character so the UI picks up vault-backed values immediately if the switch is on. Hook method `handleSyncPropertiesToVault` in `app/aurora/[id]/edit/hooks/useCharacterEdit.ts` mirrors `handleSyncPropertiesFromVault`; `app/aurora/[id]/edit/page.tsx` wraps it in `handleSyncPropertiesToVaultAndRefreshLists` so the child `PhysicalDescriptionList` and `WardrobeItemList` re-query (their data hangs off `refreshKey` props). Info log `[Characters v1] Synced character properties to vault` records the file/prompt/scenario/wardrobe counts on success. (`lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/hooks/useCharacterEdit.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/page.tsx`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/components/CharacterBasicInfo.tsx`, `help/character-editing.md`)
- **Salon — Document Mode opens and saves are now announced by the Librarian instead of costing the user their turn**: Opening a document in Document Mode, or saving one from the editor, used to funnel through `sendProgrammaticMessage` in `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx` — a USER-role message posted via the `/api/v1/messages` endpoint that immediately triggered an LLM response, eating the user's turn every time they touched a document. The announcement is now an ASSISTANT-role synthetic message attributed to a new `'librarian'` `systemSender`, paralleling how the Lantern and Aurora already speak up in chat. A new writer at `lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts` exports `postLibrarianOpenAnnouncement` and `postLibrarianSaveAnnouncement`; both use `repos.chats.addMessage` to persist the message and swallow errors so no document operation ever fails because an announcement couldn't be written. Three kinds: `opened-by-user` ("The Librarian has set out \"X\" from the project library at the user's request..."), `opened-by-character` ("The Librarian has set out \"X\" from the project library at Aurora's request..."), and `saved` (re-phrases the existing unified-diff notification to "The Librarian has filed the following alterations to \"X\"..."). The open-document and write-document action handlers in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts` post the announcement after success and return the Message in their response payload; the client hook `useDocumentMode` surfaces it via a new `onLibrarianMessage(message)` callback (replacing `onAutosaveNotify`) which `page.tsx` uses to append directly to the local messages state. `useDocumentMode.ts` generates the autosave diff client-side via the existing `formatAutosaveNotification` and sends it as an optional `diffContent` field on `write-document` so the server can bundle the announcement into the same round-trip. Character-initiated opens are covered too: `handleOpenDocument` in `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts` now looks up the acting character via `repos.characters.findById(context.characterId)` and passes `{ kind: 'opened-by-character', characterName }` to the writer, so when Aurora uses `doc_open_document` on the user's behalf the announcement names her explicitly. The avatar asset already exists at `public/images/avatars/librarian-avatar.webp`; `getMessageAvatar` in `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx` gained the Librarian branch ahead of the participant fall-through. `MessageEventSchema.systemSender` (Zod), `app/salon/[id]/types.ts`, and `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json` all widened from `'lantern' | 'aurora'` to `'lantern' | 'aurora' | 'librarian'`. No migration needed — `chat_messages.systemSender` is free-form TEXT and the enum is a Zod-level constraint. The old `sendProgrammaticMessage`/`sendProgrammaticMessageRef` plumbing is gone from `page.tsx` entirely. Debug logs `[LibrarianNotification] Posting open announcement` / `Posting save announcement` fire at the writer; info log `[LibrarianNotification] Announcement posted` confirms the persisted message id. (`lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts`, `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useDocumentMode.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/documentModeApi.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/types.ts`, `public/schemas/qtap-export.schema.json`, `CLAUDE.md`, `help/scriptorium.md`)
- **Salon — new per-chat "Shared Vaults" toggle permits cross-character vault reads in multi-character chats, read-only**: In a chat like Friday + Amy, opening Amy's `personality.md` for Friday to consult previously required linking Amy's vault to a project or copying the file out manually — the `doc_*` tool family gates access by the acting character's own `characterDocumentMountPointId` plus any mount points linked to the active project, so peer participants' private vaults were invisible. A new `allowCrossCharacterVaultReads` boolean on `ChatMetadataSchema` (default `false`) opens a narrow reads-only crossover when the user flips it on from the chat header. Wiring: `collectAccessibleMountPointIds` in `lib/doc-edit/path-resolver.ts` already folded `characterIds: string[]` into the accessible mount set (originally added for Document Mode's participant enumeration), so the enforcement point is the handler's context builder. `buildResolutionContext` in `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts` was split into `buildReadResolutionContext` (async — loads the chat, and when the flag is on passes the other present participants' character IDs as `characterIds`) and `buildWriteResolutionContext` (rejects any write whose `mount_point` names a peer's vault with a dedicated `ACCESS_DENIED` error — "*character*'s vault is read-only in this chat" — before resolution runs, so the LLM gets a specific message instead of a generic "not accessible"). Every `doc_*` handler is wired to the appropriate builder: reads (`doc_read_file`, `doc_grep`, `doc_list_files`, `doc_read_frontmatter`, `doc_read_heading`, `doc_read_blob`, `doc_list_blobs`, `doc_open_document` on existing files) admit peer vaults when the flag is on; writes (`doc_write_file`, `doc_str_replace`, `doc_insert_text`, `doc_update_frontmatter`, `doc_update_heading`, `doc_move_file`, `doc_delete_file`, `doc_create_folder`, `doc_delete_folder`, `doc_move_folder`, `doc_write_blob`, `doc_delete_blob`) stay scoped to the acting character's own vault plus project-linked stores. `getAccessibleMountPoints` gains an optional `extraCharacterIds` parameter so the enumeration paths (`doc_grep`, `doc_list_files`) expand their mount-point list when reading. `resolveBlobMountPoint` is now split into `resolveBlobMountPointForRead` / `resolveBlobMountPointForWrite` mirroring the builder split. UI toggle lives next to the existing All Whispers control in the Salon header, gated on `isMultiChar`, modeled on `handleToggleDocumentEditingMode` — `useChatControls` syncs local state from `chat.allowCrossCharacterVaultReads`, toggles via `PUT /api/v1/chats/{id}`, rolls back and toasts on failure. `updateChatSchema` (API), `ChatMetadataSchema` / `ChatMetadataBaseSchema` (model), `GET /api/v1/chats/{id}` response shape, and the Salon `Chat` TS type all carry the field through. Migration `add-chat-cross-character-vault-reads-field-v1` adds the SQLite column as `INTEGER DEFAULT 0`. Default-off means existing chats keep their pre-change behavior with no migration-time action; new chats start closed until the user opens the door. Debug log `Cross-character vault reads enabled; expanding access` fires when the builder admits peer vaults on a read; info log `Rejected write to peer character vault` fires on a blocked write. (`lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, `lib/doc-edit/path-resolver.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts`, `migrations/scripts/add-chat-cross-character-vault-reads-field.ts`, `migrations/scripts/index.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/schemas.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/get.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useChatControls.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/types.ts`, `help/shared-character-vaults.md`)
- **Document Mode — Delete button in the editor header, plus Librarian announcements for user file deletes and the character-facing `doc_delete_file` / `doc_create_folder` / `doc_delete_folder` tool calls**: `DocumentPane`'s header previously exposed only a focus-mode toggle, a Close button, and the click-to-edit title; there was no way for the user to remove a file from Document Mode without leaving the pane. Adds a trash-icon button next to Close that runs `showConfirmation("Delete \"X\"? This removes the underlying file and cannot be undone.")` and — on confirm — fires a new `onDeleteDocument` prop wired through `useDocumentMode`'s `deleteDocument` callback. New action handler `handleDeleteDocument` in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts` resolves the active chat document, dispatches on `mountType` — `deleteDatabaseDocument` from `lib/mount-index/database-store.ts` for database-backed stores, `fs.stat` + `fs.unlink` for filesystem (with a not-a-file guard) — deactivates the `chat_documents` row via `closeDocument` and flips `documentMode` back to `'normal'`, and posts a user-origin Librarian delete announcement. Wired into `CHAT_POST_ACTIONS` as `'delete-document'` in `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/post.ts` and re-exported from `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/index.ts`. Client-side, `deleteDocumentForChat` in `app/salon/[id]/hooks/documentModeApi.ts` hits the new endpoint; the `useDocumentMode` hook's `deleteDocument` cancels the pending autosave timer first (so it can't fire against a file that's about to vanish), clears the active-document state, and forwards the returned `librarianMessage` through the existing `onLibrarianMessageRef` path so it appears in the transcript. — Alongside the user-facing button, the LLM's file-structure tools now also announce via the Librarian so present characters hear about structural changes made by a peer. `handleDeleteFile`, `handleCreateFolder`, and `handleDeleteFolder` in `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts` each post after success, with a shared `resolveActorOrigin(context)` helper that mirrors `handleOpenDocument`'s character-name lookup and falls back to `{ kind: 'by-user' }` when no character ID is present or the lookup fails. The writer at `lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts` gained three kinds — `deleted` ("The Librarian has removed \"X\" from the project library at Aurora's instruction..."), `folder-created` ("The Librarian has set aside a fresh shelf for \"Drafts/\" ..."), and `folder-deleted` ("The Librarian has dismantled the empty shelf at \"Drafts/\" ...") — and a shared `LibrarianActorOrigin = { kind: 'by-user' } | { kind: 'by-character'; characterName: string }` discriminant used by all three, separate from the existing `LibrarianOpenKind` because open has distinct phrasing ("at X's request" vs "at X's instruction"). Every writer swallows errors internally so no document operation ever fails because an announcement couldn't be written. Kind labels for the shared `postLibrarianMessage` log helper distinguish `deleted-by-user` vs `deleted-by-character` (and similarly for the folder kinds) so log analysis can separate human-driven from LLM-driven destructive actions. No new migrations or schema bumps — the `'librarian'` `systemSender` already handles all four kinds. (`lib/services/librarian-notifications/writer.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/index.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/handlers/post.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/documentModeApi.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useDocumentMode.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/components/DocumentPane.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `help/scriptorium.md`, `help/document-editing-tools.md`)
- **Personified-feature avatars — bundled source art for Aurora, Concierge, Host, Lantern, Librarian, Pascal, and Prospero, optimized to WebP**: New directory `public/images/avatars/` holds the canonical avatar asset for each named personified feature of the app (the ones that can "speak up" inside a chat — currently only the Lantern, with more planned). Originals arrived as 1696×2528 PNGs weighing 2–8 MB each; `cwebp -q 82 -m 6 -mt` brings the set down to 188 KB – 1.06 MB without visible quality loss at avatar display sizes, cutting the bundled asset footprint by roughly 95% and keeping the chat's avatar fetches cheap on first paint. PNG sources deleted once the WebP outputs were verified — the directory is now WebP-only. New CLAUDE.md section "Personified-feature avatars" documents the convention so future additions (Concierge announcements, Prospero affordances, etc.) know where the art lives and how to keep it sized correctly. (`public/images/avatars/`, `CLAUDE.md`)
- **System prompt budget no longer chokes complex characters**: The system-prompt sub-budget in `getRecommendedContextAllocation` has been raised from 5%/1000-floor to 20%/4000-floor. The previous allocation was so tight that any reasonably fleshed-out character (description + personality + scenarios + system prompts + multi-character context + wardrobe + tool instructions + status reminders + the new mentioned-characters dossier) routinely overran it on mid-sized context windows — for a 65k-token model, the old budget was 3,276 tokens, and a 4,400-token system prompt was getting its tail (multi-character context, status reminder, late-appended sections) silently lopped off by `truncateToTokenLimit`. The new ceiling gives 13,104 tokens at 65k context and 40,000 at 200k, leaving roughly the same recent-message and memory budgets in place. The hard truncation remains as a final safety net but should rarely fire under normal use. (`lib/llm/model-context-data.ts`)
- **Developer docs — end-to-end Commonplace Book breakdown**: New `docs/developer/features/memory_management.md` covers how memories are formed during a chat, how the three scoring numbers (`importance`, `reinforcedImportance`, `effectiveWeight`) and the protection score relate, what the Memory Gate and three-pass housekeeping actually do, and — the main reason this doc exists — a catalogue of the Node main-thread hot spots that stall on tens-of-thousands of memories per character. Separates hot spots that were addressed on 2026-04-20 (housekeeping logger overhead, O(n²) delete-set scans, double protection computation, un-yielding loops, startup-grace timing) from those that were not (notably the per-turn `searchMemoriesSemantic` full-table hydrate-to-hydrate-top-K pattern in `lib/memory/memory-service.ts:515`, now flagged as prime suspect). Includes a frank "why the recent commits mostly made things worse" postmortem and a prioritized open-work list anchored in the existing project memories (worker-thread move, search-hit counter, rank-normalized importance). No code change — docs only. (`docs/developer/features/memory_management.md`)
- **Commonplace Book — housekeeping protection gate switches to a blended score**: The four-rule protection gate in `isProtectedMemory` — importance ≥ 0.7, `source === 'MANUAL'`, accessed within 3 months, or reinforced ≥ 5 times with a usefulness condition — has been replaced with a single blended protection score that combines four evidence streams: time-decayed LLM content importance (365-day half-life), a log-saturating reinforcement bonus, a graph-degree bonus from `relatedMemoryIds.length`, and a flat recent-access bonus for memories touched within the last 90 days. Memories scoring at or above **0.5** are protected; everything below is eligible for the cap-enforcement sweep. `source === 'MANUAL'` remains a hard override — explicit user intent is always durable. The motivation is a Friday-instance audit: on a character with 19,524 memories, **19,303 (98.9%)** were protected solely by `importance ≥ 0.7`, because the cheap-LLM extractor clusters almost every memory in the 0.7–0.9 band (0.8 was the modal value, with 8,826 memories). Under the old rule, the cap-enforcement sweep could only delete 1 memory on that character because almost everything hit the LLM-score bright line. Under the blended score, time decay and usage evidence do the discrimination the LLM number failed to — a 0.8-importance memory from 400 days ago with no reinforcement and no access drops below protection, while a reinforced well-linked recently-accessed memory stays even if the LLM rated it 0.3. The formula lives in a new `calculateProtectionScore()` in `lib/memory/memory-weighting.ts` alongside the existing `calculateEffectiveWeight()` (which still governs retrieval ranking with its different, higher floor — retrieval and protection are now two functions, intentionally). New default config `DEFAULT_PROTECTION_CONFIG` exposes every knob. Eleven new unit tests cover the scoring curves, saturation points, and the recast housekeeping behavior. Help text at `help/memory-housekeeping.md` has been rewritten to describe the new gate. (`lib/memory/memory-weighting.ts`, `lib/memory/housekeeping.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/memory-weighting.test.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/housekeeping.test.ts`, `help/memory-housekeeping.md`)
- **Memory recall — tuned the retrieval knobs toward reinforced, higher-importance memories**: Four defaults in the per-turn Commonplace Book lookup that feeds the system prompt have been rebalanced. `maxMemories` bumps from 10 to 18 so each `## Relevant Memories` block has more room (still bounded by the memory token budget that trims the tail). `minMemoryImportance` rises from 0.3 to 0.5, raising the floor on what even gets into the candidate pool. The vector-store overshoot widens from `limit × 2` to `limit × 3`, giving the post-fetch filters (importance, source, scoring) more headroom before they starve the final slice. And the hybrid ranking used by both the semantic path and the text-search fallback flips from `0.6 · cosineSimilarity + 0.4 · effectiveWeight` to `0.4 · cosineSimilarity + 0.6 · effectiveWeight` — so reinforcement count and time-decay floor now drive ordering, with raw query similarity as the secondary factor.
