Combined effect: the retrieval pool is narrower at the bottom, wider at the top, and ranked by what the character has had repeatedly confirmed rather than what happens to phrase-match the current user turn. (`lib/chat/context-manager.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-service.ts`)
- **Document Mode internals were refactored for safer Scriptorium editing flow**: the Salon-side document hook now uses a shared API client for open/read/write/close state, autosave diff generation has been extracted into a reusable utility with regression coverage, and the chat document actions now resolve document context once and reuse the same post-save refresh path for document stores. This reduces duplicated logic and hardens Document Mode behavior without changing the user workflow. (`app/salon/[id]/hooks/useDocumentMode.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/documentModeApi.ts`, `lib/doc-edit/unified-diff.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/actions/documents.ts`)
- **Scriptorium live file watching**: Each enabled document store now runs a chokidar-backed filesystem watcher while the server is up. External edits, moves, and deletions are picked up within ~1–2 seconds, the mount index is updated per-file, and embedding jobs are debounce-enqueued for newly-changed chunks — no more waiting for a restart or a manual scan. Watchers attach/refresh/detach automatically when mount points are created, updated, or deleted via the API. Set `QUILLTAP_WATCHER_POLLING=1` to fall back to polling on network filesystems where native fs events are unreliable.
- **Unified new-chat dialog**: The three divergent "start a chat" paths — homepage character cards, the Aurora character-view "Start Chat" button, and `/salon/new` — now share a single form component and submit shape. Homepage quick-chats gain a system-prompt picker when the character has more than one prompt, every entry point can expand to a group chat via an "Add another character" toggle, and `/salon/new` accepts a new `?characterId=` deep-link param that pre-selects a character
- **New-chat character picker sizing**: The "Select Characters" list now sizes itself to `max(starred-count, 3, selected-count)` rows instead of occupying nearly the full viewport. The "Select Characters" and "Selected Characters" cards are locked to the same height at all times via the grid, and auto-grow together as you star or select more characters — significantly less vertical space for small rosters
- **New-chat form split into two cards**: The customization section below the character picker is now "Character Customization" (Play As, image profile, starting scenario, starting outfit, auto-gen avatars — plus connection profile and system prompt when in single-character modal mode) and "Reality Injection Mode" (timestamp injection settings today, with room to grow)
- **Homepage Active Projects — new-chat shortcut**: Each entry in the homepage's "Active Projects" list now has a small green chat icon that jumps straight to `/salon/new?projectId=…`, matching the "New Chat" flow available from the project detail page
- **New chat dialogs — user outfit selection**: The Quick Chat dialog (homepage), `/salon/new` page, and character-view chat creation dialog now expose outfit selection for the selected "Play As" character alongside the LLM character(s), so you can dress your own persona when starting a chat (not just theirs)
- **Concurrent embedding processing**: EMBEDDING_GENERATE jobs now run up to 4 at a time in the background job processor (with a 10-minute per-job timeout), while all other job types remain single-threaded — significantly faster bulk re-embeds, especially with local providers like Ollama
- **Queue Status Badges**: Added "Emb" (embedding) badge showing active embedding jobs. Expanded "Sum" to cover all post-turn processing (context summaries, title updates, scene state tracking, conversation rendering). Added character avatar generation to "Img" badge (renamed from "BG"). Badge order: Mem|Emb|Sum|Dgr|Img.
- **Scriptorium Status Auto-Update**: Scriptorium badge on conversation cards now polls every 5 seconds after a render is triggered, showing real-time status transitions (red → amber → green) as rendering and embedding complete
- Refactored Scriptorium Document Mode for a steadier editing flow: source/rich editing now shares the same toolbar path, split-pane resizing stays in sync with persisted layout, keyboard resizing works on the divider, and autosaves use mtime conflict protection to avoid overwriting external edits
- Removed scenario text from character avatar generation prompts to prevent image models from depicting multiple people when the scenario mentions other characters
- Enhanced participant action logging: update, remove, add, and reactivate actions now log character names, status transitions, updated fields, and failure details at appropriate levels (debug/info/warn)
- perf: Consolidated health-check polling from `InstanceLockGate` and `VersionGuardGate` into a shared `useHealthCheck` hook — eliminates ~24 requests/minute of continuous `/api/health` polling during normal operation (now fires once on mount and only polls when a 409 is detected)
- perf: Cache `useUserCharacterDisplayName` hook data at module level — previously each ChatCard instance fired its own API call to `/api/v1/characters?controlledBy=user`, causing N redundant fetches for N visible cards
- Refactored document-stores UI components to use `qt-*` semantic classes instead of raw Tailwind color classes
- Added `qt-dot-success`, `qt-dot-warning`, `qt-dot-destructive`, `qt-dot-info` utility classes to `_utilities.css`
- Removed dead code: `lib/tools/handlers/memory-search-handler.ts` (unused file)
- Removed pre-built help bundle (`public/help-bundle.msgpack.gz`) and `build:help` npm script — help docs are now embedded at runtime
- **Salon — system prompt now carries a *Characters Mentioned* section listing absent characters whose names crop up in the conversation**: When a chat references a character who exists in the user's workspace but is not currently a participant — a former companion, a relative, a rival named in passing — the responding character previously had no idea who that name belonged to and either improvised details or treated the noun as unknown. `buildContext` in `lib/chat/context-manager.ts` now scans the conversation summary plus every visible USER/ASSISTANT message for whole-word, case-insensitive mentions of any candidate character's `name` or any entry in their `aliases[]`, then injects a `## Characters Mentioned` block into the system prompt with each match's name, aliases, pronouns, and full description — no per-entry length cap and no per-section cap, so the responding character always receives complete grounding for the names in play. Always-on; the section is omitted entirely when nothing matches, so single-character chats with no cross-references pay zero added prompt cost. The section is appended to `finalSystemPrompt` *after* the core-system-prompt budget-driven truncation step at `context-manager.ts:558`, so it survives even on long, complex characters whose prompt already exceeds the 5%-of-context sub-budget and gets tail-chopped — the section never gets cut as collateral damage. Candidate pool is `repos.characters.findByUserId(userId)` filtered to exclude the responding character, every present participant whose `status !== 'removed'`, and (by name) the user's own persona — so removed-and-gone participants *can* surface as mentioned characters once they leave the room, but active/silent/absent peers stay in the multi-character context block where they belong. Matching is implemented in a new `lib/chat/context/mentioned-characters.ts` module: `findMentionedCharacterIds` builds a single regex with word-boundary alternation across all candidate names+aliases (longer tokens first so multi-word names like `John Smith` win over the bare `John`), regex metacharacters in names like `Mr. O'Brien` are escaped, and each hit is mapped back to character IDs through a lowercase token table that handles aliases shared across characters. `formatMentionedCharactersSection` renders entries alphabetically (deterministic for prompt caching). The whole assembly is wrapped in try/catch — failures here log a warning and skip the section so prompt construction never breaks. Debug log `[ContextManager] Mentioned characters section built` records candidate count, matched count, names, and section tokens on every turn that finds a hit. Unit tests at `__tests__/unit/mentioned-characters.test.ts` cover word-boundary anchoring (`Alicia` does not match `Alice`), case-insensitivity, alias hits, multi-word name matching, regex metachar escaping, deduplication, alphabetical ordering, long-description preservation, and full inclusion of every matched character. (`lib/chat/context/mentioned-characters.ts`, `lib/chat/context/system-prompt-builder.ts`, `lib/chat/context/index.ts`, `lib/chat/context-manager.ts`, `__tests__/unit/mentioned-characters.test.ts`, `help/chats.md`)
- **Project file storage — the project files card now reads and writes through the linked document store (Stage 3)**: The `FileBrowser` component at `components/files/FileBrowser.tsx` grew a second mode alongside the legacy one it already had. When a project has a linked `mountType='database'`, `storeType='documents'` Scriptorium store (which every project does now, courtesy of the Stage 1 migration), the browser resolves the link via `GET /api/v1/projects/{id}/mount-points` on mount and from that point forward reads the file list from `/api/v1/mount-points/{id}/files`, uploads through `POST /api/v1/mount-points/{id}/blobs`, and deletes via `DELETE /api/v1/mount-points/{id}/blobs/{...path}` — all talking to the document store directly rather than going through the legacy `files` mirror rows. For the general-files page (no project, no link) and for the few projects that somehow ended up without a linked store, the old path still works untouched. The `FileInfo` shape that downstream components consume now carries two extra optional fields, `mountPointId` and `relativePath`, so `FileThumbnail`, `useFilePreview`, and `useFileActions` can build URLs against `/api/v1/mount-points/{id}/blobs/{path}` instead of `/api/v1/files/{id}` when those are set. A small `components/files/mountBlobUrl.ts` helper centralizes the path encoding (each segment `encodeURIComponent`d exactly once, matching the catch-all route's decode). Uploads use a new `useMountPointBlobUpload` hook (sibling of `useProjectFileUpload`) that assembles the `file` + `path` form fields the blob endpoint expects, prepending the browser's current folder so files drop where the user is looking. Folder navigation in mount mode is derived from `relativePath` prefixes — `images/foo.webp` shows under `/images/` — since there's no mount-point folder CRUD API yet; folders appear implicitly once the first file is uploaded into them. Affordances that only apply to the legacy disk model — *New Folder*, *Sync filesystem*, orphan cleanup, *Move to project* — are hidden when in mount mode to avoid misleading the user with buttons that would either 404 or touch the wrong storage layer. Callers can also pass an explicit `mountPoint={{ id, mountType, storeType, name }}` prop to `FileBrowser` to skip the auto-resolve (useful when the parent already has the mount handy, or for the DocumentPickerModal's document-store scope). Delete confirmations that check for cross-entity associations remain legacy-only — mount-blob deletes have no `files`-table associations to warn about, so they fire cleanly against the blob endpoint. The `FilesCard` wrapper in `app/prospero/[id]/components/FilesCard.tsx` is unchanged on the inline list side (that data comes from the Prospero page's own fetch and still uses the legacy shape for backwards compatibility with components not yet migrated) but its *Browse All Files* modal now spawns the Stage-3 FileBrowser which auto-resolves to mount mode. (`components/files/FileBrowser.tsx`, `components/files/FileThumbnail.tsx`, `components/files/types.ts`, `components/files/mountBlobUrl.ts`, `components/files/useMountPointBlobUpload.ts`, `components/files/FilePreview/hooks/useFilePreview.ts`, `components/files/FilePreview/hooks/useFileActions.ts`, `components/files/FileBrowserGrid.tsx`)
- **Project file storage — new writes now land in the project's database-backed Scriptorium store instead of on disk (Stage 2)**: Stage 1 moved each project's historical bytes into a per-project `storeType='documents'`, `mountType='database'` mount point; Stage 2 stops new writes from hitting `<filesDir>/{projectId}/...` in the first place. The single chokepoint is `fileStorageManager.uploadFile()` in `lib/file-storage/manager.ts` — called by every file-producing path that is project-aware, including the Lantern story-background job (`lib/background-jobs/handlers/story-background.ts`), the character-avatar generation job (`lib/background-jobs/handlers/character-avatar.ts`), the uploaded chat-file pipeline (`app/api/v1/files/shared.ts::saveFileEntry`, `lib/chat-files-v2.ts::uploadChatFile`), the image upload pipeline (`lib/images-v2.ts::uploadImage`), and the character-facing tool handlers that write files on behalf of a character (`lib/tools/handlers/file-management-handler.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/image-generation-handler.ts`, `lib/tools/shell/shell-handler.ts`, `lib/tools/capabilities-report.ts`). When a projectId is present and that project has a linked database-backed document store, the upload is rerouted into `doc_mount_blobs` (with a mirror `doc_mount_files` row so the Scriptorium tree view lists the new file) and the returned `storageKey` carries a `mount-blob:{mountPointId}:{blobId}` scheme marker. The download, delete, exists, and proxy-URL paths all branch on that scheme — `fileStorageManager.downloadFile/deleteFile/fileExists/storageKeyExists/getFileUrl` route mount-blob keys through a new `lib/file-storage/project-store-bridge.ts` module whose public surface (`getProjectDocumentStore`, `writeProjectFileToMountStore`, `readMountBlob`, `mountBlobExists`, `deleteMountBlob`, `parseMountBlobStorageKey`) is what the manager imports. The bridge does everything the HTTP blob endpoint does on its own write path: bitmap images are transcoded to WebP via the existing `transcodeToWebP`, the relative-path extension is rewritten via `normaliseBlobRelativePath`, the parent folder hierarchy is materialized with `ensureFolderPath`, the blob row is created and mirrored to `doc_mount_files` with the corresponding mirror file type (`pdf`/`docx`/`blob`), `emitDocumentWritten` nudges the mount-index subscribers, and `refreshStats` is fire-and-forget after the write so the Scriptorium card counts stay current. Name collisions inside the store are resolved by appending " (2)", " (3)", … to the filename exactly the way the on-disk path used to — up to 999 attempts before falling back to a sha-tagged name. Writes that target `_general/` (no projectId) or explicit storage keys (`uploadRaw`, used for thumbnails) are left on disk unchanged: the redirect fires *only* when a projectId resolves to a database-backed, `storeType='documents'` mount point. Non-database linked stores (filesystem / obsidian) are likewise passed through to disk so users who already manage their own on-disk layout are not disturbed. The existing `/api/v1/files/proxy/[...key]` route continues to serve all files — it looks up the FileEntry by storageKey and re-dispatches through `downloadFile`, which now understands both modes, so thumbnails, downloads, in-chat galleries, and image previews work identically regardless of where the bytes actually live. The `project_info` tool's `get_info` action now also reports the project's linked document store — new `ProjectDocumentStoreInfo` with `mountPointId`, `name`, `storeType`, `fileCount`, and `blobCount` — so characters asking about the current project learn which Scriptorium shelf their files are on. The formatter surfaces it as a `Document Store: <name> (<fileCount> files, <blobCount> blobs, storeType=<type>)` line, or `Document Store: (none linked)` when a project has no store (the Stage 1 migration creates one for every project that had an on-disk directory, but projects created *before* the migration ran and never had files, or projects created in degraded-mount-index-DB sessions, may still be storeless). Legacy `FileEntry` and `Folder` rows in the main DB continue to be written — `repos.files.create` still fires from the three write handlers, now carrying the mount-blob storageKey — so the existing `/api/v1/files?projectId=…` and related API surface keep working without rewrites. Stage 3 will eventually read file metadata through the Scriptorium directly and retire the `files`/`folders` tables. (`lib/file-storage/manager.ts`, `lib/file-storage/project-store-bridge.ts`, `lib/tools/project-info-tool.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/project-info-handler.ts`)
- **Project file storage — every project's on-disk files are now consolidated into a database-backed Scriptorium document store (Stage 1)**: Historically each project scattered its files across `<files>/{projectId}/...` on disk with metadata in the `files` table; the Scriptorium (internally "mount points") has supported storing entire document stores inside the encrypted `quilltap-mount-index.db` for a while, but nothing had ever actually moved project files into it. A new startup migration `convert-project-files-to-document-stores-v1` does that move in one pass: for every project whose `<files>/{projectId}` directory still exists and whose `<files>/{projectId}_doc_store_archive` sibling does not, the migration creates a `mountType='database'`, `storeType='documents'` DocMountPoint named `Project Files: <project name>`, walks the project directory, and imports every file it finds — text formats (`.md`, `.markdown`, `.txt`, `.json`, `.jsonl`, `.ndjson`) land in `doc_mount_documents` with a mirror `doc_mount_files` row; PDFs and DOCX land in `doc_mount_blobs` with extracted text populated via the existing `convertBufferToPlainText` converter; everything else (images, arbitrary binaries) lands in `doc_mount_blobs` as `fileType='blob'` with `extractionStatus='none'`. Folder hierarchy is mirrored into `doc_mount_folders` so the Scriptorium tree view renders the same shape the user had on disk, and the project is linked to the new store via `project_doc_mount_links`. The original directory is renamed to `{projectId}_doc_store_archive` as a safety net — nothing is deleted. Per-project failures (an unreadable file, a rename collision) are caught, the partial mount point rolled back, and the rest of the projects continue to migrate; the migration only returns `success: false` on catastrophic failures like "mount index DB can't open." Chunking and embedding are deliberately deferred — users can hit the scan button on the new store to trigger chunking of text documents and bring the text search index up. The migration is idempotent per-project via a simple filesystem check (archive sibling exists ⇒ skip), so restarting the server is a no-op on projects already migrated. Legacy `FileEntry` and `Folder` rows in the main DB are intentionally left in place in this stage; Stage 2 will rewire the `/api/v1/files/*` and `/api/v1/projects/[id]/files` code paths to read/write through the mount store and clean up the orphaned metadata. Until Stage 2 lands, download URLs served by the legacy file API will 404 because the on-disk directory is archived — users should access project files through the `/scriptorium` route for now. (`migrations/scripts/convert-project-files-to-document-stores.ts`, `migrations/scripts/index.ts`)
- **OpenAI plugin (1.0.34) — `gpt-image-2` added to the image-provider model list**: OpenAI shipped `gpt-image-2` on 2026-04-21 (snapshot `gpt-image-2-2026-04-21`), positioned as the successor to `gpt-image-1` / `gpt-image-1.5` and available via the Images API for organizations with API Organization Verification. Added the new model id to `OpenAIImageProvider.supportedModels` in `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openai/image-provider.ts` and to the `FALLBACK_PROVIDERS` entry in `components/image-profiles/ImageProfileForm.tsx` so it appears in the default-model dropdown on instances that haven't re-fetched the live provider model list. No request-path changes needed — the existing `isGptImageModel` helper matches `startsWith('gpt-image-')`, so gpt-image-2 inherits the gpt-image size allow-list (`1024x1024`, `1024x1536`, `1536x1024`, `auto`) and the "skip `quality` / `style`" branch that gpt-image-1.x already gets. Help text at `help/image-generation-profiles.md` now enumerates the GPT Image lineage alongside the legacy DALL-E models. Quality granularity (`low`/`medium`/`high`/`auto`) and the larger flexible-size envelope (up to 3840px edges, multiples of 16) that gpt-image-2 supports natively are not yet wired up — those require a broader image-profile parameter surface and are deliberately left for a later pass. (`plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openai/image-provider.ts`, `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openai/package.json`, `plugins/dist/qtap-plugin-openai/manifest.json`, `components/image-profiles/ImageProfileForm.tsx`, `help/image-generation-profiles.md`)
- **The Lantern — announce generated images to characters in the chat**: New inheritable setting that, when on, injects a synthetic ASSISTANT-role message into the chat whenever one of the three image pipelines completes (story background via `lib/background-jobs/handlers/story-background.ts`, wardrobe avatar via `lib/background-jobs/handlers/character-avatar.ts`, and the character-invoked `generate_image` tool via `lib/tools/handlers/image-generation-handler.ts`). The announcement names the image's nature (background / avatar of {character} / picture on behalf of {requester}) and attaches the generated file ID, so the thumbnail renders in the Salon bubble (click opens the existing `ImageModal` full-screen viewer) and becomes part of every character's recent-history context on their next turn. The setting lives at two levels with `null`-means-inherit semantics: `defaultAlertCharactersOfLanternImages` on the project (`ProjectSchema`) inherited by chats, overridable per chat via `alertCharactersOfLanternImages` on `ChatMetadataSchema`; the global default is off. Resolution lives in `lib/services/lantern-notifications/resolver.ts::isLanternImageAlertEnabled`, injection in `lib/services/lantern-notifications/writer.ts::postLanternImageNotification` (writes via the existing `repos.chats.addMessage` with `role: 'ASSISTANT'`, `participantId: null`, and `attachments: [fileId]`, then links the file to the message via `repos.files.addLink`). Errors never propagate — a failed announcement logs and returns without breaking the image pipeline. To let vision-capable providers actually *see* the image on the next LLM turn (the existing context-builder only attached files to the last user message), `buildMessageContext` in `lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts` now also pulls image attachments from the last 6 ASSISTANT messages via a new `collectRecentAssistantImageFileIds` helper, loads them with the existing provider-aware `loadChatFilesForLLM`, and merges them into the attachments array so the multimodal content block arrives alongside user uploads. The project toggle lives on `app/prospero/[id]/components/ImageGenerationCard.tsx` (tri-state "Inherit from global / Announce to characters / Keep silent"), wired through a new `handleSaveAlertCharactersOfLanternImages` in `useProjectDetail`. The chat override lives on `components/chat/ChatSettingsModal.tsx` with the matching "Inherit from project" option. API update schemas accept the new field at `app/api/v1/projects/[id]/schemas.ts` and `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/schemas.ts`. New unit tests at `__tests__/unit/lantern-notifications-resolver.test.ts` (chat × project fallback truth table) and `__tests__/unit/lantern-notifications-writer.test.ts` (writer skips when disabled, writes with correct shape, never throws on DB error). (`lib/schemas/project.types.ts`, `lib/schemas/chat.types.ts`, `lib/services/lantern-notifications/resolver.ts`, `lib/services/lantern-notifications/writer.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/story-background.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/character-avatar.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/image-generation-handler.ts`, `lib/services/chat-message/context-builder.service.ts`, `app/prospero/[id]/components/ImageGenerationCard.tsx`, `app/prospero/[id]/hooks/useProjectDetail.ts`, `app/prospero/[id]/types.ts`, `app/prospero/[id]/page.tsx`, `components/chat/ChatSettingsModal.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/components/ChatModals.tsx`, `app/salon/[id]/types.ts`, `app/api/v1/projects/[id]/schemas.ts`, `app/api/v1/chats/[id]/schemas.ts`, `migrations/scripts/add-lantern-image-alert-fields.ts`, `migrations/scripts/index.ts`, `help/lantern.md`)
- **Aurora & Scriptorium — Vault overlay is now symmetric: writes to managed fields land in vault files, not the DB row**: The `readPropertiesFromDocumentStore` overlay covered reads but not writes — every save still went to the `characters` row, the Aurora editor papered over the asymmetry by disabling overlay-managed inputs, and any background path that bypassed that UI guard (the AI character wizard, importers re-importing onto a vault-mode character, the optimizer, future AI tool calls) silently let the vault drift out of sync. New `applyDocumentStoreWriteOverlay()` in `lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts` is the symmetric counterpart to the existing `applyDocumentStoreOverlay()`: when a character is in vault mode and a `repos.characters.update()` patch touches a managed field, the field is routed to the matching vault file (single-file `description.md`/`personality.md`/`example-dialogues.md`/`physical-description.md`, JSON read-modify-write for `properties.json`/`physical-prompts.json`, full-projection-with-stale-cleanup for `Prompts/*.md`/`Scenarios/*.md`, with `physicalDescriptions[0]`'s overlaid sub-fields handled in lockstep) and stripped from the DB-bound patch. Non-managed fields (tags, defaultPartnerId, defaultImageId, controlledBy, etc.) still go to DB on the same call. Vault writes happen *before* the DB write so a vault failure aborts the whole update — no half-committed states where DB and vault disagree on which value is current. The overlay is driven by a new `CHARACTER_VAULT_DESCRIPTORS` table that's the single source of truth for "which character fields live in which vault file"; both the new write overlay and a new consolidated reader (`readCharacterVaultManagedFields`) iterate it instead of carrying their own copies of the mapping. The nine standalone `readCharacterVault*` helpers are now reached only through that consolidated reader — the `sync-properties-from-vault` action in `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts` was rewritten to call it once and pass the resulting `Partial<Character>` to a new `repos.characters.updateRaw()` (a sibling of `findByIdRaw()`) that bypasses the write overlay so the sync-back doesn't loop the values right back into the vault. The Aurora edit form (`app/aurora/[id]/edit/components/CharacterBasicInfo.tsx`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/hooks/useCharacterEdit.ts`) is no longer read-only when the overlay is on — every input stays editable and the repository routes the writes correctly — and the `OVERLAY_MANAGED_FIELDS` strip from the PUT payload is gone. The "Sync from vault" button is renamed to "Snapshot to database" since its meaning has shifted: vault is now the source of truth while the overlay is on, so the button is for taking a snapshot into the DB before flipping the switch off, not for catching the DB up to vault edits. Semantics: writes route to vault, the DB row holds whatever it had at the moment overlay was first turned on, toggling overlay off restores those frozen values (run a snapshot first if you want to keep recent vault edits). The four small file-format helpers in `lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts` (`buildSystemPromptFile`, `buildScenarioFile`, `sanitizeFileName`, `renderPhysicalPromptsJson`) are now exported so the write overlay can reuse them — vault file format stays defined in one place. The existing batched read overlay's per-kind logic is intentionally kept inline and unchanged for performance; the descriptor table mirrors its mapping and the comment block flags that adding a managed field requires updating both. (`lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/characters.repository.ts`, `lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/hooks/useCharacterEdit.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/components/CharacterBasicInfo.tsx`, `help/character-editing.md`)
- **Aurora & Scriptorium — Live overlay now covers the wardrobe**: The per-character `readPropertiesFromDocumentStore` switch now extends to `wardrobe.json`, bringing the total to nine vault targets the overlay knows how to read. When the flag is on and the character has a linked vault, `WardrobeRepository.findByCharacterId` / `findDefaultsForCharacter` and `OutfitPresetsRepository.findByCharacterId` source their results from the vault file instead of the `wardrobe_items` and `outfit_presets` tables — so the Salon sidebar, the wardrobe/preset API routes (`/api/v1/characters/[id]/wardrobe`, `.../presets`), the wardrobe tool handlers (`wardrobe-list-handler`, `wardrobe-update-outfit-handler`), the chat context builder, and the scene-state tracker all read the user's hand-edited file without any caller-side code changes. Fallback is per-file all-or-nothing: a missing, malformed, or schema-invalid `wardrobe.json` logs a warning and returns the DB rows. New `CharacterVaultWardrobeSchema` accepts `{ items, presets, outfit? }` — `outfit` is the per-chat equipped state placeholder that the scaffold writes, accepted on read but not consumed (equipped state still lives on the chat row, not the character vault). Items parsed from the vault have their `characterId` coerced to the lookup ID so a hand-edited `characterId` mismatch can't confuse downstream consumers. The archived-items filter still applies (the `includeArchived=false` default strips items with a non-null `archivedAt`), and `findDefaultsForCharacter` filters `isDefault=true` after the overlay replaces the list. Two new raw variants — `findByCharacterIdRaw` on both repos — bypass the overlay and are used by the vault-provisioning code (`lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts`, to avoid self-reading the file it's about to write) and the export paths (`lib/export/ndjson-writer.ts`, `lib/export/quilltap-export-service.ts`, so `.qtap` archives always reflect canonical DB rows regardless of the character's overlay flag). A new one-time startup task, `refreshVaultWardrobe()`, chained after `migrateVaultPhysicalFiles()` in `instrumentation.ts`, sweeps every character with a linked vault and rewrites its `wardrobe.json` from the current DB state — needed because the file was historically written once at vault creation and never rewritten from the database after that, so existing vaults carry stale snapshots. Gated by the `wardrobe_json_refreshed_v1` flag in `instance_settings`, so it runs exactly once per database and no-ops on every subsequent startup; if any character errors during the sweep the flag stays unset so the next boot retries. Per the existing overlay contract writes still target the DB (matches parity with how `properties.json` / prompts / scenarios behave today), so when the flag is on the vault file is the read source and API mutations will drift from it until the user edits the file themselves. The **Sync from vault** button has been extended to cover the wardrobe too — it now reads `wardrobe.json` and replaces the character's `wardrobe_items` and `outfit_presets` rows wholesale (including archived items, to keep the "vault == DB" reconciliation guarantee), preserving each item/preset's id and timestamps so outfit-preset slot references survive the round-trip. Empty-patch short-circuit still guards against clicking the button when nothing in the vault is valid; the Aurora edit page also now bumps its `PhysicalDescriptionList` and `WardrobeItemList` refresh keys after a sync completes so those child panes re-fetch. All nine overlay targets (`properties.json`, `description.md`, `personality.md`, `example-dialogues.md`, `physical-description.md`, `physical-prompts.json`, `Prompts/*.md`, `Scenarios/*.md`, `wardrobe.json`) are now covered in both directions — overlay on read and sync on write. (`lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/wardrobe.repository.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/outfit-presets.repository.ts`, `lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts`, `lib/export/ndjson-writer.ts`, `lib/export/quilltap-export-service.ts`, `lib/startup/refresh-vault-wardrobe.ts`, `instrumentation.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/page.tsx`)
- **Connection profiles — per-profile image-upload capability flag**: Image attachment support is no longer inferred from the provider name. Connection profiles carry a new `supportsImageUpload` boolean, toggled by a *Supports image attachments (vision input)* checkbox on the profile edit form, and every vision-aware code path — the chat attachment fallback, the wardrobe image analysis, the AI wizard's description source step, the *Image Description Profile* selector in Chat settings, the in-chat fallback resolver — now reads that flag via `profileSupportsMimeType()`. `profileSupportsMimeType()` itself routes image MIME types through the per-profile flag while leaving PDF and text MIME types on the historic per-provider capability map (Anthropic still natively accepts PDFs; OpenAI still doesn't). Existing installs are migrated by `add-profile-supports-image-upload-field-v1`, which seeds `supportsImageUpload = 1` for every profile whose provider was previously hardcoded as vision-capable (`OPENAI`, `ANTHROPIC`, `GOOGLE`, `GROK`) and leaves every other provider at the default `0` — so behavior on day one matches the old hardcoded table, but users can now enable image support on any `OPENROUTER`, `OLLAMA`, or `OPENAI_COMPATIBLE` profile that actually proxies a vision-capable model (gpt-4o through OpenRouter, LLaVA through Ollama, etc.). New profiles default from the same provider map on the server side, so clients that don't send the field keep their current behavior. The `.qtap` import path shims missing `supportsImageUpload` values on older exports using the same provider seed, so round-tripping pre-4.3 archives does not regress. The hardcoded `VISION_PROVIDERS` tuple that previously drove the *Image Description Profile* filter in `components/settings/chat-settings` has been removed. (`lib/schemas/profile.types.ts`, `lib/llm/connection-profile-utils.ts`, `migrations/scripts/add-profile-supports-image-upload-field.ts`, `migrations/scripts/sqlite-initial-schema.ts`, `migrations/scripts/index.ts`, `app/api/v1/connection-profiles/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/connection-profiles/[id]/route.ts`, `components/settings/connection-profiles/ProfileForm.tsx`, `components/settings/connection-profiles/hooks/useProfileForm.ts`, `components/settings/connection-profiles/types.ts`, `components/settings/chat-settings/ImageDescriptionSettings.tsx`, `components/settings/chat-settings/types.ts`, `lib/import/quilltap-import-service.ts`, `__tests__/unit/llm-attachment-support.test.ts`, `__tests__/unit/lib/chat/file-attachment-fallback.test.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — inter-character memory handler routes through the Memory Gate**: The INTER_CHARACTER_MEMORY job handler previously called the cheap-LLM extraction directly and then wrote every candidate to `repos.memories.create` inline, bypassing `runMemoryGate` entirely. That meant none of the 4.3 gate improvements — NEAR_DUPLICATE skip at 0.90, MERGE at 0.85, SKIP_EMBEDDING_FAILED, the retry-once-then-drop embedding policy, reinforcement on match, related-memory linking, or the post-write auto-housekeeping watermark — applied to observer→subject memories in multi-character chats. Those memories landed as duplicates with NULL embeddings in exactly the way the single-character path used to, only still. The handler has been reduced to a 70-line adapter that loads the connection profile, chat settings, danger resolution, and chat context, then hands off to `processInterCharacterMemory` in `lib/memory/memory-processor`. That function already contained the full gate-aware code path for inter-character extraction — introduced alongside the single-character processor but never wired to production — including the rate-limit check from the 4.3 extraction-limits work. Net effect: one code path now covers all three extraction flavors (user memories, character-self memories, inter-character memories), with identical gate behavior. New unit test suite at `__tests__/unit/background-jobs/inter-character-memory-handler.test.ts` covers five cases (delegation, missing profile, missing chat settings, dangerous-chat propagation, graceful failure). Debug-log persistence on the source message is deliberately left out of the inter-character path for now — the single-character handler's pattern overwrites `debugMemoryLogs` on each write, which would race when multiple observers all log against the same source message; the prior handler didn't persist them either, so this is behavior-preserving. (`lib/background-jobs/handlers/inter-character-memory.ts`, `__tests__/unit/background-jobs/inter-character-memory-handler.test.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — per-character cap overrides in the UI**: The Memory Housekeeping card now surfaces the `perCharacterCapOverrides` setting (previously API-only) as a collapsible list under the global-cap input. The list shows every character owned by the user, their current memory count, and an optional cap input; leaving the input blank falls back to the global cap, and characters already over their effective cap flag the count in red so users can spot the busy ones at a glance. A new lightweight endpoint `GET /api/v1/memories?action=character-memory-counts` powers the list — rather than loading the full enriched character payload from `/api/v1/characters` and paying for the per-character chat lookup that enrichment does, this returns only `{id, name, memoryCount}` triples so the Housekeeping card stays fast even on instances with many characters. Saves fire on blur via the existing `?action=housekeeping-config` POST path; the list sorts characters by memory count descending so the ones most likely to need attention appear first. (`components/tools/memory-housekeeping-card.tsx`, `app/api/v1/memories/route.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — *Repair Missing Embeddings* admin card**: A new card in the Commonplace Book tab (second from the top, between *Embedding Profiles* and *Memory Housekeeping*) lists how many memories across every character are still missing an embedding, how many embedding jobs are currently in flight for this user, and offers a button to enqueue up to 500 more at a time. The button is disabled when the remaining count reaches zero; the card polls `GET /api/v1/memories?action=backfill-embeddings` every four seconds to keep its counters fresh without a page reload. The backfill mechanism is motivated by the pre-4.3 gate fallback path (deleted in the 4.3 gate rework) that wrote memory rows without embeddings whenever the embedding provider was briefly unavailable — on the Friday audit instance, 41% of 32,364 memories landed this way and were invisible to every subsequent dedup check. Two new repository methods drive the flow: `countWithoutEmbedding(characterId?)` runs a targeted `COUNT` behind the existing filter abstraction and `findIdsWithoutEmbedding({ characterId?, limit? })` returns `{id, characterId}` pairs for up to `limit` memories with a `null` embedding. The POST handler (`POST /api/v1/memories?action=backfill-embeddings`) resolves the user's default embedding profile (single-profile instances only — consistent with the locked decision for this PR), then fans out `EMBEDDING_GENERATE` jobs via the existing `enqueueEmbeddingGenerate` helper, which dedupes per entity so repeated clicks can't pile up work. Progress-reporting GET uses a lightweight `findByUserId` sweep filtered in memory to count in-flight jobs whose payload `entityType === 'MEMORY'`. Run repeatedly for large backlogs; jobs drain through the usual background-job processor. (`components/tools/memory-backfill-card.tsx`, `components/settings/tabs/MemorySearchTabContent.tsx`, `app/api/v1/memories/route.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/memories.repository.ts`, `help/memory-housekeeping.md`)
- **Commonplace Book — per-hour extraction rate limit with a graduated importance floor**: A companion guard to auto-housekeeping that applies back-pressure at the front of the memory pipeline rather than the back. When enabled, the limiter counts how many memories a character has accrued in the trailing hour and — as volume approaches the cap — tightens what the extraction pass is allowed to commit: below 70% of the cap, candidates flow through unchanged; between 70% and 100%, candidates whose importance falls below the soft floor are dropped; at or above 100%, extraction is skipped entirely for this exchange and logged to the per-message `debugMemoryLogs` so the user can see why their memories stopped appearing. Default values once enabled: 20 memories/hour/character, soft band at 70% of that, importance floor 0.7. A new `countCreatedSince(characterId, since)` method on the memories repository drives the check using the existing `createdAt` index. Settings persist to a new `memoryExtractionLimits` JSON column on `chat_settings` (migration `add-memory-extraction-limits-field-v1`) and are readable/writable via `GET`/`POST /api/v1/memories?action=extraction-limits-config`. The limiter applies to all three extraction paths — user memories, character memories (both in `processMessageForMemory`), and inter-character memories (in the background-jobs `inter-character-memory.ts` handler, which writes directly rather than going through the unused `processInterCharacterMemory` entry point). **Shipped disabled by default** and not yet exposed in the UI; it is the API-only backstop for instances whose gate improvements alone are not enough. Complementary to auto-housekeeping: housekeeping is retrospective and the rate limit is prospective. (`lib/schemas/settings.types.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-processor.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/memory-extraction.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/inter-character-memory.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/memories.repository.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/chat-settings.repository.ts`, `app/api/v1/memories/route.ts`, `migrations/scripts/add-memory-extraction-limits-field.ts`, `migrations/scripts/sqlite-initial-schema.ts`, `help/memory-housekeeping.md`, `docs/developer/DDL.md`, `__tests__/unit/lib/memory/memory-processor-regression.test.ts`)
- **Commonplace Book — automatic housekeeping (off by default)**: The Commonplace Book tab (formerly *Memory & Search*) now carries a Memory Housekeeping card that, once enabled, automatically prunes stale, low-importance memories before any single character's count spirals out of proportion. Two triggers: (1) a reactive post-write watermark that enqueues a sweep whenever a character passes 90% of its configured cap after a new memory lands, and (2) a daily scheduled pass that catches characters whose counts crept up while no one was chatting with them. Both share a new `MEMORY_HOUSEKEEPING` background-job handler, which calls the existing `runHousekeeping` retention-policy engine under per-user settings: global per-character cap (default **2000**, up from the housekeeping module's legacy 1000), per-character overrides, and an optional merge-similar pass at cosine threshold 0.90. The enqueue helper de-dupes against in-flight jobs for the same (userId, characterId) pair, so a storm of writes can't launch a storm of sweeps. The tab itself now reads **Commonplace Book** and surfaces a *Run housekeeping now* button that kicks a one-shot sweep across every character owned by the user. Settings persist to a new `autoHousekeepingSettings` JSON column on `chat_settings` (migration `add-auto-housekeeping-settings-field-v1`). The protection rule for heavily reinforced memories has been tightened: a count of five or more reinforcements used to grant permanent immunity on its own; it now additionally requires either `reinforcedImportance >= 0.5` or access within the last 90 days, which stops noisy phrase-variant duplicates from becoming immortal simply because they got re-extracted many times. Off by default; opt in from the Commonplace Book tab. (`lib/schemas/settings.types.ts`, `lib/memory/housekeeping.ts`, `lib/memory/memory-service.ts`, `lib/schemas/job.types.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/queue-service.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/memory-housekeeping.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/handlers/index.ts`, `lib/background-jobs/scheduled-housekeeping.ts`, `instrumentation.ts`, `app/api/v1/memories/route.ts`, `app/settings/page.tsx`, `components/settings/tabs/MemorySearchTabContent.tsx`, `components/tools/memory-housekeeping-card.tsx`, `migrations/scripts/add-auto-housekeeping-settings-field.ts`, `migrations/scripts/sqlite-initial-schema.ts`, `help/memory-housekeeping.md`, `help/settings.md`, `help/startup-wizard.md`, `docs/developer/DDL.md`)
- **DDL docs — correct `memories.embedding` column type**: The DDL reference at `docs/developer/DDL.md` listed the `memories.embedding` column as `TEXT`, but it was migrated to `BLOB` in 2.11.0 by `normalize-vector-storage-v1` (Float32 bytes, 4 bytes per dimension). The docs now reflect reality; no schema change. (`docs/developer/DDL.md`)
- **Salon — Per-participant system-prompt dropdown on the Participant Card**: Each character card in the Participant Sidebar now carries a second dropdown, tucked just under the connection-profile selector, for picking which of that character's named system prompts the LLM will speak from. The selector lists every entry in the character's `systemPrompts[]` array (with the default one marked) plus a *Use default prompt* option at the top; changes fire an immediate `POST /api/v1/chats/:id?action=update-participant` carrying `selectedSystemPromptId` and re-fetch the chat, so the next generation (nudge, auto-turn, or swipe) uses the new prompt without any page reload or settings-modal detour. The dropdown only renders for LLM-controlled character participants whose character has at least one named prompt — user-controlled participants and prompt-less characters keep the old card layout unchanged. The field was already present on `ChatParticipantBase` and consumed by `buildSystemPrompt()`; this change exposes it to the enrichment layer and wires it to a live control. (`app/api/v1/chats/[id]/schemas.ts`, `lib/services/chat-enrichment.service.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/types.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useParticipants.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/hooks/useChatControls.ts`, `app/salon/[id]/page.tsx`, `components/chat/ParticipantCard.tsx`, `components/chat/ParticipantSidebar.tsx`, `help/chat-participants.md`)
- **Aurora & Scriptorium — Live overlay now covers example dialogues, named prompt variants, and named scenarios**: The per-character `readPropertiesFromDocumentStore` switch has been extended to a third wave of vault targets, bringing the total to eight files the overlay knows how to read. `example-dialogues.md` joins `description.md` and `personality.md` as a single-file overlay driving `character.exampleDialogues`; an empty file maps to `null` (the valid "no examples" state) and a missing file falls back to the DB. Two new directory overlays — `Prompts/*.md` and `Scenarios/*.md` — let each prompt variant and each scenario live as its own Markdown file. Prompt files carry a YAML frontmatter carrying `{name, isDefault}`; the body after the closing `---` becomes the prompt content. Scenario files use their first `# heading` as the title and everything after it as the body (with a filename-based fallback when the heading is missing). Both directory overlays are all-or-nothing per directory: if at least one file parses cleanly the vault listing fully replaces the DB array; if the folder is empty or every file is malformed the DB values are used. Entries synthesize RFC-4122 v8-formatted IDs deterministically from `(mountPointId, relativePath)` via SHA-256, so a chat's stored `selectedSystemPromptId` / `defaultScenarioId` survives across reads as long as filenames don't change. The overlay layer now issues eight backend queries per batch (six single-file reads, two folder enumerations) and still applies at the `CharactersRepository` read layer, so `buildSystemPrompt()` and every other consumer picks up vault-sourced prompts, scenarios, and example dialogues without code changes. The Aurora edit form disables the Example Dialogues textarea and the scenarios editor (title inputs, body text boxes, add/remove buttons) when the switch is on, and the overlay banner now lists every file and folder the switch covers. The `sync-properties-from-vault` action copies every available overlay value back to the DB — including the new example-dialogues string and the full vault-sourced `systemPrompts` / `scenarios` arrays when their folders are non-empty — regenerating stable IDs rather than keeping the DB's originals. (`lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/doc-mount-documents.repository.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/hooks/useCharacterEdit.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/components/CharacterBasicInfo.tsx`, `help/character-editing.md`)
- **Aurora & Scriptorium — Live overlay now covers description, personality, and the primary physical description**: The per-character `readPropertiesFromDocumentStore` switch, which previously overlaid only the five fields in `properties.json`, has been extended to cover four more vault files, each governing its own slice of the character. `description.md` and `personality.md` drive the character's Description and Personality fields; `physical-description.md` and a new `physical-prompts.json` drive the **first** (default) entry of `physicalDescriptions[]` — its `fullDescription` for the former, and the `{short, medium, long, complete}` prompt quartet for the latter. Fallback is now per-file (all-or-nothing within a file, but other files are unaffected): a malformed `physical-prompts.json` leaves the DB prompts in place while `description.md` still wins if it parses cleanly. The overlay still applies transparently at the repository read layer, so system-prompt builders, image-generation prompt expansion, scene-state tracking, and every other consumer that goes through `repos.characters.findById()` sees the overlaid values without code changes. The Aurora edit form now disables the Description and Personality inputs when the switch is on; the Descriptions tab grows a banner noting that the first physical description's full description and prompts are being read from the vault. The `sync-properties-from-vault` action copies every available overlay value back to the DB (properties.json, description.md, personality.md, physical-description.md, and physical-prompts.json), patching `physicalDescriptions[0]` rather than replacing the array. `populateVaultWithCharacterData()` has been updated so new vaults write the single primary `fullDescription` to `physical-description.md` (not the old aggregate markdown) and emit a JSON `physical-prompts.json` alongside. A new startup step — `migrateVaultPhysicalFiles()` — runs after the existing vault backfill to convert existing vaults to the new shape: it creates `physical-prompts.json` when absent and regenerates `physical-description.md` from the DB primary description, using the presence of `physical-prompts.json` as its idempotency marker. The migration also sweeps away a legacy `physical-prompts.md` file that a brief window of development builds seeded before the extension was corrected to `.json`, so vaults caught by the earlier pass end up with only the right file. The character-store scaffold gains `physical-prompts.json` as an eighth seeded file so fresh vaults match the populated shape. (`lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts`, `lib/mount-index/character-scaffold.ts`, `lib/startup/migrate-vault-physical-files.ts`, `instrumentation.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/**`, `app/aurora/[id]/view/components/DescriptionsTab.tsx`, `help/character-editing.md`)
- **Aurora & Scriptorium — Live overlay of character properties from the vault**: A new per-character switch, `readPropertiesFromDocumentStore`, can be flipped in the Aurora edit page to have `pronouns`, `aliases`, `title`, `firstMessage`, and `talkativeness` read live from the character's linked Scriptorium vault (`properties.json`) instead of the DB row. The overlay is applied transparently at the `CharactersRepository` read layer (`findById`, `findAll`, `findByUserId`, `findByIds`, `findUserControlled`, `findLLMControlled`, `findByDefaultImageId`, `findByAvatarOverrideImageId`, `findByTag`) so every consumer — system-prompt builder, turn manager, homepage roster, chat — sees the overlaid values without code changes. Writes still target the DB: when the switch is on, the Aurora edit form disables the five overlay-managed inputs and strips them from the PUT payload so a stray save cannot silently persist the vault-derived values back into the database. A manual **Sync from vault** button (`POST /api/v1/characters/:id?action=sync-properties-from-vault`) copies `properties.json` values into the DB record when the user wants to reconcile. Fallback is all-or-nothing: if `properties.json` is missing, malformed, or fails schema validation, a warning logs and the DB values are returned for all five fields. Batched: one `doc_mount_documents` query hydrates an arbitrary number of characters. The SillyTavern `.json`/`.png` export still uses overlaid values (what the user sees) while `.qtap` export uses raw DB values (via `findByIdRaw` / `findAllRaw`) so round-trips are lossless. Schema column `readPropertiesFromDocumentStore INTEGER` added via migration `add-read-properties-from-document-store-field-v1`. (`lib/schemas/character.types.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/character-properties-overlay.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/characters.repository.ts`, `lib/database/repositories/doc-mount-documents.repository.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts`, `app/aurora/[id]/edit/**`, `migrations/scripts/add-read-properties-from-document-store-field.ts`, `migrations/scripts/sqlite-initial-schema.ts`, `lib/export/ndjson-writer.ts`, `lib/export/quilltap-export-service.ts`, `lib/startup/backfill-character-vaults.ts`, `docs/developer/DDL.md`, `help/aurora.md`)
- **Aurora & Scriptorium — Characters always carry their own vault into the room**: When an LLM takes the stage as a character and reaches for the `doc_*` tools, that character's own document vault is now extended to it as a matter of course — even when the vault has not been independently linked to the active project. The path resolver now considers two sources when deciding which mount points the tools may see: the stores linked to the active project (as before) and the single store named by `characters.characterDocumentMountPointId` (new). The two sets are merged and deduplicated, so linking a vault to a project on top of the character link does not multiply it. `DocEditToolContext` and `PathResolutionContext` each grew an optional `characterId`, threaded in from the chat `ToolExecutionContext`; `getAccessibleMountPoints()` and `resolveDocumentStorePath()` consult it. To plug the matching gap on the other end, character creation no longer leaves new characters without a vault until the next server boot: the provisioning logic previously inlined in `backfill-character-vaults.ts` has been extracted into a reusable `ensureCharacterVault()` helper at `lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts`, and the three character-create paths (`POST /api/v1/characters`, `?action=quick-create`, `?action=import`) now call it fire-and-forget immediately after `repos.characters.create()`. The helper remains idempotent — if a character already carries `characterDocumentMountPointId`, it is a no-op — so the startup backfill continues to catch anything a failed background provisioning dropped on the floor. (`lib/doc-edit/path-resolver.ts`, `lib/tools/handlers/doc-edit-handler.ts`, `lib/chat/tool-executor.ts`, `lib/mount-index/character-vault.ts`, `lib/startup/backfill-character-vaults.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/route.ts`)
- **Scriptorium — Startup backfill of character vaults**: On every server boot, Quilltap now sweeps through every Aurora character that isn't already linked to a character document store and conjures one in the Scriptorium on its behalf. The new vault is a database-backed store with `storeType='character'`, named after the character (e.g. a character called *Friday* acquires *Friday Character Vault*), scaffolded through the existing `scaffoldCharacterMount()` helper, and then populated from the character's current data: `identity.md` gets a name-and-pronouns-and-title-and-aliases header, `description.md` / `personality.md` / `example-dialogues.md` receive the corresponding character fields verbatim, `physical-description.md` renders each entry from `physicalDescriptions[]` as a Markdown section with all its prompt fields, `properties.json` serializes `pronouns`, `aliases`, `title`, `firstMessage`, and `talkativeness`, and `wardrobe.json` captures the character's `WardrobeItem[]` / `OutfitPreset[]` from the DB plus any legacy `clothingRecords[]` migrated in as synthetic items (with `migratedFromClothingRecordId` set so the provenance is preserved). Named `systemPrompts[]` and `scenarios[]` each get their own file in `Prompts/` and `Scenarios/` respectively. The backfill runs as new Phase 3.2 in `instrumentation.ts` — after file-storage init and before the mount-point scan, so freshly created vaults land in the first scan pass. It is idempotent (characters with `characterDocumentMountPointId` already set are skipped) and fault-tolerant (a failure for one character logs and continues to the next). The scaffold itself has been extended so new empty vaults match the populated shape: `example-dialogues.md` is now part of the preset structure, and `properties.json` gains `firstMessage: ''` and `talkativeness: 0.5` (with `pronouns` flipped from empty-string to `null` to keep the schema object-shaped). (`lib/startup/backfill-character-vaults.ts`, `lib/mount-index/character-scaffold.ts`, `instrumentation.ts`, `help/mount-points.md`)
- **Aurora — Link a character to its character document store**: Characters now carry an optional `characterDocumentMountPointId` field that names a single Scriptorium document store (by convention, one classified as *Character* and backed by the database). This lays the first stone for the larger migration in which everything about a character except memories — identity, description, personality, scenarios, prompts, wardrobe, lore, images — eventually lives inside a dedicated store rather than in character columns. The field is a soft foreign key (nullable, no FK constraint, since the mount point lives in a separate database) wired through the character Zod schema, the characters table (via migration `add-character-document-mount-point-field-v1`), the create/update API validation, and `.qtap` export/import. On import, if the referenced mount point isn't part of the same archive, the link is cleared rather than left dangling; if it is, it's remapped to the newly-created mount point's id. No UI surface yet — a dropdown in the character edit dialog will follow once the broader character-in-store plan firms up. (`lib/schemas/character.types.ts`, `migrations/scripts/add-character-document-mount-point-field.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/characters/[id]/route.ts`, `lib/import/quilltap-import-service.ts`, `docs/developer/DDL.md`)
- **Scriptorium — Character document stores arrive pre-scaffolded**: When a database-backed document store is created with `storeType='character'`, or when an existing database-backed store is flipped to Character via the Edit dialog, Quilltap now lays in the conventional preset structure automatically: four blank Markdown files (`identity.md`, `description.md`, `personality.md`, `physical-description.md`), two seeded JSON files (`properties.json` with `{pronouns, aliases, title}` mirroring the Character schema shape, and `wardrobe.json` with empty `items[]` / `presets[]` and a slot-null `outfit` mirroring `lib/schemas/wardrobe.types.ts`), and five empty folders (`Prompts`, `Scenarios`, `lore`, `images`, `files`). Filesystem and Obsidian character stores are left untouched — the user is presumed to be pointing at an existing vault of their own. The scaffold is idempotent: pre-existing files are never overwritten, so flipping a populated store to Character simply fills in whatever gaps remain. Implementation lives in a new `lib/mount-index/character-scaffold.ts` helper and is called from both `POST /api/v1/mount-points` and the `PATCH` endpoint's storeType-flip branch. (`lib/mount-index/character-scaffold.ts`, `app/api/v1/mount-points/route.ts`, `app/api/v1/mount-points/[id]/route.ts`, `help/mount-points.md`)
- **Scriptorium — `storeType` classification on document stores**: Every document store now carries a `storeType` field in addition to its `mountType`. The two allowed values are `'documents'` (the default — general notes, references, research) and `'character'` (character sheets and related Aurora material). The Create and Edit dialogs expose a *Contents* dropdown so the classification can be set at creation and changed at any time afterwards. The card on the Scriptorium index shows a new *Documents* / *Character* badge. The field is wired through the API (`POST`/`PATCH /api/v1/mount-points[/:id]`), `.qtap` export/import (backward-compatible; older archives default to `'documents'`), the public export JSON schema, and `DDL.md`. The `doc_mount_points` table gains the new column via in-repo idempotent `ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN` on first access for existing installations.
- **Scriptorium — Arbitrary binary uploads in database-backed stores with extracted-text embeddings**: Any file type can now be uploaded to a database-backed document store. PDF and DOCX uploads get their plain text extracted into a new `extractedText` column on `doc_mount_blobs`; that text is chunked, embedded, and made searchable alongside native `.md` / `.txt` / `.json` documents. Arbitrary binaries (zip, audio, video, `.bin`, etc.) are stored as-is and surface in the tree with `fileType='blob'` — future converters can fill in extracted text for additional formats without schema changes. Bitmap uploads (PNG/JPEG/GIF/TIFF/HEIC/HEIF/AVIF) still transcode to WebP; already-WebP uploads are now stored as-is without re-encoding. The Scriptorium detail page's separate BlobManager pane has been folded into the main file table — every file, text or binary, lives in one unified tree with an Upload button on database-backed stores. `doc_read_file` on a blob with extracted text returns the derived plain text with `derivedFromBlob: true` so LLMs can read PDFs and DOCX uploads through the same tool they use for Markdown. Folder moves now also rename contained blobs, closing the last gap from the earlier blob-path TODO. `.qtap` export and import round-trip the new blob columns (`extractedText`, `extractedTextSha256`, `extractionStatus`, `extractionError`, `descriptionUpdatedAt`); the public export schema has been updated to match. Older `.qtap` archives that predate these fields import without regressions and leave new blobs in the default `extractionStatus='none'` state.
- **Scriptorium — Test coverage for folder and JSON/JSONL document stores (Phase 4.0 Deliverable 3 — Phase D)**: Added 103 Jest unit tests across folder path utilities, database-store folder operations (create/delete/move/backfill), doc-edit handler folder-tool registration, the MIME registry (JSON/JSONL parse/serialize/validate), and the doc-edit handler's JSON response shape. Suite now at 5200 tests across 269 suites.
- **Scriptorium — JSON and JSONL as first-class document types (Phase 4.0 Deliverable 3 — Phase C)**: `doc_read_file` on `.json` files returns native JS objects/arrays in `content` with `parsed: true` and the original string in `rawContent`. `doc_write_file` accepts either a string (validated) or a native value (serialized canonically). `.jsonl` and `.ndjson` are supported: reads return per-line parse results so one malformed line does not poison the whole file. Invalid JSON on write is rejected with a clear error. `doc_str_replace` continues to operate on the raw string. Database-backed document stores now accept `.json` and `.jsonl` files alongside `.md` and `.txt`.
- **Scriptorium — Folder-aware operations on database-backed document stores (Phase 4.0 Deliverable 3 — Phase B)**: `doc_create_folder`, `doc_delete_folder`, `doc_list_files`, and new `doc_move_folder` tool now operate on first-class folder rows for database-backed stores. Filesystem stores gain folder entries in `doc_list_files` output. Move cascades path and `folderId` updates to all descendants and emits embedding events post-commit. Existing DB-backed stores are backfilled once on first access (`PRAGMA user_version = 1`). Export/import now round-trips folder rows in `.qtap` files.
- **Scriptorium — Explicit folder entity schema for database-backed document stores (Phase 4.0 Deliverable 3 — Phase A)**: Added `DocMountFolder` schema, `doc_mount_folders` repository and table, and `folderId` columns to `doc_mount_files` and `doc_mount_documents`. New `folder-paths.ts` utilities provide path resolution, folder hierarchy creation, and content checking. Filesystem-backed stores continue to derive folder structure from the OS. Schema and utilities are foundation for Phase B folder-aware operations.
- **Scriptorium — Convert and Deconvert document stores between backends**
  - Each document-store card on the Scriptorium page now sports a **Convert** button (on filesystem and Obsidian stores) and a **Deconvert** button (on database-backed stores) alongside the familiar Scan/Edit/Delete controls.
  - **Convert** reads every indexed file from the store's `basePath` and moves its bytes inside the encrypted mount-index database: text files land in `doc_mount_documents`, binaries in `doc_mount_blobs`. The original files on disk are left untouched. The store's `mountType` flips to `'database'` and the filesystem watcher detaches.
  - **Deconvert** prompts for a target directory (which must be empty or nonexistent), writes every document and blob out to disk at its relative path, flips `mountType` back to `'filesystem'`, and attaches a fresh filesystem watcher against the new `basePath`.
  - **Embeddings are preserved** across either direction. The `doc_mount_files` row and its `doc_mount_chunks` children (including the `embedding` BLOB) stay in place throughout; only the `source` column flips. No re-embedding is necessary.
  - New `POST /api/v1/mount-points/:id?action=convert` and `?action=deconvert` endpoints for programmatic access; the deconvert body accepts `{ targetPath }` and validates emptiness server-side.
  - New `conversionStatus` / `conversionError` columns on `doc_mount_points` drive the in-flight "Converting…" / "Deconverting…" badges on each card; an in-repo ALTER-TABLE migration adds them automatically on first access after upgrade.
- **Scriptorium — Database-backed document stores and universal blob layer**
  - New `mountType: 'database'` option for Scriptorium document stores. Documents and binary assets live entirely inside the SQLCipher-encrypted `quilltap-mount-index.db` — no filesystem path required. DB-backed stores are automatically covered by the existing 24-hour physical-backup sweep.
  - New universal blob table (`doc_mount_blobs`) available to every mount type. Uploaded images are transcoded to WebP server-side via `sharp`; original filename, original MIME type, user-supplied description, and SHA256 are preserved as metadata.
  - New blob REST endpoints: `GET`/`POST /api/v1/mount-points/:id/blobs` (list / upload multipart) and `GET`/`PATCH`/`DELETE /api/v1/mount-points/:id/blobs/<path>` (stream / update description / delete).
  - Four new `doc_*` tools — `doc_write_blob`, `doc_read_blob`, `doc_list_blobs`, `doc_delete_blob` — let characters upload, reference, and curate images alongside the existing document editing tools.
  - Scriptorium UI gains a third "Database-backed" mount type option and a BlobManager on every store detail page (thumbnail grid, description editing, "Copy Markdown" helper).
  - `MessageContent` renderer accepts a `blobMountPointId` prop; when set, relative Markdown image references like `![alt](images/avatar.webp)` resolve through the blob API so DB-backed assets display inline.
  - `.qtap` export/import gains a new `document-stores` entity type that round-trips mount point configuration plus — for DB-backed mounts — document bodies and base64-encoded blobs.
- **Scriptorium (Phase 1)**: Deterministic Markdown rendering of conversations with annotation support and semantic search chunking
  - Conversations are automatically rendered to Markdown after each turn with sequential message numbering and interchange grouping
  - New `read_conversation` tool allows characters to read the full rendered conversation with or without annotations
  - New `upsert_annotation` and `delete_annotation` tools enable characters to add persistent commentary to specific messages
  - Conversation interchanges are embedded as searchable chunks via the existing embedding pipeline
- **Scriptorium (Phase 2)**: Unified search and cross-conversation access
  - Rendered conversations now include a metadata header with title, ID, dates, participants, and counts
  - New unified `search` tool replaces `search_memories`, searching across both character memories and conversation chunks with unified ranking
  - `read_conversation` tool now accepts an optional `conversationId` parameter to read any conversation, not just the current one
  - Metadata header is embedded with chunk 0 for semantic searchability of conversation titles
  - Removed standalone `search_memories` tool (functionality consolidated into `search`)
- **Scriptorium (Phase 3.1)**: Lexical rich text editor integration for chat composer
  - Replaced plain textarea in ChatComposer with Meta's Lexical rich text framework
  - Rich text formatting (bold, italic, headings, lists) via document mode toolbar now uses native Lexical commands
  - Custom markdown transformer set preserves roleplay delimiters (e.g. `*narration*`) as literal text — italic uses underscore only
  - Undo/redo support via Lexical's built-in HistoryPlugin
  - Messages continue to be stored and transmitted as plain markdown strings — no schema changes
  - Foundation for Phase 3 collaborative document editing features
- **Scriptorium (Phase 3.1 cont.)**: Formatting toolbar enhancements
  - CODE button toggles code blocks (no selection) or inline code (with selection); shows as /CODE when cursor is inside a code block
  - Blockquote button with smart-quote label converts blocks to blockquotes
  - H4, H5, H6 heading buttons added
  - Delimiter buttons (Nar, OOC, etc.) now toggle: wrap selected text, or unwrap if already delimited
  - Enter on a blank trailing line inside a code block exits the block and creates a new paragraph
  - All toolbar buttons now preserve editor selection via `onMouseDown` preventDefault
  - Button styling: headings use serif font, CODE uses monospace, blockquote uses bold serif smart-quote
  - Tooltips updated (Bold, Italic, Unordered List, Ordered List, Blockquote, Heading N)
  - UL/OL button labels changed to `• …` and `1. …` for clarity
  - New themeable CSS custom properties: `--qt-formatting-heading-font`, `--qt-formatting-code-font`
- **Scriptorium (Phase 3.1 cont.)**: Source mode editor and toolbar source-mode support
  - Replaced "Preview message" toggle with "Source mode" toggle — shows raw markdown in a monospace textarea for direct editing
  - When toggling back to rich text mode, source edits are synced into the Lexical editor
  - All formatting toolbar buttons (bold, italic, headings, lists, blockquote, code, delimiters) work in source mode with textarea manipulation
  - Source mode uses `qt-source-mode-textarea` CSS class with monospace font
- **Scriptorium (Phase 3.2)**: Document mount points and auto-embedding
  - Mount external document directories (filesystem paths, Obsidian vaults) as searchable knowledge sources
  - New `quilltap-mount-index.db` database (third database, separate from main and LLM logs) with SQLCipher encryption, WAL mode, and graceful degradation
  - Four new tables: `doc_mount_points`, `doc_mount_files`, `doc_mount_chunks`, `project_doc_mount_links` (many-to-many)
  - Format conversion pipeline: PDF (pdf-parse v2), Word (.docx via mammoth.js), Markdown (regex syntax stripping), plain text
  - Intelligent chunking engine: 800-1200 token chunks with 200-token overlap, heading context tracking
  - SHA-256 checksum-based change detection on startup — new/modified files automatically re-ingested, deleted files purged
  - Auto-embedding via existing embedding infrastructure with new `MOUNT_CHUNK` entity type
  - New `'documents'` source type in the unified search tool — document chunks appear alongside memories and conversations
  - Fire-and-forget startup scanning (Phase 3.3) — large vaults don't block server startup
  - REST API: `/api/v1/mount-points` CRUD, `?action=scan` manual re-scan trigger, `/api/v1/projects/[id]/mount-points` link/unlink
  - New npm dependency: `mammoth` for DOCX text extraction
- **Scriptorium (Phase 3.3)**: Quilltap-native document editing tools
  - 10 new LLM tools for reading, editing, and searching files in document stores and project files
  - **Tier 1 — Text primitives**: `doc_read_file`, `doc_write_file`, `doc_str_replace`, `doc_insert_text`, `doc_grep`, `doc_list_files`
  - **Tier 2 — Markdown-aware**: `doc_read_frontmatter`, `doc_update_frontmatter`, `doc_read_heading`, `doc_update_heading`
  - Unified path resolution across three scopes: document stores, project files, and general files
  - `str_replace` with unique-match constraint — text itself serves as the "address", no structural IDs needed
  - Unicode diacritics normalization for search and replace (e.g., "Nimue" matches "Nimuë")
  - Lightweight markdown parser for heading trees and YAML frontmatter (using `yaml` npm package)
  - Path traversal prevention and mount point access control
  - Optimistic concurrency via mtime-based conflict detection
  - Fire-and-forget single-file re-indexing after edits to keep search results current
  - Tools automatically enabled when a project has linked document stores
  - New npm dependency: `yaml` for frontmatter parsing/serialization
- **Scriptorium (Phase 3.4)**: File management tools for document editing
  - `doc_move_file` — Move or rename files within document stores, project files, or general files
  - `doc_delete_file` — Permanently delete files
  - `doc_create_folder` — Create folders (with parent directory creation, idempotent)
  - `doc_delete_folder` — Delete empty folders (non-empty folders are rejected for safety)
  - All four tools support all three scopes (document_store, project, general)
  - Completes the 14-tool `doc_*` family, closing MCP feature gaps for file management
- **Document Mode (Scriptorium Phase 3.5)**: Split-panel editor for collaborative document editing alongside chat
  - Three layout states: Normal (chat only), Split (chat + document), Focus (document only)
  - Resizable divider between chat and document panes with minimum width enforcement
  - Document picker modal with source selection (new blank, project library, mounted stores)
  - Document picker shows "Recent" section with previously opened documents for quick reopen
  - Document store file browsing uses the mount point's indexed files (not the project file browser)
  - Lexical-based document editor with formatting toolbar, word count, and save status
  - `doc_open_document` and `doc_close_document` tools for LLM participants
  - Keyboard shortcuts: Cmd+Shift+D (toggle document mode), Cmd+Shift+F (toggle focus), Escape (exit focus)
  - Debounced autosave (30s idle) with immediate flush on editor blur
  - Sends unified diff to LLM on autosave so it can see what the user changed
  - Sends LLM notification message with file path and tool instructions when a document opens
  - Document editor updates live when LLM edits the file via doc_* tools
  - Document state persists per chat and restores on page reload or revisit
  - Closed documents are preserved as inactive records for quick-reopen history
  - Editing document store files triggers re-indexing, embedding, and stats refresh
  - Responsive: Document Mode button hidden below 1026px viewport width
- **Document Mode Quality of Life (Scriptorium Phase 3.6)**: Three improvements to the document editing experience
  - **Scroll position persistence**: Document pane remembers scroll position across re-renders, tool calls, layout transitions, and document reopen within the same session
  - **Left-hand gutter**: Narrow gutter beside document content showing change markers (blue bars on modified lines since last save) and an attention marker (eye icon at the last `doc_focus` target)
  - **`doc_focus` tool**: LLM participants can scroll the user's viewport to a heading, text passage, or line number — with ephemeral highlight animation and persistent gutter eye icon. Supports `anchor` (heading), `highlight` (text search), `line` (line number), and `clear_focus` parameters
- **Document Stores UI**: Full management interface for document mount points
  - New "Document Stores" button in left sidebar navigation (database icon, below Files)
  - List page at `/document-stores` with card grid showing name, path, type, file/chunk counts, scan status, and last scan time
  - Create dialog with name, path, mount type (filesystem/Obsidian), include/exclude pattern configuration
  - Edit dialog with all fields plus enable/disable toggle
  - Delete confirmation dialog with clear warning about data removal
  - Scan button on each card triggers filesystem scan and embedding job queuing with progress feedback
  - Detail page at `/document-stores/[id]` with summary stats, pattern display, and full file table
  - File table with sortable columns (name, type, size, conversion status, embedding chunks, last modified), filter search, and summary bar
  - Updated help file to reference new UI instead of API-only management
- **Project Document Stores**: Link/unlink document stores on the project detail page
  - New "Document Stores" expandable card on the Prospero project page
  - Shows linked stores with name, type, file count, and total size
  - Inline picker to link available document stores to the project
  - Unlink button on each linked store
- **Document editing tools in tool settings**: All 10 doc_* tools appear in the tool settings UI (per-chat and per-project defaults) with availability status based on whether the project has linked document stores
- **Tool settings grouping**: Built-in tools are now organized into collapsible groups by category — "Document Editing", "Wardrobe", "Workspace" (VM/Docker shell tools), and "Quilltap Help" — each toggleable as a unit
